Dispute on Bequest to a Named Person and Masakin
Intra-Hanafi dispute on distribution of a bequest involving a named person and the masakin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on dividing a bequest between a named person and the masakin, explain the usul basis for each, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The plural with definite article (al-masakin) is a genus for Shaykhayn, so one recipient suffices; for Muhammad, it retains the plural minimum of two.

This lesson extends the earlier intra-Hanafi dispute over the interpretation of plural nouns with the definite article. Here, the bequest is to a named person and to the masakin, and separately to masakin alone. Two great Hanafi masters, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (Shaykhayn) hold one view, while Imam Muhammad holds another. Understanding this difference sharpens your ability to apply usul principles in estate distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage contains two distinct cases: a combined bequest to a named person and masakin, and a sole bequest to masakin. Recognize the structure.
2
State the Shaykhayn's position and dalil
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the definite article on 'al-masakin' makes it a genus (jins), so the minimum is one. In the combined bequest, half goes to the named person and half to the masakin. In the sole bequest, one miskin suffices.
3
State Muhammad's position and dalil
Imam Muhammad holds that the plural 'masakin' indicates at least two individuals, so the named person gets one-third and the masakin two-thirds, and for the sole bequest, at least two miskin must receive.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: the distribution of shares differs. Note that this is a valid ikhtilaf within the school.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The text consistently presents the Shaykhayn view as the relied position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولو أوصى بثلثه لفلان وللمساكين فنصفه لفلان ونصفه للمساكين عندهما وعند محمد ثلثه لفلان وثلثاه للمساكين ولو اوصى للمساكين له صرفه الى مسكين واحد عندهما وعنده لا يصرف إلا الى مسكينين بناء
He said: And if he bequeaths one-third to so-and-so and to the masakin, then half is for so-and-so and half for the masakin according to them (Shaykhayn), and according to Muhammad: one-third for so-and-so and two-thirds for the masakin. And if he bequeaths to the masakin, he may give it to one miskin according to them, and according to him (Muhammad) he may not give except to two miskin, based on the earlier.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This is a continuation of the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of plural nouns with the definite article. Here, the bequest is to a named individual (fulan) and to the masakin as a category. According to Shaykhayn, since masakin is a genus, the minimum is one, so the one-third is divided equally: half to the named person and half to the masakin. Imam Muhammad, holding that the minimum of plural is two, gives the named person one-third and the masakin two-thirds (since the named person is one, the masakin as a category receives double by his reasoning). The second part of the ruling addresses a bequest solely to masakin: Shaykhayn allow giving it to one miskin, while Muhammad insists on at least two miskin, based on the same principle. This lesson demonstrates the practical application of the usul al-fiqh principle in estate distribution.

Key Terms
مسكين (miskin): A poor person; in this context, a category of recipients for a bequest.
بناء (bina'an): Based on the earlier ruling; referring to the same principle already established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Half to sister, half to masakin (one miskin suffices)
B) One-third to sister, two-thirds to masakin (two miskin required)
C) One-third to sister, two-thirds to masakin (one miskin suffices)
D) All to the sister

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school’s view on bequests involving al-masakin hinges on whether the definite article turns the plural into a genus (Shaykhayn) or retains the plural minimum (Muhammad), with the former being the relied position.

Division of a Bequest Among Three Groups: The Dispute on the Minimum Plural
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing one-third among three beneficiary groups

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad on dividing a bequest among ummahat al-awlad, fuqara, and masakin, and apply the principle of jama' muhalla bi-l-alif wa-l-lam to justify the Hanafi mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When a plural noun has the definite article, it indicates the genus; distribution requires only one from each category.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hadaya, the commentator explains a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on how to divide a bequest of one-third when the testator names three groups: ummahat al-awlad, fuqara, and masakin. The disagreement hinges on the linguistic interpretation of the plural noun with the definite article. Should we apply the inheritance rule that a plural requires at least two, or does the definite article shift the meaning to genus, allowing just one? Let's trace the reasoning of both sides.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to three categories: ummahat al-awlad (mothers of his slave children), fuqara, and masakin. The question is how many individuals from each category must receive a share to fulfill the bequest.
2
Understand Imam Muhammad's Position
Imam Muhammad argues that the words 'fuqara' and 'masakin' are plural, and in inheritance (mirath), the minimum plural is two as proven by the Quran. Therefore, he analogizes and gives each category at least two shares, plus three for ummahat al-awlad, totaling seven shares.
Muhammad's position relies on an analogy (qiyas) with inheritance rules.
3
Understand the Shaykhayn's Position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (Shaykhayn) counter that the plural noun with the definite article (al-jama' al-muhalla bi-l-alif wa-l-lam) indicates the genus (jins). It includes the minimum individual (al-adna) and potentially all, but when giving to all is impractical, the minimum suffices. Thus, one from each category is enough, giving three for ummahat al-awlad and one each for fuqara and masakin, total five shares.
The definite article transforms the meaning from a counted plural to a generic category.
4
Analyze the Linguistic Principle
The core of the dispute is whether the plural with definite article is treated like an absolute plural (which has a known minimum of two) or as a genus (which has no fixed number, only the concept). Hanafi usul rules that alif-lam on a plural indicates the genus, so only one individual is needed to represent the category.
This principle is distinct from inheritance where the plural is used without the definite article in a specific context.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of the Shaykhayn. It is more widely adopted because it aligns with the usul principle and the testator's likely intention to benefit each category as a whole, given the limited one-third.
Later Hanafi works generally favor this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لمحمد ان المذكور لفظ الجمع وادناه في الميراث اثنان نجد ذالک فی القرآن فكان من كل فريق اثنان وامهات الاولاد ثلث فلهذا يقسم على سبعة ولهما ان الجمع المحلى بالالف واللام يراد به الجنس وانه يتناول الادنى مع احتمال الكل لاسيما عند تعذر صرفه الى الكل فيعتبر من كل فريق واحد فبلغ الحساب خمسة والثلثة للثلث
According to Muhammad: The mentioned word is plural, and its minimum in inheritance is two, as we find in the Quran. So from each group [there are] two, and the mothers of children are three. Therefore it is divided into seven. According to them (Shaykhayn): The plural with alif and lam refers to the genus, and it includes the minimum while also implying all, especially when it is difficult to refer to all. So one is considered from each group, and the calculation reaches five; three are for the third (the mothers of children).
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) regarding the division of a bequest of one-third to three categories: ummahat al-awlad (mothers of children), fuqara, and masakin. Imam Muhammad argues that the words 'masakin' and 'fuqara' are plural and, by analogy with inheritance (where the minimum plural is two), each group should receive at least two shares. Combined with the three for ummahat al-awlad, the total shares are seven. The Shaykhayn counter that when a plural noun is prefixed with the definite article 'alif-lam', it indicates the genus (jins), which encompasses the minimum individual (al-adna) while also potentially including all. Since it is impractical to distribute to all individuals of each genus (due to the limited one-third), they adopt the minimum: one share per category, resulting in five shares total (three for ummahat al-awlad, one each for fuqara and masakin). This difference has practical consequences for the distribution of wasiyya.

Key Terms
جمع محلى بالالف واللام (jama' muhallan bi-l-alif wa-l-lam): A plural noun with the definite article alif-lam (e.g., المساكين). In Hanafi usul, this indicates the genus (jins) and denotes the minimum individual of that genus when distribution to all is impracticable.
أمهات الأولاد (ummahat al-awlad): Mothers of children (i.e., slave women who have borne a child to their master). In this context, they are a category of beneficiaries in a bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Bequest to a Named Person and to Masakin: Shaykhayn vs. Muhammad
Ruling on dividing a bequest between a named person and masakin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad on dividing a bequest to a named person and 'al-masakin', and apply the Hanafi rule that the plural with alif-lam indicates the genus.

Core Idea
The plural with alif-lam signifies the genus, allowing one miskin to suffice and equally splitting the bequest.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute over how to distribute a bequest of one-third to both a named individual and 'al-masakin'. The disagreement hinges on whether the plural noun with the definite article requires a minimum number of recipients or can be satisfied by a single individual. The ruling has practical implications for executors and heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Note the two cases in the passage: (1) bequest to a named person and to 'al-masakin' jointly, and (2) bequest solely to 'al-masakin'.
2
State the Shaykhayn's ruling
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, in the joint bequest the named person and the masakin each receive half of the one-third. In the sole bequest, it can be given to one masakin.
3
State Imam Muhammad's ruling
Muhammad holds that in the joint bequest the named person gets one-third and the masakin get two-thirds. In the sole bequest, it must be given to at least two masakin.
4
Trace the underlying usul principle
The difference stems from interpreting the plural 'al-masakin' with the definite article: Shaykhayn view it as indicating the genus (so one individual suffices), while Muhammad views it as plural requiring a minimum of two.
This principle is based on the earlier discussion in the text about the minimum number for plural with alif-lam.
5
Apply the principle to reach the distribution ratio
Because Shaykhayn treat 'al-masakin' as a genus, the bequest is split equally between the two categories (named person and the genus). Muhammad, requiring at least two masakin, gives them a larger share to cover the minimum.
The ratio difference (1/2 vs 1/3 for the named person) reflects the number of miskin needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولو أوصى بثلثه لفلان وللمساكين فنصفه لفلان ونصفه للمساكين عندهما وعند محمد ثلثه لفلان وثلثاه للمساكين ولو اوصى للمساكين له صرفه الى مسكين واحد عندهما وعنده لا يصرف إلا إلى مسكينين بناء على ما بيناه
He said: If he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to a certain person and to the miskin, then half of it is for that person and half for the miskin according to them (Shaykhayn). According to Muhammad, one-third of it is for that person and two-thirds for the miskin. If he bequeaths to the miskin, he may give it to one miskin according to them, but according to him, he cannot give it except to two miskin, based on what we have explained.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage continues the application of the previous principle. When a testator bequeaths one-third to a named individual and to 'the masakin' (with the definite article), the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) rule that the named person takes half and the masakin take half. Muhammad rules that the named person takes one-third and the masakin take two-thirds. The difference mirrors the earlier dispute about the minimum number for plural with alif-lam: Shaykhayn consider it as genus requiring only one individual, so the masakin as a category receive a share that can be given to a single miskin. Muhammad, requiring at least two, gives the masakin a larger portion (two-thirds) to accommodate two individuals. If the bequest is simply 'to the miskin' without a named person, the same disagreement applies: Shaykhayn allow giving to one miskin; Muhammad insists on at least two.

Key Terms
مساكين (masakin): The poor; a category of beneficiaries in bequests. With the definite article, it is treated as a genus by Shaykhayn, allowing a single individual to suffice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) All to Zaid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest to 'al-masakin' is split equally with a named person per Shaykhayn, because the definite article indicates a genus, allowing one recipient to suffice.

Interpreting the Sharing Clause (Ishrak) in Wills
Ruling on distribution with ishrak in wills

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for distributing bequests when a testator uses the word 'ishrak' (share) to include a third party, distinguishing between equal and unequal original bequests.

Core Idea
Ishrak implies equality; when full equality is impossible, we approximate by taking half from each legatee.

A testator sometimes uses the phrase 'I have included you as a partner' to bring a third person into an existing bequest. How should the shares be divided? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling based on the linguistic meaning of 'partnership' (sharika) and the principle of implementing the testator's words as far as possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the testator's wording
Note that the testator said 'I have included you as a partner with them' (اشركتك معهما). The key term is 'ishrak', which linguistically implies equality (musawat).
The ruling depends on the literal meaning of this term.
2
Check equality of the original bequests
Compare the amounts given to the first two legatees. If they are equal (e.g., 100 each), perfect equality among all three is possible. If they are unequal (e.g., 400 and 200), perfect equality is impossible.
Uniformity of the original bequests allows a simple third-of-each distribution.
3
Apply the appropriate distribution
For equal bequests, the third person takes one-third from each bequest, so all three end up with equal shares. For unequal bequests, the third person takes half of each bequest, achieving equality with each legatee individually (i.e., he takes the same amount that legatee retains after giving half).
This honors the testator's intent to the fullest extent possible.
4
Understand the rationale
The Hanafi ruling is based on the linguistic meaning of 'ishrak' as equal sharing. When full equality among all is impossible, we still act on the wording by making the third person equal with each legatee in terms of the share taken from each.
The underlying principle is to fulfill the testator's wish as much as possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن اوصى لرجل بمائة درهم ولأخر بمائة ثم قال لاخر قد اشركتك معهما فله ثلث كل مائة لان الشركة للمساواة لغة وقد امكن اثباته بين الكل بما قلناه لا تحاد المال لانه يصيب كل واحد منهم ثلثا مائة بخلاف ما اذا اوصى لرجل باربع مائة ولاخر بمائتين ثم كان الاشراك لانه لا يمكن تحقيق المساواة بين الكل التفاوت المالين فحملناه على مساواته كل واحد بتنصيف نصيبه عملا باللفظ بقدر الامكان
He said: And whoever bequeaths to a man one hundred dirhams and to another one hundred, then says to another: I have included you as a partner with them, then he gets one-third of each hundred, because partnership linguistically means equality, and it is possible to establish it among all by what we said due to the unity of wealth, so each one of them gets two-thirds of a hundred. Contrary to when he bequeaths to a man four hundred and to another two hundred, then he includes a third, because equality among all cannot be achieved due to the disparity of the two amounts. So we interpret it as his being equal with each one by halfing his share, acting on the wording as much as possible.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage explains two scenarios of a 'sharing clause' in a will. The principle is that the word 'ishrak' (partnership) implies equality (musawat) in language. In the first case, where two legatees each receive 100 dirhams, and the testator tells a third person 'I have included you as a partner with them,' we can achieve perfect equality among all three by giving the third person one-third of each bequest (i.e., 33.33 from each), resulting in each of the three having 66.67 dirhams (since each of the first two keeps 66.67 after giving 33.33). This works because the original bequests are equal. In the second case, the bequests are unequal: 400 to one, 200 to another. The testator then tells a third person that he is included as a partner. Since perfect equality among all three is impossible (the total is 600, and equal thirds would be 200 each, but that would require taking more from the first than is possible? Actually the issue is that if we try to make all three equal, each should get 200, but the first originally was to get 400, so he would have to give up 200, and the second would have to give up nothing? No, the second would have to give up 0? Let's analyze: Total 400+200=600. Three equal shares = 200 each. So the first would have to give 200 to the third, the second would have to give 0? That would not be a partnership. Alternatively, if we treat the third as having a claim to half of each bequest (like taking a 50% share in each), then the first gives 200, keeps 200; the second gives 100, keeps 100; the third gets 200+100=300. That yields amounts of 200, 100, 300 — not equal. But the text says we 'make him equal with each one by halfing his share' (مساواته كل واحد بتنصيف نصيبه). This means we achieve equality between the third and each of the first two individually (i.e., the third gets the same as what each of the first two keeps after giving half). So from the first, the third takes half of the original bequest (200), and from the second half (100), so the third gets 300. The first keeps 200, the second keeps 100. The third is not equal to the first or second overall, but he is equal to the first in the sense that he took half of the first's bequest? Actually the phrase 'equal with each one' likely means that the third's share from each legatee is equal to what that legatee retains after giving half? Let's read the Urdu explanation: 'خالد عمرو سے دو سو اور بکر سے سولے گا' - so Khaled takes 200 from Amr and 100 from Bakr. That does not give equality among all three. The ruling is that we act on the wording of partnership as much as possible. Since full equality is impossible, we give the third half of each bequest, making him a 'partner' in a sense of taking an equal portion from each. This is the only feasible way to honor the sharing clause.

Key Terms
اشراك (ishrak): The act of including someone as a partner (sharik) in a bequest. Linguistically implies equality (musawat) in sharing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first scenario (two bequests of 100 each), what share does the third person (the one included as a partner) receive from each of the first two?
A) Half of each (50 from each)
B) One-third of each (33.33 from each)
C) All of one and none of the other
D) None; the partnership is invalid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school implements the testator's sharing clause (ishrak) by giving the third person one-third of each bequest when original bequests are equal, and half of each when they are unequal, maximizing fulfillment of the testator's words.

Istihsan Overrides Qiyas: Acknowledging an Unknown Debt
Explanation of istihsan vs qiyas in debt acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a testator instructs heirs to confirm a debt claimant and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.

Core Idea
A testator's instruction to confirm a claimant is treated as a will delegating amount estimation to the legatee, limited to one-third.

This passage explores a nuanced Hanafi ruling where a testator tells his heirs that someone has a debt upon him and instructs them to confirm the claimant's statement. The surface analogical reasoning (qiyas) would reject the claim, but the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) to uphold it up to one-third. Understanding this distinction deepens your grasp of the role of intention and need in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the apparent ruling
Identify that the testator says 'So-and-so has a debt upon me, confirm him' to his heirs. The ruling: the claimant is confirmed up to one-third of the estate by istihsan.
2
Identify the qiyas argument
Qiyas would reject the claim entirely because the acknowledgment is of an unknown amount, which requires clarification before enforcement, and the instruction to confirm without proof contradicts Sharia principles.
3
Identify the flaw in qiyas and basis for istihsan
The testator's known intent to benefit the claimant over the heirs is achievable via a will, and the claimant may need to discharge the debt. Istihsan recognizes this intent and the need.
4
Understand the istihsan reasoning
The instruction is construed as a will delegating the estimation of the debt amount to the legatee, as if the testator said: 'Give him whatever he claims from my wealth.'
5
Determine the limit of confirmation
Since it is treated as a will, it is limited to one-third of the estate. The claimant is confirmed up to one-third, not beyond, even if he claims more.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن قال لفلان على دين فصدقوه معناه قال ذلك لورثته فانه يصدق إلى الثلث وهذا استحسان وفي القياس لا يصدق لان الاقرار بالمجهول وان كان صحيحا لكنه لا يحكم به إلا بالبيان وقوله فصدقوه صادر مخالفا للشرع لأن المدعى لا يصدق إلا بحجة فتعذر اثباته إقرارا مطلقا فلا يعتبر. وجه الاستحسان انا نعلم ان من قصده تقديمه على الورثة وقد امكن تنفيذ قصده بطريق الوصية وقد يحتاج اليه من يعمل باصل الحق عليه دون مقداره سعيا منه في تفريغ ذمته فيجعلها وصية جعل التقدير فيها إلى الموصى له كانه قال اذا جاءكم فلان وادعى شيئا فاعطوه من مالي ما شاء هذه معتبرة من الثلث فلهذا يصدق على الثلث دون الزيادة.
تشریح: زید اپنے ورثہ سے کہتا ہے کہ خالد کا میرے ذمہ قرض ہے تو جب وہ آپ لوگوں کے پاس اگر اپنے قرض کا مطالبہ کرے اور جو مقدار بتا دے تو تم اس کی تصدیقی کرنا، لہذا خالد زید کے مرنے کے بعد آیا اور اپنے قرض کا مطالبہ کیا اور اس کی مقدار بتائی تو تہائی ترکہ تک اس کی تصدیق کی جائے گی، اور یہ حکم استحسان کا ہے ورنہ قیاس یہ چاہتا ہے کہ خالد کی بالکل تصدیق نہ کی جائے اسلئے کہ زید نے اگر چہ اقرارتو کیا ہے لیکن اس میں قرض کی مقدار نہیں کھولی اور اقرار مجہول اگر چہ صحیح ہو جاتا ہے لیکن اس پر حکم کا ترتب اس وقت ہوتا ہے جبکہ اس کا بیان آگیا ہو اور بیان نہیں آیا تھا یہاں تک کہ موصی کا انتقال ہو گیا اور اب وہ بیان کرنے کا محل نہیں رہا۔ اور اس نے جو یہ کہا تھا کہ تم اس کی تصدیق کر دینا یہ بھی اقرار مذکور کے لئے بیان نہیں بن سکتا کیونکہ اس کا صادر خود خلاف شرع ہوا ہے اسلئے کہ شریعت کا ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ جب مدعی کوئی دعوی کرے تو اس کی تصدیق حجت کے بعد کی جاتی ہے اور موصی کہتا ہے کہ بغیر حجت کے اس کی تصدیق کر دینا یہ خلاف شرع ہے، تو یہ اقرار اقرار مطلق نہ ہوا کہ اس پر اقرار کے احکام جاری کئے جائیں اسلئے قیاس کا تقاضہ تھا کہ یہ اقرار غیر معتبر ہو اور خالد کی بالکل تصدیق نہ کی جائے۔ مگر ہم نے قیاس کو چھوڑ دیا اور استحسان پر عمل کیا ہے۔
استحسان کی دلیل: ہم جانتے ہیں کہ اس کا ارادہ فلاں کو ورثا پر مقدم کرتا ہے اور اس کے ارادہ کی تحفیظ ممکن ہے وصیت کے طریقہ پر اور کبھی اس اقرار کی جانب وہ شخص محتاج ہوتا ہے جو اپنے اوپر اصل حق کو جانتا ہے نہ کہ اس کی مقدار کو اپنی جانب سے اپنے ذمہ کی تفریغ میں کوشش کرتے ہوئے تو وہ اس کو ایسی وصیت قرار دیتا ہے جس میں تقدیر موصی لہ کی جانب محول ہو گویا کہ موصی نے یوں کہا کہ جب تمہارے پاس فلاں شخص آئے اور میرے مال میں سے کچھ کا دعوی کرے تو میرے مال میں سے اس کو اتنا دے دینا جتنا وہ چاہے اور یہ وصیت تہائی سے معتبر ہوتی ہے اسی وجہ سے فلاں کی تہائی تک تصدیق کی جائے گی نہ کہ زیادہ میں۔
He said: And whoever says 'So-and-so has a debt upon me, so confirm him' — meaning he said that to his heirs — then he is confirmed up to one-third, and this is istihsan. In qiyas, he is not confirmed because acknowledgment of an unknown (amount) is valid but is not ruled upon except with clarification. And his statement 'confirm him' is contrary to Sharia because a claimant is not confirmed except with proof, so establishing this as an absolute acknowledgment is impossible, so it is not considered. The basis of istihsan: we know that his intent is to give him preference over the heirs, and it is possible to execute his intent through the path of a will. Sometimes a person who knows the existence of the right upon him but not its amount acts to discharge his liability, so he makes it a will where the estimation is delegated to the legatee, as if he said: 'When So-and-so comes to you and claims something, give him whatever he wishes from my wealth.' This is considered from one-third, so he is confirmed up to one-third, not beyond.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and its justification from the Hanafi school. The passage type is 'ruling with proof' where the ruling is stated, followed by the qiyas (analogy) that would contradict it, and then the istihsan (juristic preference) that overrides the qiyas. The author first states the ruling: if a person (the testator) tells his heirs that someone has a debt upon him and instructs them to confirm that person's claim, then the claimant's statement is believed up to one-third of the estate. This is istihsan. In qiyas, the claimant would not be believed at all because the testator's acknowledgment was of an unknown amount, and such an acknowledgment requires clarification to be enforceable. Moreover, instructing the heirs to confirm without proof contradicts the Sharia principle that a claimant must provide evidence. Thus qiyas would render the acknowledgment invalid. However, istihsan is applied because the testator's intent is to benefit the claimant over the heirs, and this intent can be realized through a will. Since the testator knows a debt exists but not its exact amount, his statement is construed as a will where the legatee determines the amount, but limited to one-third. The key point is that the ruling is based on istihsan due to the testator's known intent and the need to facilitate the discharge of obligations, even though the strict analogy would reject it.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to a stronger consideration (need, intent, or custom).
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning from an established case to a new one.
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right or debt; it is a binding admission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the testator's acknowledgment is treated as a will where the legatee determines the amount.
B) Because qiyas allows it on the basis of necessity.
C) Because the heirs are obligated to fulfill the debt regardless of amount.
D) Because the testator's statement is an absolute acknowledgment that is binding.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to treat a testator's instruction to confirm a debt claimant as a will limited to one-third, overriding the strict analogy that would reject the claim.

8 min
Priority of Known Wills Over Unknown Claims in Estate Distribution
Ruling on distributing estate when there are known wills and an unknown acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for distributing an estate when there are both known specific wills and an unknown acknowledgment, and apply it to a numerical example.

Core Idea
Known shares separate first; an unknown claim cannot compete with known rights.

In the previous lesson, we learned that if a testator makes a vague acknowledgment (e.g., 'Khalid has a claim on me'), the executor confirms him up to one-third of the estate. But what if the testator also made specific wills? This lesson shows that known bequests and inheritance shares take absolute priority; the unknown claim only affects the residual one-third after known wills are satisfied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the known rights
Determine which parties have defined, quantifiable rights: heirs are entitled to two-thirds of the estate (unless other fixed shares apply), and beneficiaries of specific wills are entitled to their stated amounts from the one-third portion.
Heirs' shares are fixed by inheritance rules; specific wills are fixed by the testator's instruction.
2
Separate the known shares immediately
From the total estate, set aside the portion for known bequests (maximum one-third) and the residue for heirs. This separation is obligatory before considering any unknown claim.
The known rights are 'ma'lum' and must be satisfied first.
3
Analyze the status of the unknown claim
The unknown acknowledgment (e.g., Khalid's claim) is 'majhul'. In Hanafi law, a majhul right does not compete with ma'lum rights. Therefore, it cannot displace known shares.
This is a key principle: the unknown yields to the known.
4
Apply the rule to the one-third pool
The unknown claim can only be considered from the one-third that was set aside for bequests, and only after all specific known wills from that one-third have been fully paid. If the unknown claim plus known wills exceed one-third, the claims are proportionally reduced within the one-third, but known wills take precedence.
If known wills consume the entire one-third, the unknown claim gets nothing.
5
Perform a sample calculation
Given an estate of 3000 dirhams, a specific will of 300 to Zayd, and an unknown claim from Khalid, the one-third is 1000. Zayd takes his full 300 from the 1000. The remaining 700 of the one-third is available for Khalid, up to his claimed amount (if less than 700, he gets the lesser).
The unknown claim is satisfied only from the residual of the bequest portion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وان اوصی بوصايا غير ذالك يعزل الثلث لاصحاب الوصايا والثلثان للورثة لان ميراثهم معلوم وكذا الوصايا معلومة وهذا مجهول فلا يزاحم المعلوم فيقدم عزل المعلوم.
تشریح: اس سے پہلے مسئلہ میں جبکہ موصی نے یہ وصیت کی تھی کہ جب خالد آئے اور میرے مال میں اپنا حق بتائے تو جتنا وہ حق بنائے اس کو دے دینا تو یہ حکم جو مذکور ہوا ہے کہ ثلث تک خالد کی تصدیق کی جائے گی اس وقت ہے جبکہ موصی نے کچھ اور وصایا اسکے علاوہ نہ کی ہوں لیکن اگر اس نے اس کے علاوہ اور بھی وصیتیں کر رکھی ہیں تو پھر یہ حکم نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کا حکم یہ ہے جو یہاں مذکور ہے۔ یہاں سب سے پہلا کام تو یہ ہو گا کہ اصحاب الوصایا جو خالد کے علاوہ ہیں پورے ترکہ میں سے ان کا ثلث الگ کر دو اور ورثا کے دو ثلث الگ کر دو، یعنی کل ترکہ کے تین حصے کر دئیے جائیں ان میں سے ایک اصحاب الوصایا کیلئے اور دو ورثا کے لئے، اس لئے کہ اصحاب الوصایا کا ثلث معلوم ہے اور ورثا کا ثلثان معلوم ہے اور خالد کا حق مجہول ہے معلوم کا مزاحم نہیں ہوسکتا اس لئے سب سے پہلا کام یہ ہوگا کہ
He said: And if he made other wills besides that, one-third is set aside for the beneficiaries of the wills, and two-thirds for the heirs, because their inheritance is known, and likewise the wills are known, and this (the unknown acknowledgment) is unknown, so the unknown does not compete with the known, thus separating the known is given priority.
Commentary: In the previous issue, when the testator made a will that when Khalid comes and claims his right from my property, give him whatever he claims, that ruling that Khalid is confirmed up to one-third applies only when the testator made no other wills besides that. But if he made other wills in addition, then the ruling changes. Here, the first step is to separate one-third for the other will beneficiaries (excluding Khalid), and two-thirds for the heirs. That is, the total estate is divided into three parts: one part for the known will beneficiaries, and two parts for the heirs. Because the share of the will beneficiaries is known, and the heirs' share is known, while Khalid's right is unknown, so the unknown cannot compete with the known, so the first step is to separate the known.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage provides a supplementary ruling to the previous one. The passage type is a ruling statement explaining how to distribute the estate when there are both known wills (with specified beneficiaries) and an unknown acknowledgment (like the earlier case). The author clarifies that the earlier ruling (accepting the unknown claim up to one-third) only applies when no other wills exist. If other wills exist, they take priority. First, the total estate is divided: one-third is allocated to the beneficiaries of the known wills, and two-thirds to the heirs. The unknown claim (Khalid's) then can only affect the one-third that was meant for wills, but since that one-third is already taken by known wills, Khalid's claim may be limited to any surplus after the known wills are satisfied, still within the overall one-third limit. The rationale is that known rights (inheritance shares and specific wills) are definite and cannot be displaced by an unknown claim. Thus, the unknown claim does not compete with the known shares; the known shares are separated first, and the unknown claim is considered only within the residuary one-third (the bequest portion) after satisfying known wills.

Key Terms
وصایا (wasaya): Plural of wasiyya (will); here refers to specific bequests made by the testator.
ثلث (thulth): One-third of the estate, which is the maximum limit for bequests without heirs' permission.
معلوم (ma'lum): Known; refers to heirs' shares and specific will beneficiaries whose entitlements are determined.
مجھول (majhul): Unknown; here refers to the undefined claim of Khalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator made a specific will of 100 dirhams to Zayd and an acknowledgment that Khalid has a claim, with an estate of 600 dirhams, how is the estate distributed?
A) Separate one-third (200) for wills; Zayd takes 100, the remaining 100 goes to Khalid; heirs take 400.
B) Divide the entire estate equally between Zayd, Khalid, and heirs.
C) Pay Khalid first as a debt, then give Zayd his 100 from the remainder, then heirs get the rest.
D) Combine Zayd and Khalid's shares and split the one-third proportionally.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, known rights (inheritance and specific wills) are separated from the estate before considering any unknown claim; the unknown claim is limited to the residual of the one-third.

Different Interpretations in Conditional Bequests
Illustrates how testator's intent differs for conditional bequest components

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a single conditional phrase can have different legal effects for each component of a conditional statement, using the Hanafi principles of mutlaq and muhaqqaq.

Core Idea
A conditional phrase may be interpreted differently for each consequence based on the intended legal effect.

This passage explores how a testator's conditional statement about a specific room is interpreted: if the room falls into his share, the exact room is given; otherwise, an equivalent place. The author illustrates this with an analogy from family law, showing that the same phrase 'first child' means different things for divorce and for freeing a slave. This lesson will guide you through the reasoning and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two components of the conditional bequest
Note that the testator's statement has two possible outcomes: if the room falls into his share, the exact room is intended; if not, an equivalent place is intended.
2
Understand the analogy: the slave girl's child scenario
Zayd declares: 'When my slave girl bears her first child, that child is free, and my wife is divorced.' Analyze how the same condition 'first child' applies differently to divorce and freeing.
3
Distinguish mutlaq vs muhaqqaq in the analogy
For divorce, an absolute (mutlaq) child is intended — alive or dead, both trigger divorce. For freeing, a verified (muhaqqaq) living child is required because the right to freedom cannot pass to a dead child.
4
Apply the same reasoning to the room bequest
If the specific room falls into the testator's share, it is the exact room (muhaqqaq). If not, an equivalent place is intended (mutlaq in the sense of value).
5
Conclude on testator's intention
The testator's intention is deduced from the nature of each legal consequence. Different parts of a conditional statement may require different interpretations.
This principle is used in Hanafi jurisprudence to reconcile seemingly contradictory conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جزاء میں مطلق بچہ ہے اور محقق کے حق میں زندہ بچہ ہے۔
تشریح یہ آخری جو جواب دیا گیا ہے کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ موسی کی مرادی پہلے سے یہ ہو کہ اگر یہ کمرہ میرے حصہ میں آجائے تو بعینہ یہی دیا جائے گا اور اگر یہ میرے حصہ میں نہ آئے تو اس کے مثل جگہ دی جائے گی۔
یہاں سے مصنف اس کی نظیر پیش فرماتے ہیں، مثلا زید کی ایک باندی ہے جس کا اس نے خالد سے نکاح کر رکھا ہے اور ایک زید کی بیوی ہے، اب زید کہتا ہے کہ میری باندی جب پہلا بچہ جنے گی تو وہ بچہ آزاد ہے اور بیوی کو طلاق ہے، لہذا جب وہ بچہ پیدا ہوا تو آزاد ہوگا اور زید کی بیوی کو طلاق پڑے گی۔ لیکن طلاق اور معشق دونوں مراد جدا گانہ ہے یعنی وقوع طلاق کے لئے مطلق بچہ مراد ہے یعنی بچہ زندہ پیدا ہو یا مردہ بہر دوصورت طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی، اور آزاد ہونے کے لئے زندہ بچہ مراد ہے، یعنی اگر وہ زندہ بچہ جنی تو بچہ آزاد ہوگا ورنہ اگر بچہ مرا ہوا پیدا ہوا تو وہ آزاد ہوگا، لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ زید نے پہلے بچہ سے طلاق کے حق میں مطلق بچہ مراد لیا ہے اور عشق کے حق میں زندہ مراد لیا ہے، اسی طرح یہاں اگر یہ کمرہ میرے حصہ میں آجائے تو یہی کمرہ مراد ہے اور اگر حصہ میں نہ آئے تو اس کے مثل دوسری جگہ مراد ہے۔
Regarding the consequence, an absolute child is intended, and regarding the verified (right), a living child is intended. Explanation: This last answer given is that it is possible that the testator's intention from the beginning was that if this room falls into my share, then exactly this same (room) will be given, and if it does not fall into my share, then a place equivalent to it will be given. From here, the author presents an analogy for this, for example: Zayd has a slave girl whom he has married to Khalid, and Zayd also has a wife. Now Zayd says: When my slave girl bears her first child, that child is free, and my wife is divorced. So when that child is born, it will be free and Zayd's wife will be divorced. But divorce and freeing are intended separately: for the occurrence of divorce, an absolute child is intended, i.e., whether the child is born alive or dead, in both cases divorce occurs; and for freeing, a living child is intended, i.e., if she bears a living child, the child is free, otherwise if the child is born dead, it will not be free. Hence it is understood that Zayd, with 'first child', intended an absolute child for divorce and a living child for freeing. Similarly, here: if this room falls into my share, then this very room is intended; and if it does not fall into my share, then another place equivalent to it is intended.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling that explains how a testator's conditional statement can have different legal implications for each consequence. The author provides an analogy from family law: a man declares that his slave girl's first child will be free and his wife divorced. The 'first child' is interpreted absolutely for divorce (born alive or dead) but restrictively for freeing (only if born alive). This illustrates that in the bequest context, the testator's phrase 'this room' means the exact room if it falls into his share, but an equivalent place if it does not. The legal principle is that different parts of a conditional statement may require different interpretations based on the intended effect. The analogy is purely illustrative and does not introduce new evidence; it clarifies the earlier ruling on the bequest of a specific room.

Key Terms
مطلق (mutlaq): Unrestricted, absolute; here it means the child is considered without qualification (alive or dead) for the purpose of divorce.
محقق (muhaqqaq): Verified; here it refers to the established right (of the legatee) which requires the child to be alive for freeing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the analogy, why does the word 'first child' have different meanings for divorce and freeing?
A) Because the testator used different words for each.
B) Because divorce requires an absolute child while freeing requires a living child due to their different legal effects.
C) Because the slave girl is married to Khalid.
D) Because the testator changed his mind.

Key Takeaway
The same conditional phrase can have different legal implications for each part of a conditional statement based on the nature of the right and the testator's inferred intent.

Method of Division When Bequeathed Room Falls into Other Share: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the calculation method for compensating legatee when specific room falls into other partner's share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs regarding compensation for a specific bequest that falls into a partner's share, and apply the respective calculation methods.

Core Idea
Compensation for a bequeathed room falling into another's share: half or full value? The dispute centers on the portion the testator owned.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a nuanced scenario: a testator bequeaths a specific room in a jointly owned house, but that room falls into the partner's share. The estate must compensate the legatee, but how much? Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) differ on the calculation. Understanding this dispute illuminates deeper principles of bequests and division of property in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The testator owns half of a 100-cubit house and bequeaths a 10-cubit room. At death, the room falls into the partner's share. Determine the testator's portion: 50 cubits.
2
Understand Imam Muhammad's view
Imam Muhammad holds that the legatee is entitled to half the room (5 cubits) because the testator only owned half the house. Thus, the testator's 50 cubits are divided into 10 shares of 5 cubits each: 9 shares (45 cubits) to heirs, 1 share (5 cubits) to legatee.
Denominator = 10 shares.
3
Understand the two shaykhs' view
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the legatee is entitled to the whole room (10 cubits) because the will was for the entire room. The testator's 50 cubits are divided into 5 shares of 10 cubits each: 4 shares (40 cubits) to heirs, 1 share (10 cubits) to legatee. (The text also expresses this as 11 shares of 5 cubits, but simplifies to 5 shares.)
Denominator = 5 shares (or 11 if broken into 5-cubit units).
4
Compare the two methods
Note the different denominators and resulting shares. Imam Muhammad's method gives the legatee 5 cubits; the two shaykhs give 10 cubits. The dispute reflects a difference in interpreting the scope of the bequest.
5
Reflect on the author's note
The author (al-Marghinani) adds a note (tanbeeh) suggesting that the two shaykhs' view is simpler: divide into 5 shares. This indicates a preference, though the mufta bihi is not explicitly stated.
Refer to Zaylai's commentary for further tarjih.

Source Text

تقسیم کا طریقہ
ثم اذا وقع البيت فى نصيب غير الموصى والدار مائة ذراع والبيت عشرة اذرع يقسم نصيبه بين الموصى له و بين الورثة على عشرة اسهم تسعة منها للورثة وسهم للموصى له وهذا عند محمد فيضرب الموصى له بخمسة اذرع نصف البيت ولهم بنصف الدار سوى البيت وهو خمسة واربعون فيجعل كل خمسة سهما فيصير عشرة ترجمہ پھر جب کہ کمرہ غیر موصی کے حصہ میں آئے اور حویلی سوگز ہو اور کمرہ دس گز ہوتو موصی کا حصہ موضی لڈ اور ورثا کے درمیان ت تقسیم کیا جائے گا ان میں سے نو ورثا کے لئے اور ایک حصہ موضی لا کے لئے ہے اور یہ محمد کے نزدیک ہے پس موصی لۂ نصف بیت کے تناسب سے پانچ گزلے گا اور ورثا کے لئے آدھی حویلی ہے کمرہ کے علاوہ اور وہ ( کمرہ کے علاوہ آدھی حویلی ) پینتالیس گز ہیں تو ہر پانچ گز کو ایک حصہ قرار دیا جائے گا تو دس حصے ہو جائیں گے۔ تشریح جب یہ معلوم ہو چکا ہے کہ اگر وہ کمرہ زید کے حصہ میں نہ آئے تو اس کے برابر زمین خالد کو دی جائے گی تو اس تقسیم کا کیا طریقہ ہوگا اگر چہ مسئلہ خود واضح تھا مگر مصنف نے اس کو بیان کیا ہے۔ فرمایا ہے کہ امام محمد کے نزدیک موصی لیہ کو کمرہ کے نصف کا عوض دیا جائیگا لہذا اگر پورا گھر سو گز ہے اور کمرہ دس گز ہے تو موضعی لن کو پانچ گرملیں گے یعنی زید کے حصہ میں دار کے پچاس گز آگئے اور کمرہ کا نصف پانچ گز ہے لہذا پانچ گز زمین زید کو دی جائے گی اور باقی پینتالیس گز زید کے ورثہ کے لئے ہوں گے۔
اس کو بالفاظ دیگر یوں کہ لیجئے کہ زید کے پورے ترکہ کے دس سہام کر کے ان میں سے نو زید کے ورثا کو اور ایک موصی لۂ کو دیا جائے گا کیونکہ پچاس میں سے پینتالیس (2) ہے اور پچاس میں سے پانچ ہے ہے، یہ تفصیل امام محمد کے نزدیک ہوگی کہ بنوارہ دس سہام پر ہوگا اور ہر پانچ گز کو ایک سہم قرار دیا جائے گا۔

كتاب الوصايا
۱۵۲
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۹
شیخین کے نزدیک تقسیم کا طریقہ
وعندهما يقسم على احد عشر سهما لان الموصى له يضرب بالعشرة و هم بخمسة واربعين فتصير السهام احد عشر للموصى له سهمان ولهم تسعة
ترجمہ اور شیخین کے نزدیک (موضی کا حصہ ) گیارہ حصوں پرتقسیم کیا جائیگا اس کے لئے موضعی لہ دس گھر کے حساب سے لگا اور ورثہ پینتالیس کے تو سہام گیارہ ہو جائیں گے موسی لہ کیلئے دو حصے اور ورثا کے لئے نو ۔ تشریح یہ حضرات شیخین کے نزدیک تقسیم کا طریقہ ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ موصی کے حصہ میں جو پچاس گز آئے ہیں ان کے گیارہ حصے کر لئے جائیں ان میں سے نو حصے ورثا کو اور دو موضعی لہ کو دئیے جائیں گے۔
یعنی پچاس کو بڑھا کر ٫۵۵ میں سے دس موضی لڈ اور پینتالیس ورثہ کے ہوں گے کیونکہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہی کمرہ دس گز کا ہے لہذا وہی دس مذکورہ طریقہ پر موضی لیا کو دیئے جائیں گے۔ جس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ زید نے خالد کوگو یا اس کی وصیت کی ہے اور پورا دار سوگز ہے جب سو میں دس نکل گئے تو نوے باقی رہے جو دونوں شریکوں کے درمیان مشترک ہیں اور ہر فریق کے پینتالیس ہو گئے مگر شریک کا حصہ گھٹایا نہیں جاسکتا لہذا انکو تو اسکے پورے پچاس ملیں گے البتہ مابقی پہچاس میں ورثا کے پینتالیس اور موصی لہ کے دس کے حساب سے جب دیکھا گیا اور ہر حصہ پانچ گز کا ہو تو اصل کو ۵۵ / قرار دیا جائے گا تا کہ گیارہ حصے ہو سکیں ۔
تنبیہ یہ مصنف نے طول لا حائل اختیار کیا ہے ورنہ فرماتے کہ شیخین کے نزدیک پچاس گز وں کو پانچ سام پرتقسیم کیا جائے گا یعنی چالیس ۴۰ ورثہ کے اور ایک سہم یعنی دس موصی لا کے ہوں گے امام محمد کے نزدیک چونکہ کمرہ کا نصف پکتا ہے تو وہ مجبور اس سہام پر تقسیم امام کے قائل ہوں گے مگر شیخین کے نزدیک پورے کمرہ کا مثل ملے گا تو پانچ حصوں پر تقسیم کر دیا جائے گا۔ (زیلعی ۱۹۴ ج ۶)
Method of division on ten shares. Then when the house falls into the portion of other than the testator, and the courtyard is one hundred cubits and the room is ten cubits, his portion is divided between the legatee and the heirs into ten shares: nine for the heirs and one for the legatee. This is according to Muhammad. So the legatee takes five cubits, half the room, and they (heirs) take half the courtyard excluding the room, which is forty-five cubits. Then every five cubits is made one share, resulting in ten shares. Translation: Then when the room falls into the portion of other than the testator, and the courtyard is one hundred cubits and the room is ten cubits, the testator's portion is divided between the legatee and the heirs, nine for the heirs and one for the legatee, and this is according to Muhammad. So the legatee takes five cubits according to half the room, and the heirs take half the courtyard excluding the room, which is forty-five cubits, then every five cubits is made one share, resulting in ten shares. Explanation: Since it has been known that if that room does not fall into Zayd's portion, then land equivalent to it will be given to Khalid, so what will be the method of division? Although the issue itself was clear, the author has stated it. He said that according to Imam Muhammad, the legatee is compensated with half the room. So if the entire house is one hundred cubits and the room is ten cubits, then the legatee will take five cubits, i.e., Zayd's portion of the house is fifty cubits, and half the room is five cubits; so five cubits of land will be given to Zayd (the legatee), and the remaining forty-five cubits will be for Zayd's heirs. In other words, Zayd's entire estate is made into ten shares, nine for Zayd's heirs and one for the legatee, because fifty minus forty-five is forty-five? (text unclear) and fifty minus five is five. This detail is according to Imam Muhammad: division is into ten shares, every five cubits being one share. The method of division according to the two shaykhs. And according to them, it is divided into eleven shares because the legatee takes ten and they take forty-five, so the shares become eleven: two for the legatee and nine for them. Translation: And according to the two shaykhs, (the testator's portion) is divided into eleven shares; for this, the legatee takes at the rate of ten (cubits of the room) and the heirs take forty-five, so the shares become eleven: two for the legatee and nine for the heirs. Explanation: This is the method of division according to the respected two shaykhs. The result is that the fifty cubits that came into the testator's portion are divided into eleven shares, nine shares to the heirs and two to the legatee. That is, fifty is increased to fifty-five, of which ten go to the legatee and forty-five to the heirs, because according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the room is ten cubits, so those ten are given to the legatee in the mentioned manner. The detail is: Zayd made a will to Khalid for that (room), and the entire house is one hundred cubits. When ten are taken out, ninety remain, which are shared between the two partners, each getting forty-five. But the partner's share cannot be reduced, so he gets his full fifty. However, from the remaining fifty, when considered as forty-five for heirs and ten for legatee, and each share is five cubits, the base is made 55/ (55?) so that eleven shares can be made. Note: The author has adopted a lengthy method; otherwise, he says that according to the two shaykhs, the fifty cubits are divided into five shares: forty for the heirs and one share (ten) for the legatee. According to Imam Muhammad, since half the room is given, he will be bound to follow that division into shares, but according to the two shaykhs, the legatee gets the equivalent of the whole room, so division is into five shares. (Zaylai 194, vol. 6)
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the method of compensating the legatee when the bequeathed specific room falls into the share of the testator's partner (not the testator's own share). The testator's estate is half the house (50 cubits) because the house is 100 cubits and the testator owned half. The room is 10 cubits. Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) holds that the legatee is entitled to half the room (5 cubits) because the bequest is of a specific room, but since the testator only owned half the house, the effective compensation is half. Thus the testator's 50 cubits are divided into ten shares of 5 cubits each: 9 shares (45 cubits) to the heirs, 1 share (5 cubits) to the legatee. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the legatee is entitled to the entire room (10 cubits) because the testator's will was for the whole room; the fact that it fell into the partner's share means the testator's estate must compensate fully. Therefore, from the testator's 50 cubits, the heirs get 40 cubits (8 shares of 5) and the legatee gets 10 cubits (2 shares of 5), totaling 11 shares of 5 cubits each? Actually the calculation yields 11 shares only if base is 55, but the note clarifies that in effect it is 5 shares: 40 for heirs, 10 for legatee. The dispute centers on whether the legatee receives half or the entire equivalent of the room. Imam Muhammad's view gives the legatee half, while the two shaykhs give the full value. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but the author's note suggests the two shaykhs' view is simpler.

Key Terms
سهم (sahm): Share, portion; used here as a unit of division of the testator's estate.
موصى له (musa lahu): Legatee, the person to whom a bequest is made.
نصيب (naseeb): Portion, specifically the testator's portion of the jointly owned property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 1 share
B) 2 shares
C) 9 shares
D) 10 shares

Key Takeaway
When a bequeathed specific asset falls outside the testator's share, compensation is due; the amount depends on the agreed interpretation of the bequest's scope.

Difference Between Will and Acknowledgment for Property Not Owned
Ruling that acknowledgment of another's property is valid but will is not if property is not owned

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between an acknowledgment (iqrar) and a will (wasiyya) in terms of ownership requirement, and state the Hanafi ruling for each when the property is not owned at the time of declaration.

Core Idea
Acknowledgment of another's property is valid even without ownership; a will of unowned property is void even if later owned.

In this passage from the Hidayah, the author examines a critical distinction between two similar legal acts: acknowledgment (iqrar) and will (wasiyya). Although both involve declaring a right to property, they differ fundamentally in their legal nature and validity conditions. Understanding this distinction resolves a potential ambiguity in joint ownership cases and clarifies the scope of intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two legal acts
Recognize that the passage contrasts acknowledgment (iqrar) and will (wasiyya), both involving property not owned by the declarant at the time of declaration.
2
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note the report of two positions: some scholars say the same dispute (whether the legatee gets the exact property or equivalent) applies to acknowledgment, while Imam Muhammad holds there is no dispute and acknowledgment is valid by consensus.
3
Understand Imam Muhammad's distinguishing proof
The proof is the difference in legal nature: acknowledgment is akin to testimony (shahada) and does not require ownership at the time, while a will is a disposition (tasarruf) that requires ownership at the time of bequest.
4
Apply to the example
Apply the ruling to the example of a jointly owned house: if Zayd acknowledges a specific room as belonging to Khalid, Khalid will definitely get that room or equivalent, regardless of Zayd's ownership at the time, resolving the dispute that arises if it were a will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كان مكان الوصية اقرار قيل هو على الخلاف وقيل لا خلاف فيه لمحمد والفرق له ان الاقرار بملک الغير صحيح حتى ان من اقر بملك الغير لغيره ثم ملكه يؤمر بالتسليم الى المقر له والوصية بملك الغير لا تصح حتى لو ملكه بوجه من الوجوه ثم مات لا تصح وصيته ولا تنفذ
ترجمہ اور اگر وصیت کی جگہ اقرار ہو تو کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ اختلاف پر ہے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ اس میں محمد کا اختلاف نہیں ہے اور محمد کے لئے وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ ملک غیر کا اقرار صحیح ہے یہاں تک کہ جس نے ملک غیر کا اقرار کیا اپنے غیر کے لئے پھر مقر اس کا مالک ہو گیا تو مقر کو مقولہ کی جانب سپرد کرنے کا حکم دیا جائے گا اور دوسرے کی ملکیت کی وصیت کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر موصی موضی یہ کا کسی طریقہ پر مالک ہو جائے پھر مر جائے تو اس کی وصیت صحیح نہ ہوگی اور نہ نافذ ہوگی ۔
تشریح مثلا زید و عمرو کے درمیان ایک مکان مشترک ہے اور زید نے اس میں سے ایک معین کمرے کے بارے میں خالد کے لئے اقرار کیا کہ یہ خالد کی ملکیت ہے تو یہاں بالاتفاق خالد کو یہ پورا کمرہ ملے گا یا اسکے برابر زمین ملے گی یعنی اس میں امام محمد کا اختلاف نہیں ہے
And if instead of a will there was an acknowledgment, it has been said that it is subject to the same difference, and it has been said that there is no difference for Muhammad. And the distinguishing reason for him is that acknowledgment of another's property is valid, to the extent that if someone acknowledges another's property as belonging to someone else, then later becomes its owner, he is ordered to hand it over to the acknowledged person. But a will of another's property is not valid, to the extent that if the testator becomes the owner of the bequeathed property in some way and then dies, his will is not valid and not executed. Explanation: For example, Zayd and Amr jointly own a house, and Zayd acknowledges to Khalid regarding a specific room that it is Khalid's property. Here, by consensus, Khalid will get that entire room or land equivalent to it, i.e., there is no difference from Imam Muhammad.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof that distinguishes between a will (wasiyya) and an acknowledgment (iqrar) regarding property that is not owned by the declarant at the time of declaration. The issue arises in the context of a specific room in a jointly owned house: if the testator makes a will of that room (which may not be his exclusive property), there is a dispute among the Hanafi imams about whether the legatee gets the exact room or equivalent compensation. However, if the testator instead makes an acknowledgment that the room belongs to the legatee, the ruling is different. According to Imam Muhammad (and some say it is unanimous), an acknowledgment of another's property is valid and binding even if the acknowledger does not own it at the time. If the acknowledger later acquires ownership, he must hand it over. In contrast, a will of unowned property is invalid ab initio; even if the testator later becomes owner, the will does not become valid. The proof is the principle that acknowledgment is a form of testimony that does not require ownership, whereas a will is a disposition of property that requires ownership at the time of bequest. The practical consequence is that in the example, Khalid will definitely receive the room or its equivalent if the declaration is acknowledgment, removing the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment; a declaration that someone else has a right to property, even if the declarant does not own it.
وصية (wasiyya): Will, bequest; a disposition of property to take effect after death, requiring ownership at the time of bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, why is acknowledgment of another's property valid while a will of unowned property is not?
A) Because acknowledgment is a type of sale.
B) Because acknowledgment does not require ownership at the time, while a will is a transfer that requires ownership.
C) Because a will must be witnessed.
D) Because acknowledgment can be revoked.

Key Takeaway
Acknowledgment of unowned property is valid and binds the acknowledger upon acquisition; a will of unowned property is void ab initio.

The Key Distinction: Bequest vs. Acknowledgment of Another's Property
Clarifies the ruling difference when a testator acknowledges a room vs. bequeaths it from another's property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Muhammad distinguishes between acknowledgment (iqrār) and bequest (waṣiyyah) concerning another's property, and state the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Acknowledgment of another's property is binding; bequest of another's property is void, even if you later own it.

This passage addresses a subtle dispute within the Hanafi school: does Imam Muhammad agree with Abu Hanifa on the validity of acknowledging another's property? The preferred view says yes, and the distinction rests on the nature of acknowledgment as a declaratory act versus bequest as a dispositive one. Understanding this difference is crucial for drafting valid wills and handling property acknowledgments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two transactions
Recognize that the passage discusses both acknowledgment (iqrār) and bequest (waṣiyyah) when the property belongs to someone else at the time of the act.
2
State the Hanafi position on each
Acknowledgment of another's property is valid and binding; bequest of another's property is invalid (batil) even if the testator later acquires ownership.
This is the established position of Abu Hanifa.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some scholars claim Imam Muhammad differs on acknowledgment, giving only half the property. The preferred view (mukhtār) says he agrees with Abu Hanifa on full validity.
The text says 'this absence of disagreement is the chosen position.'
4
Understand the talil (reasoning)
Acknowledgment informs a pre-existing right (it is declaratory); bequest creates a new right that requires ownership at the time of bequest. Thus, later acquisition does not validate the bequest but does bind the acknowledger.
This is the distinguishing reason (فَرْق) attributed to Imam Muhammad.
5
Apply the thamarah (practical outcome)
If a person acknowledges a room in another's house for a third party, the third party gets the whole room by consensus. If he bequeaths it, the bequest is void unless the owner consents after death.
This shows the real-world impact of the distinction.

Source Text

And if instead of a bequest there was an acknowledgment, it is said that it is subject to disagreement, and it is said that there is no disagreement regarding Muhammad. The distinction for him is that acknowledgment of another's property is valid, such that if someone acknowledges that a property belongs to someone else, then later becomes its owner, he is ordered to hand it over to the acknowledgee. But a bequest of another's property is not valid, such that even if the testator comes to own it in some way and then dies, his bequest is not valid and is not executed. Translation: And if instead of a bequest there was an acknowledgment, it is said that this is based on disagreement, and it is said that there is no disagreement in it regarding Muhammad. The distinguishing reason for Muhammad is that acknowledgment of another's property is valid, to the extent that if someone acknowledges that a property belongs to another, and then the acknowledger becomes its owner, he is commanded to surrender it to the acknowledgee. But bequeathing another's property is not valid; even if the testator comes to own the bequeathed item in any way and then dies, his bequest is not valid and not executed. Explanation: For example, Zaid and 'Amr share a house, and Zaid makes an acknowledgment to Khalid regarding a specific room in it that 'This room is Khalid's property.' Here, by consensus, Khalid will get the entire room or land equivalent to it, i.e., there is no disagreement of Imam Muhammad in this. And this absence of disagreement is the chosen position, although some scholars have said that Imam Muhammad also has a disagreement here: whether the room is half or an equivalent of half will be given. In the case of no disagreement, an objection arises against Imam Muhammad: why did he differentiate between bequest and acknowledgment? The answer is that there is a difference between acknowledgment and bequest: acknowledgment regarding another's property is valid, but bequest of another's property is not valid. The proof for acknowledgment's validity is that if Zaid acknowledges that this house of Khalid belongs to Bakr, and then Zaid becomes the owner of the house, he is bound by his acknowledgment and is ordered to hand over the house to Bakr. But if he bequeaths another's property and then becomes the owner of the bequeathed item, still the bequest is not valid and not executed.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage addresses a key distinction within Hanafi fiqh: the difference between a bequest (waṣiyyah) and an acknowledgment (iqrār) concerning property belonging to someone else. The author first notes that there is a difference of opinion on whether Imam Muhammad's view differs from Abu Hanifa in the case of acknowledgment. According to the preferred view, Imam Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa that acknowledgment of another's property is valid and binding, whereas a bequest of another's property is not. The commentator explains the reasoning: acknowledgment is a legal recognition of pre-existing ownership; if the acknowledger later acquires ownership, he must fulfill his acknowledgment. A bequest, however, is a disposition of property; if it belongs to another at the time of bequest, it is void ab initio, and subsequent acquisition of ownership does not validate it. The example of a jointly owned house clarifies the application: if Zaid acknowledges that a specific room belongs to Khalid, Khalid gets it by consensus; but if Zaid bequeaths that room to Khalid while it is not his, the bequest is invalid even if Zaid later becomes owner. This distinction is important for practical fatwa.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrār): Admission or acknowledgment of a fact; here specifically acknowledgment of another's ownership over property.
وصیت (waṣiyyah): A bequest or will directing the transfer of property after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Khalid gets nothing
B) Khalid gets the whole room by consensus
C) Khalid gets only half
D) It depends on the heirs' approval

Key Takeaway
Acknowledgment informs a pre-existing right and is binding even if the property is not owned at the time; bequest creates a new right and requires ownership at the time—a distinction that must be maintained in practice.

Bequest of Another's Property: Owner's Permission and Delivery Requirement
Explains validity and owner's option when bequeathing another's property with permission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on bequeathing another's property with the owner's permission, explain the owner's right to refuse delivery, and distinguish this from the heirs' permission on excess bequest.

Core Idea
Owner's permission alone does not bind delivery; the bequest becomes a gift requiring possession.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced scenario: a testator bequeaths a specific item he does not own, such as a trust held for someone else. After the testator's death, the owner may permit the bequest. However, the owner retains the right to withhold delivery. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its underlying reasoning, comparing it to the case of bequests exceeding one-third where heirs' permission eliminates their objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is bequeathing another's property. The ruling: it is suspended on the owner's permission; if permitted, the owner may still refuse delivery.
Focus on the phrase 'فان دفعه فهو جائز وله ان يمنع' — if he gives it, it is valid, and he has the right to refuse.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites no explicit Quran or hadith; the ruling is derived from the principle that a tabarru' from another's property is suspended on ratification, and delivery is required for completion of a gift.
The proof is based on the nature of tabarru' and qabḍ.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The reasoning: the testator's act is a tabarru' with another's property, so it depends on the owner's permission (ijāzah). When the owner permits, it becomes his own tabarru', which is like a gift (hibah) requiring delivery (qabḍ) for completeness.
The key word is 'تبرع' — gratuitous act.
4
Contrast with the heirs' permission case
The text contrasts with bequest exceeding one-third where heirs permit: there the bequest is valid from the testator, and permission only removes the heirs' objection, so delivery is obligatory.
The distinction hinges on whose property the bequest originated from.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The legatee cannot compel the owner to deliver; the owner can change his mind even after permitting.
This protects the owner's property rights.

قال ومن اوصى من مال رجل لاخر بالف بعينه فاجاز صاحب المال بعد موت الموصى فان دفعه فهو جائز وله ان يمنع لان هذا تبرع بمال الغير فيتوقف على اجازته واذا اجاز يكون تبرعا منه ايضا فله ان يمتنع من التسليم بخلاف ما اذا اوصى بالزيادة على الثلث واجازت الورثة لان الوصية فى مخرجها صحيحه لمصادفتها ملک نفسه والامتناع لحق الورثة فاذا اجازوها سقط حقهم فنفذ من جهة الموصى ترجمہ اہم احمد نے فرمایا اور جس نے دوسرے کے لئے معین ہزار کی وصیت کی دوسرے شخص کے مال میں سے پھر موسی کی موت کے بعد صاحب مال نے اجازت دیدی پس اگر اس نے وہ مال موضی لا کو دید یا تو جائز ہے اور صاحب مال کو اختیار ہے کہ دینے سے انکار کرے اس لئے کہ یہ موصی کا فعل ) غیر کے مال سے تبرع ہے تو صاحب مال کی اجازت پر موقوف ہے اور جب کہ اس نے اجازت دیدی تو اسکی جانب سے بھی تبرع ہوگا تو مالک مال کو حق ہے انکار کرے بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ موصی نے تہائی سے زیادہ کی وصیت کی اور ورثا نے اجازت دیدی اس لئے کہ وصیت اپنے مخرج میں صحیح واقع ہوئی اس کے ملنے کی وجہ سے اپنی ملک سے اور زائد میں منع ہو نا حق ورثا کی وجہ سے تھا پس جب ورثا نے اس کی اجازت دیدی تو ان کا حق ساقط ہو گیا پس وصیت موجی کی جانب سے نافذ ہو گئی۔ تشریح زید کے پاس مثلاً خالد کی امانت رکھی ہوئی ہے اس میں سے ہزار روپے کی وصیت بکر کے لئے کردی تو چونکہ یہ وصیت مال غیر کی ہے اسلئے یہ وصیت خالد کی اجازت پر موقوف ہے اگر اس نے موجی کی موت کے بعد اس کی اجازت دیدی تو ٹھیک ورنہ باطل ہے۔ اور جواز کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ خالد موضی بہ کو بکر کے قبضہ میں دیدے، وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ خالد کا فعل مذکور ہبہ کے درجہ میں ہے اور ہبہ کی تمامیت کے لئے قبضہ شرط ہے اور اگر خالد نے اجازت دیدی لیکن موضی بہ کو ابھی موضی لا کے سپردنہیں کیا تھا تو اس کو حق ہے کہ دینے سے رک جائے۔ کیونکہ یہاں زید کا فعل غیر کے مال سے تبرع ہے تو یہ اس غیر کی اجازت پر موقوف ہوگا اور جب غیر نے اجازت دیدی تو غیر کی
He said: And whoever bequeaths from the property of a man to another a specific thousand, then the owner of the property permits after the death of the testator, if he gives it, it is valid, and he has the right to refuse because this is a gratuitous act with another's property, so it depends on his permission. And when he permits, it becomes a gratuitous act from his side as well, so he has the right to abstain from delivery, unlike the case when he bequeaths more than one-third and the heirs permit, because the bequest in its origin is valid, coinciding with his own property, and the prevention was due to the right of the heirs. So when they permit, their right falls, and the bequest is executed from the side of the testator. Translation: Ahmad (probably Imam Ahmad, but here it's the text of Hidayah) said: And whoever bequeaths to another a specific thousand from the property of a man, then the owner of the property permits after the testator's death, if he hands it over, it is valid, and he has the right to refuse because this act of the testator is a gratuitous act with another's property, so it is suspended on the owner's permission. And when he permits, it becomes a gratuitous act from his side as well, so the owner has the right to refuse delivery, unlike the case when the testator bequeaths more than one-third and the heirs permit, because the bequest in its origin is valid, coinciding with his own property, and the prevention was due to the right of the heirs. So when they permit, their right falls, and the bequest is executed from the side of the testator. Explanation: For example, Zaid has Khalid's amānat (trust) with him, and he bequeaths a thousand rupees from it to Bakr. Since this bequest is of another's property, it is suspended on Khalid's permission. If he permits after the testator's death, it is fine; otherwise it is void. For validity, it is necessary that Khalid give the bequeathed item into Bakr's possession. The reason is that Khalid's mentioned act is like a gift (hibah), and delivery is a condition for the completion of a gift. And if Khalid permitted but did not yet hand over the bequeathed item to the legatee, he has the right to refuse delivery. Because Zaid's act here is a gratuitous act with another's property, so it is suspended on that other's permission, and when the other permits, then the other (the owner) becomes the donor, and delivery is required.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on a bequest of a specific item from another person's property. The testator (mūṣī) bequeaths an item he does not own (e.g., a thousand dirhams held as trust) to a legatee. After the testator's death, the owner of that property (e.g., the bailor) may give permission (ijāzah). If he permits and then hands over the item, the bequest is valid. However, the owner has the option (khiyār) to refuse delivery, because the bequest is a gratuitous act (tabarru') with another's property, and it only becomes effective from the owner's side as a new gift. The commentator distinguishes this from the case where a testator bequeaths more than one-third of his own property and the heirs permit: in that case, the bequest is originally valid from the testator (since it was his own property), and the heirs' permission merely removes their right to object, so delivery is obligatory. Here, the bequest was never valid from the testator, so the owner's permission makes it a separate gift, requiring delivery (qabḍ) for completion. The explanation uses the example of a trust (amānat): Zaid has Khalid's money as trust and bequeaths it to Bakr. Khalid's permission and delivery are needed for Bakr to own it.

Key Terms
تبرع (tabarru'): A gratuitous act or donation; here the testator's act of bequeathing another's property is a tabarru' that depends on the owner's permission.
اجازة (ijāzah): Permission or ratification given by the owner after the testator's death, making the bequest a valid gift from him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If Khalid permits after Zaid's death regarding the bequest of his trust property to Bakr, but then refuses to hand it over, what happens?
A) Bakr can force Khalid to deliver
B) The bequest is void
C) Khalid is entitled to refuse, and Bakr has no claim
D) The heirs must deliver

Key Takeaway
Owner's permission alone does not obligate delivery; the bequest becomes a gift requiring actual possession.
