Legatee vs Creditor: The Istihsan Reasoning for Partnership
Explains istihsan reasoning for legatee being partner with heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that a legatee is a partner with heirs, not a priority claimant, and apply the istihsan reasoning to distinguish a bequest from a debt.

Core Idea
A legatee is a partner with heirs; a creditor takes priority — the distinction is based on istihsan.

In Hanafi inheritance law, not all claims on an estate are treated equally. While a creditor is given precedence over heirs, a legatee (musa lahu) is classified as a partner with the heirs. This lesson explores the istihsan reasoning behind this distinction, as explained in Al-Hidayah, and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of claims
Distinguish between debt (dain) and bequest (wasiyyah) as claims on the estate. Debt takes precedence over inheritance, while bequest is limited to one-third and does not enjoy priority.
2
Recognize the base ruling (qiyas)
If a bequest were treated like a debt, the legatee would have priority over heirs, but this would risk exceeding the one-third limit if multiple heirs confessed.
This is the qiyas that istihsan overrides.
3
Trace the istihsan reasoning
The confession to a bequest is confined to the confessor's share because the estate is common property in the hands of multiple heirs. The legatee cannot take from the other heir's share without that heir's own confession.
The key phrase: 'he is confessing to one-third of what is in his hand'.
4
Apply the ruling
In a two-heir scenario where one confesses, the legatee receives one-third of the confessor's share only, preserving the heirs' two-thirds intact.
5
Contrast with debt
A debt confession obligates the entire estate because debt takes precedence over inheritance; the confessor's admission of precedence affects all heirs equally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیہ - مگر مقر کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کل ترکہ میں وہ میرا مساوی ہے میرے مقبوضہ میں وہ میر امسادی نہیں ہے۔
استحسان کی دلیل ، صاحب دین ورنا سے مقدم ہوتا ہے
كتاب الوصايا
(تدبر)
وجه الاستحسان انه اقر بثلث شائع فى التركة وهى فى ايديهما فيكون مقرا بثلث ما في يده بخلاف ما اذا اقر احدهما بدين لغيره لان الدين مقدم على الميراث فيكون مقرا بتقدمه فيقدم عليه
ترجمہ استحسان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقر نے ترکہ کے اندر ثلث شائع کا اقرار کیا ہے اور ترکہ ان دونوں کے قبضہ میں ہے تو وہ اپنے مقبوضہ میں ثلث کا اقرار کرنے والا ہو گا بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک نے اپنے غیر کے لئے قرض کا اقرار کیا ہو تو وہ غیر کے تقدم کا اقرار کرنے والا ہوگا پس وہ غیر اس پر مقدم کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح مگر ہم نے قیاس مذکور کو چھوڑ کر استحسان پر عمل کیا ہے، استحسان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقر نے کل ترکہ میں بطریق شیوع ثلث کا موضی لہ کے لئے اقرار کیا ہے اور کل ترکہ دونوں بھائیوں کے قبضہ میں ہے تو مقر کے قبضہ میں جو کچھ ہے وہ اس کے ثلث کا اقرار کرنے والا ہوگا۔
البتہ اگر ان دونوں میں سے ایک نے یہ اقرار کیا کہ باپ پر خالد کا اتنا قرض ہے تو اب اگر مقر کا سارا حق بھی ختم ہو جائے تو اس کی پرواہ نہیں کی جائیگی بلکہ مقر لہ کا حق ادا کیا جائے گا کیونکہ دین میراث پر مقدم ہوتا ہے تو اس نے خود اقرار کیا ہے کہ فلاں مجھ پر مقدم ہے لہذا اس کے اقرار کے مطابق اس کو مقدم رکھا جائے گا۔
موصی لہ ورثا کے ساتھ شریک ہوتا ہے
اما الموصى له بالثلث شریک الوارث فلا يسلم له شى الا ان يسلم للورثة ثلثاه ولانه لواخذ منه نصف ما في یده فربما يقر الابن الاخر به ايضا فيا خذ نصف ما في يده فيصير نصف التركة فيزاد على الثلث
ترجمہ بہر حال موضی لا بالشٹ و ہ وارث کا شریک ہے تو اس کے لئے کوئی چیز پر نہیں کی جائے گی مگر اس صورت میں کہ ورثا کے لئے ترکہ کا دو ثلث سالم رہے اور اس لئے کہ موضی لذا گر مقر سے اس کے مقبوضہ کا نصف لے لے تو ہو سکتا ہے کہ دوسرا بیٹا بھی اس کا اقرار کرے تو موضی لیا اس کے مقبوضہ کا نصف لیگا تو ترکہ کا نصف ہو جائے گا تو وہ ٹکٹ سے زیادہ ہو جائے گا۔ تشریح تو صاحب دین ور سے مقدم ہوتا ہے اور موصی لۂ مقدم نہیں ہوتا بلکہ ور خا کا شریک ہوتا ہے،لہذا موضی لۂ کو اس کا حق اسی وقت دیا جائے گا جب کہ دو ثلث ورثا کے لئے سالم بچے ۔
لہذا صورت مذکورہ میں مقر کے مقبوضہ کا ثلث ہی اس کو دیا جائے گا نہ کہ نصف ، کیونکہ اگر موصی لیا کو نصف دیدیا گیا اور ہوسکتا ہے کہ دوسرا بیٹا بھی اقرار کر لے تو اس سے بھی نصف دلایا جائے گا تو اب موصی لیہ کو آدھا تر کر مل گیا حالانکہ اس کو ثلث سے زیادہ نہیں دیا جائے گا۔
لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ موضی لیہ کو مقر کے مقبوضہ کا ٹکٹ ملے گا۔
Warning - But the confessor's meaning is that in the entire estate he is my equal, but in my possession he is not my partner. The proof of istihsan: the creditor is given precedence over the heir. The book of bequests. (Contemplate) The face of istihsan: He confessed to one-third of the estate as a common share, and the estate is in their hands, so he is confessing to one-third of what is in his hand, contrary to if one of them confessed to a debt for another, because debt is given precedence over inheritance, so he confesses to its precedence, so it is given precedence over him. Translation: The proof of istihsan is that the confessor confessed to one-third of the estate as a common share, and the estate is in the possession of both, so he will be confessing to one-third of his own possession, unlike the case where one of them confesses to a debt for another, then he confesses to the precedence of that other, so that other will be given precedence over him. Explanation: But we abandoned the mentioned analogy and acted upon istihsan. The proof of istihsan is that the confessor confessed to one-third of the entire estate for the legatee in a common manner, and the entire estate is in the possession of both brothers, so whatever is in the confessor's possession, he will be confessing to its one-third. However, if one of them confessed that the father owes Khaled such a debt, then even if the confessor's entire right is lost, it will not be considered; rather the right of the confesse will be paid because debt is given precedence over inheritance, so he himself confessed that so-and-so is given precedence over me, so according to his confession, he will be given precedence. The legatee is a partner with the heirs. As for the legatee of one-third, he is a partner of the heir, and nothing is delivered to him unless two-thirds are delivered to the heirs, and because if he were to take from him half of what is in his hand, perhaps the other son might also confess to him, so he would take half of what is in his hand, making it half of the estate, exceeding the third. Translation: In any case, the legatee of one-third is a partner of the heirs, so nothing will be delivered to him except when two-thirds of the estate remain intact for the heirs, and because if the legatee takes half of the confessor's possession, perhaps the other son might also confess, then the legatee would take half of his possession, making it half of the estate, which exceeds the third. Explanation: So the creditor is given precedence over the heir, but the legatee is not given precedence; rather he is a partner of the heirs. Therefore, the legatee's right will be given only when two-thirds remain intact for the heirs. Hence in the mentioned case, only one-third of the confessor's possession will be given to him, not half, because if half were given to the legatee and perhaps the other son also confesses, then he would be given half from him too, resulting in half the estate for the legatee, whereas he cannot be given more than one-third. Therefore, it is understood that the legatee will receive one-third of the confessor's possession.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the text of Al-Hidayah, explaining the legal status of a legatee (musa lahu) in relation to heirs and creditors. The author begins by clarifying a warning (tanbih): when a person confesses to a share of the estate for another, that other is a partner in the entire estate, not just in the confessor's own portion. The key distinction is between a debt and a bequest. A creditor is given precedence over heirs because debt is superior to inheritance. However, a legatee is not given such precedence; he is merely a partner with the heirs. The proof of istihsan (juristic preference) is provided: if one of two heirs confesses to a bequest of one-third of the entire estate, since the estate is in the hands of both heirs, the confession applies to the confessor's share only, not the other's. This is contrary to a debt confession, which establishes precedence over the entire estate. The passage then explains the practical application: the legatee takes from the confessor's portion up to one-third of the estate, not more, to avoid exceeding the one-third limit if the other heir also confesses. Thus, the legatee does not take half from each; only one-third from the confessor's share. This preserves the heirs' right to two-thirds of the estate.

Key Terms
موصى له (musa lahu): The person in whose favor a bequest is made; the legatee.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas to avoid hardship, used here to give the legatee only from the confessor's share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if one of two heirs confesses to a bequest of one-third of the estate to a third party, what does the legatee receive?
A) One-third of the entire estate from both heirs equally
B) One-third of the confessor's share only, not half from each
C) One-half of the confessor's share
D) The entire estate if the other heir also confesses

Key Takeaway
The legatee is a partner with the heirs and only receives from the confessor's share within one-third, unlike a creditor who takes precedence over inheritance.

Bequest of a Slave Girl Who Gives Birth After Testator's Death: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Allocation
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute on bequest allocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a bequest of a slave girl who gives birth after the testator's death, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn when the mother and child exceed one-third of the estate.

Core Idea
When a bequest exceeds one-third, Abu Hanifa takes the shortfall fully from the mother first; the Sahibayn take proportionally from both.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in bequest law: a testator bequeaths a slave girl (jariyah), and after his death, she gives birth before the estate is divided. The passage from Al-Hidayah first states the agreed ruling when the mother and child are within one-third of the estate, then presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on how to allocate the one-third when their combined value exceeds it. Understanding this dispute sharpens your skill in distinguishing between principal and dependent subjects in bequests.

Guided Path
1
State the agreed ruling when within one-third
When the combined value of mother and child does not exceed one-third of the estate, both go to the legatee. The child follows the mother because it is a follower (taba'an) and the estate is still in the testator's ownership until division.
This ruling is agreed upon by all Hanafi authorities.
2
Identify the trigger of the dispute
When the combined value exceeds one-third, the legatee can only take one-third of the value. The dispute is on allocation: entirely from the mother or proportionally from both.
The shortfall is the amount exceeding one-third.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
The legatee takes his one-third entirely from the mother first; if anything remains, he takes from the child.
Abu Hanifa considers the mother the original subject.
4
State the Sahibayn's position
The legatee takes his one-third proportionally from both mother and child.
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad treat both as co-subjects of the bequest.
5
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf with a numerical example
If mother value = 100, child value = 100, one-third = 120: Abu Hanifa gives 100 from mother, 20 from child. Sahibayn give 60 from each.
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa the child mostly goes to heirs; under Sahibayn the legatee gets a greater share of the child.

Source Text

قال ومن أوصى لرجل بجارية فولدت بعد موت الموصى ولداو كلاهما يخرجان من الثلث فهما للموصى لان الام دخلت في الوصية اصالة والولد تبعا حين كان متصلا بالام فاذا ولدت قبل القسمة و التركة قبلها مبقاة على ملك الميت حتى يقضى بها دیونه دخل في الوصية فيكونان للموصى له
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی شخص کے لئے باندی کی وصیت کی پس اس نے موسی کی موت کے بعد بچہ جنا اور وہ دونوں تہائی سے نکل جاتے ہیں تو وہ دونوں موصی لنڈ کے لئے ہوں گے اس لئے کہ ماں وصیت میں اصالہ داخل ہے اور بچہ تبعا جب کہ وہ مال کے ساتھ متصل تھا پس جب کہ باندی نے ہوارہ سے پہلے بچہ جنا اور ترکہ ہوارہ سے پہلے میت کی ملکیت پر باقی رہتا ہے یہاں تک کہ اس سے میت کے قرضے ادا کئے جاتے ہیں تو بچہ دعیت میں داخل ہو گیا تو یہ دونوں موصی لا کے لئے ہوں گے۔ تشریح زید نے خالد کے لئے اپنی باندی کی وصیت کی اور زید کی موت کے بعد تقسیم ترکہ سے پہلے باندی نے ایک بچہ جنا اور باندی اور بچہ کی قیمت اتنی ہے کہ یہ دونوں ترکہ کی تہائی سے نکل جاتے ہیں یعنی ترکہ اور ان کا دو ثلث یا اس سے زیادہ موجود ہے تو باندی اور بچہ دونوں خالد کو ملیں گے اس لئے کہ وصیت میں ماں اصالہ داخل ہے کیونکہ اس کی وصیت زید نے کی ہے اور بچہ چونکہ بوقت وصیت ماں کے ساتھ متصل ہے تو بچہ بر بنا ہو تبعیت وصیت کے اندر داخل ہے اور ترکہ ہوارہ سے پہلے میت کی ملکیت پر برقرار رہتا ہے۔
دلیل جس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ میت کے ترکہ سے میت کے قرضے ادا کئے جاتے ہیں تو جب تر کہ ابھی میت ( زید ) کی ملکیت پر برقرار ہے اور کوئی مانع موجود نہیں ہے تو بچہ بھی وصیت کے اندر داخل ہو جائے گا اور جب ماں اور بچہ وصیت کے اندر داخل ہو گئے تو یہ دونوں خالد کو ملیں گے۔
ماں اور بیٹا تہائی سے خارج نہ ہوں تو کیا حکم ہے، اقوال فقہاء
وان لم يخرجا من الثلث ضرب بالثلث و اخذ ما يخصه منهما جميعا في قول أبي يوسف و محمد وقال ابو حنيفه ياخد ذالك من الام فان فضل شى اخذ من الولد
ترجمہ اور اگر وہ دونوں تہائی سے نکلیں تو موصی لا تنہائی کو لے گا اور ان دونوں میں سے جو اس کے حصہ میں آئے گا صاحبین کے قول پر اور ابوحنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ وہ ثلث ماں سے وصول کرے گا پس اگر کچھ بچ جائے تو اس کو بچہ سے لے گا۔
تشریح اور اگر ماں اور بچہ دونوں تہائی سے نہ نکلیں، یعنی ان کی قیمت کے علاوہ دو ثلث یا اس سے زیادہ باقی نہ بچے تو اس میں امام ابوحنیفہ وصاحبین کا اختلاف ہے، امام ابوحنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ اپنی تہائی ماں سے لیگا اگر ماں سے اس کی تنہائی پوری ہو جائے تو فبہا ورنہ اگر کچھ رہ جائے تو اس کی کو بچہ سے پورا کر لیا جائے گا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ماں اور بچہ دونوں سے اکٹھے ثالث کو وصول کیا جائے گا جس کی توضیح آئندہ مثال میں آرہی ہے۔ فرماتے ہیں۔
He said: And whoever bequeaths a slave girl to a man, and she gives birth after the testator's death, and both come out of the third, then both belong to the legatee, because the mother entered the bequest as a principal and the child as a follower since it was connected to the mother. So when she gives birth before division, and the estate before division remains in the ownership of the deceased until his debts are paid, the child enters the bequest, so both belong to the legatee. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And whoever bequeaths a slave girl to a person, and she gives birth after the testator's death, and both exit from the third, then both belong to the legatee, because the mother enters the bequest as a principal and the child as a follower, since it was connected to the mother. So when she gives birth before division, and the estate remains in the deceased's ownership until his debts are paid, the child enters the bequest, so both belong to the legatee. Explanation: Zaid bequeathed his slave girl to Khalid, and after Zaid's death, before division of the estate, the slave girl gave birth to a child, and the value of the slave girl and child is such that both come out of one-third of the estate, i.e., two-thirds or more of the estate remains, so both the slave girl and child will go to Khalid, because the mother enters the bequest as a principal, as Zaid bequeathed her, and the child, being connected to the mother at the time of the bequest, follows her into the bequest, and the estate remains in the deceased's ownership before division. The proof: The proof is that from the deceased's estate his debts are paid, and when the estate remains in the ownership of the deceased (Zaid) and there is no impediment, the child will also enter the bequest, and when mother and child have entered the bequest, both will go to Khalid. And if both do not come out of the third, what is the ruling? Statements of the jurists: And if they do not come out of the third, he takes according to the third and takes what is allocated to him from both of them in the statement of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. And Abu Hanifa said: He takes that from the mother, and if anything remains, he takes it from the child. Translation: And if both do not exit from the third, then the legatee takes according to the one-third and takes what is allocated to him from both of them according to the Sahibayn, and Abu Hanifa said: He will take that (the one-third) from the mother, and if anything remains, he takes from the child. Explanation: And if both mother and child do not exit from the third, i.e., two-thirds or more do not remain aside from their value, then there is a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Imam Abu Hanifa says that he will take his one-third from the mother; if the mother covers his one-third, then good, otherwise if something remains, he completes it from the child. And according to the Sahibayn, the one-third is taken from both together, the detail of which will come in the following example. They said.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage addresses the bequest of a slave girl (jariyah) who gives birth after the testator's death. It is a ruling with an intra-Hanafi dispute. The passage first states the ruling from the matn of Al-Quduri: if the mother and child together are within one-third of the estate (i.e., the rest of the estate is sufficient to cover two-thirds for the heirs), then both go to the legatee. The reason is that the mother is the primary subject of the bequest, and the child follows her because it was connected to her at the time of the bequest (even though born after death). The estate remains in the ownership of the deceased until division, so the child's birth before division means it is part of the estate and follows the mother into the bequest. The proof is based on the principle that the estate is treated as still belonging to the deceased until debts are paid and division occurs, so no impediment prevents the child from being included. Then the passage presents the dispute when the mother and child exceed one-third of the estate (i.e., their value is more than one-third). Imam Abu Hanifa's position: the legatee takes his one-third entirely from the mother first; if the mother's value is less than one-third, he takes the remainder from the child. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the legatee takes his one-third proportionally from both mother and child together. The text notes that a clarifying example follows. This difference arises from the principle: Abu Hanifa considers the mother to be the original subject of the bequest, so the child only takes what remains; the Sahibayn treat them as co-subjects.

Key Terms
جارية (jariyah): A female slave; in this context, the subject of a bequest.
تبعا (taba'an): As a follower or dependent, used here for the child that follows the mother into the bequest.
ضرب بالثلث (darb bil-thuluth): The legatee takes according to the one-third proportion, i.e., allocates the one-third among the items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a bequest of a slave girl exceeds one-third of the estate together with her after-born child, the legatee:
A) Gets nothing
B) Gets the slave girl only
C) Gets the slave girl and child proportionally (Sahibayn view, mufta bihi)
D) Gets the child only

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi bequest law, when a bequeathed slave girl gives birth after the testator's death, the child follows the mother into the bequest, but if the combined value exceeds one-third, the legatee takes only one-third proportionally, with the Sahibayn's view (proportional from both) being the relied-upon position.

Dispute on Bequest of Pregnant Slave Woman: The Follower Does Not Compete
Intra-Hanafi dispute with qiyas rebuttal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the child is not included in the bequest and evaluate the rebuttal of the Sahibayn's analogy to sale.

Core Idea
The follower cannot compete with the original; in bequest, including the child would nullify part of the original bequest.

The bequest of a pregnant slave woman raises a subtle question: does the child, born before the estate is divided, fall under the same bequest? The Sahibayn argue yes, by analogy to sale and manumission. Imam Abu Hanifa disagrees, applying a fundamental principle: the mother is the original, the child is a follower, and the follower cannot reduce the original's share. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply Hanafi usul principles—especially the limit of qiyas and the rule of tabi‘.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling Scenario
A person makes a bequest of a pregnant slave woman. She gives birth before the estate is divided. Does the child enter the bequest along with the mother? The dispute is about the scope of the bequest.
The bequest is limited to one-third of the testator's estate.
2
State the Sahibayn's Position and Their Analogy
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the child is included, analogizing to sale (where the child follows the mother in the sale) and manumission (where freeing the mother also frees the child). If the combined value exceeds one-third, the one-third is divided proportionally between mother and child.
This is a qiyas on established rules in other contracts.
3
State Imam Abu Hanifa's Position and His Principle
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the child is not included. His principle: the mother is the original (asl), the child is a follower (tabi‘), and the follower does not compete with the original. Including the child would effectively nullify part of the bequest in the mother, which is impermissible.
The principle that the follower cannot compete is a settled maxim in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Compare the Qiyas: Why the Analogy Fails
In sale, if the sale is enforced on the follower (the child), the original sale of the mother remains intact. The only effect is on the price, which itself is a follower in the contract—the price can be adjusted without invalidating the sale. In bequest, the bequest itself is the subject; if the child takes part, the bequest in the mother is reduced, directly affecting the original. Thus the analogy is dissimilar.
Abu Hanifa's rebuttal is based on the nature of the contract: in sale, price is tabi‘; in bequest, the subject matter (the mother) is asl and cannot be partially nullified by a tabi‘.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf and the Mufta Bihi
Practical consequence: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the legatee receives only the mother (up to one-third of the estate). The child is free and goes to the heirs. According to the Sahibayn, the legatee receives both mother and child, but the one-third is divided proportionally if the total exceeds it. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, as it aligns with the stronger principle.
This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and preferred by later Hanafi authorities like al-Marghinani.

اور اس کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے کسی نے حاملہ باندی بیچی اور ابھی تک مشتری نے باندی پر قبضہ نہیں کیا تھا کہ اس نے بچہ جنا تو بچہ بھی بیع میں داخل ہوگا اور وہ بھی مبیع شمار کیا جائے گا، اور جیسے کسی نے حاملہ باندی کو آزاد کیا تو سبعاً اس کا بچہ بھی آزاد ہو جائے گا تو جب وہ بچہ پیدا ہو گیا یعنی منفصل ہو گیا تو بچہ اپنی صفت حریت پر باقی رہے گا۔ یا یوں کہئے کہ کسی نے اپنی حاملہ باندی سے عشق کی وصیت کی پھر موصی کی موت کے بعد بٹوارہ سے پہلے اس نے بچہ جنا تو عشق ان دونوں میں نافذ ہوگا اور اگر وہ دونوں تہائی سے نہ نکلیں تو ثلث کو ان دونوں کے درمیان تقسیم کیا جائے گا۔ تو اسی طرح یہاں بھی جو بچہ بٹوارہ سے پہلے پیدا ہوا ہے اس کی جانب وصیت سرایت کرے گی اور دونوں کو موصی لہ کے لئے قرار دیا جائے گا لیکن اگر وہ ثلث سے نہ نکل سکیں تو ثلث کو ماں اور بچہ کے درمیان تقسیم کیا جائے گا یہ صاحبین کی دلیل ہے۔
امام اعظم کی دلیل
وله ان الام اصل والولد تبع فيه والتبع لا يزاحم الاصل فلو نفذنا الوصية فيهما جميعا تنتقض الوصية في بعض الاصل وذالك لا يجوز بخلاف البيع لان تنفيذ البيع فى التبع لا يؤدى الى نقضه في الاصل بل يبقى تا ما صحيحا فيه الا انه لا يقابله بعض الثمن ضرورة مقابله بالولداذ اتصل به القبض ولكن الثمن تابع في البيع حتى ينعقد البيع بدون ذكره وان كان فاسدا
ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ماں اصل اور بچہ اس میں تابع ہے اور تابع اصل کے مزاحم نہیں ہوا کرتا پس اگر ہم ان دونوں کے اندر وصیت کو نافذ کر دیں تو بعض اصل کے اندر وصیت ٹوٹ جائے گی اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے بخلاف بیع کے اس لئے کہ تابع میں بیع کو نافذ کر دینا اصل کے اندر بیج کو توڑنے کی جانب موڈی نہ ہوگا بلکہ اصل میں بیع نام صحیح باقی رہے گی مگر اصل کے مقابلہ میں شمن کا بعض حصہ نہ آسکے گا بعض ثمن کے مقابل ہونے کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے بچہ کے ساتھ جب کہ بچہ کے ساتھ قبضہ متصل ہو جائے لیکن بیچ میں شمن تابع ہے یہاں تک کہ شمن کو ذکر کئے بغیر بیع منعقد ہو جائے گی اگر چہ فاسد ہوگی۔
تشریح یہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ وعیت میں ماں اصل اور بچہ اس کے تابع ہے اور یہ اصول اپنی جگہ مسلم ہے کہ تابع اصل کا مزائم نہیں ہوا کرتا تو یہاں بچہ ماں کا مزاتم کیسے ہو سکتا ہے اس لئے کہ اگر ماں اور بچہ دونوں کے اندر وصیت کو نافذ مان لیا جائے تو بچہ ( تابع ) ماں کا ( اصل کا ) مزاحم ہو کر ماں کے کچھ حصہ میں وصیت کو باطل کر دے گا اور یہ نا جائز ہے کہ بچہ اصل کے اندر وصیت کو باطل کر دے۔ اس لئے کہ صاحبین کے قول کے مطابق ماں کا () وصیت میں داخل ہے اور (4) وصیت سے خارج ہو گیا اور یہ سب تابع کی وجہ سے ہوا ہے، اور آپ نے جو اس کو بیچ پر قیاس کیا ہے تو یہ قیاس مع الفارق ہے اس لئے کہ اگر بناء پر تبعیت تابع میں بیج کو نافذ کر دیا جائے تو اس سے اصل کی بیچ پر کوئی اثر نہیں پڑتا بلکہ بیچ بدستور نام اور صحیح رہے گی۔ تو بیع کو بیچ ہونے میں کوئی خلل نہیں پڑا، البتہ اتنا فرق پڑا کہ بچہ پر قبضہ کر رہا گیا تو چونکہ من کا کچھ حصہ بچہ کے مقابل ہوگا تو اصل کے مقابل جو شمن تھا اس میں کچھ کمی ہو گئی۔
خلاصہ کلام فرق مبیع پر یا بیچ پر نہیں پڑا بلکہ مشن پر فرق پڑنے کی وجہ سے کچھ خلل نہ ہوگا کیونکہ بیع میں شمن تابع ہے اصل نہیں ہے یہی تو وجہ ہے کہ بیع میں شمن کا ذکر نہ کیا جائے تو بیع منعقد ہو جاتی ہے اگر چہ فاسد ہوتی ہے، تو شمن پر فرق پڑنے کی وجہ سے کچھ خلل نہ ہوگا۔ اور یہاں وصیت میں خلل پڑ گیا ہے یعنی موضعی یہ پوری باندی تھی اور اب رہ گئی اس کا دو ثلث به
And its example is like someone sold a pregnant slave woman and the buyer had not yet taken possession when she gave birth, so the child is included in the sale and considered sold. And like someone freed a pregnant slave woman, then her child is also freed, so when the child is born separately, it remains free. Or say someone made a bequest of his pregnant slave woman, then after the testator's death before division she gives birth, the bequest applies to both, and if they both do not come out of one-third, the one-third is divided between them. Similarly here, the child born before division is included in the bequest and both are assigned to the legatee, but if they do not come out of one-third, the one-third is divided between mother and child. This is the evidence of the Sahibayn.

Imam Azam's evidence: He said that the mother is the original and the child is a follower, and the follower does not compete with the original. If we enforce the bequest in both, the bequest would be nullified in part of the original, which is not permissible. Unlike sale, because enforcing the sale in the follower does not lead to its nullification in the original; rather the sale remains valid in the original, except that some part of the price does not correspond to it due to the necessity of the child corresponding to some of the price when possession is connected. But the price is a follower in sale, so that the sale is concluded without mentioning it, even if it is invalid.

Translation: And Abu Hanifa's evidence is that the mother is the original and the child is a follower, and the follower does not compete with the original. So if we enforce the bequest in both, the bequest would break in part of the original, which is not permissible. Unlike sale, because enforcing the sale in the follower does not lead to breaking the sale in the original; rather the sale remains sound and valid in the original, but some part of the price cannot correspond to the original due to the necessity of the child corresponding to some of the price when possession is connected. But in sale, the price is a follower, so that the sale is concluded without mentioning it, even if it is invalid.

Explanation: This is Abu Hanifa's evidence, the gist of which is that in bequest, the mother is the original and the child is a follower, and it is a settled principle that a follower does not compete with the original. So how can the child compete with the mother? Because if we consider the bequest enforced in both, the child (follower) would compete with the mother (original) and nullify the bequest in some part of the mother, which is impermissible. Because according to the Sahibayn, the mother is included in the bequest and (some part) becomes excluded due to the follower. And the analogy to sale is a dissimilar analogy, because if we enforce the sale in the follower, it does not affect the sale of the original; rather the sale remains valid and sound. So no defect occurs in the sale itself, except that since possession of the child is taken, some part of the price corresponds to the child, so the price for the original decreases. Summary: The defect is not in the sold item or the sale, but in the price; therefore no defect occurs because in sale the price is a follower, not the original. This is why if the price is not mentioned, the sale is concluded, though invalid. So defect in price does not cause defect. But here in bequest, a defect occurs: the testator's entire slave woman was bequeathed, but now only two-thirds of her remains.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) regarding the ruling on a bequest of a pregnant slave woman when the child is born before the division of the estate. The Sahibayn argue that the bequest covers both the mother and the child, and if the combined value exceeds one-third, the one-third is divided proportionally between them. They analogize to sale and manumission, where the child follows the mother. Imam Abu Hanifa disagrees, asserting that the mother is the original (asl) and the child is a follower (tabi‘), and a follower cannot compete with the original. If the bequest were enforced in both, part of the original (the mother) would be voided, which is impermissible. He distinguishes the analogy to sale: in sale, enforcing the sale in the follower does not nullify the sale of the original; it only affects the price, which is a follower and can be adjusted. In bequest, however, the matter is different because the bequest is a testamentary disposition that must come from one-third, and the follower cannot reduce the original's share. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, as it aligns with the principle that the follower does not compete with the original.

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyyah): A testamentary disposition of property that takes effect after death, limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs consent.
تابع (tabi‘): A follower or dependent, legally considered part of the original (asl) in certain contexts.
اصل (asl): The original or principal subject of a legal ruling; here, the mother slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is the child of a pregnant slave woman not included in the bequest if born before division?
A) Because the child is not owned by the testator
B) Because the child is a follower and cannot compete with the mother as the original
C) Because the child is born after death and thus not part of the estate
D) Because the child must be freed automatically

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the principle that the follower does not compete with the original governs testamentary dispositions: the child of a bequeathed pregnant slave woman is not automatically included in the bequest.

Child Born After Division Belongs to Legatee
Ruling on child born after estate division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a child born after estate division and explain the legal principle of nama' (increase).

Core Idea
After estate division, a child born from the slave woman is the legatee's pure property — ownership once established attracts all subsequent increase.

This passage clarifies the legal status of a child born after the division of the estate in a bequest scenario. The key distinction is timing: if the slave woman gives birth before division, there are further rules; but if she gives birth after division, the ruling is clear and straightforward. Understanding this ruling reinforces the Hanafi principle that once ownership is settled, all subsequent gains belong to the owner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the slave woman giving birth after the estate is divided. The ruling is that the child belongs solely to the legatee (the recipient of the bequest).
This is a clear-cut ruling with no dispute.
2
Identify the legal reason (ta'lil)
The child is considered a pure increase (nama') of the legatee's property, because his ownership over the slave woman was established after division. In Hanafi law, once ownership is final, all subsequent accretions belong to the owner.
The principle of nama' is key.
3
Contrast with the pre-division scenario
The passage mentions that if birth occurs before division, different rules apply (likely subject to the one-third limitation). This contrast highlights the decisive role of timing.
Focus on the post-division rule for now.
4
Apply the ruling to similar cases
Generalize: any increase (fruit, rent, offspring) from property that has been finally assigned to an owner after division belongs to that owner, not to the estate.
This avoids confusion in modern contexts.

This is a straightforward application of the principle that once ownership is established, all subsequent gains accrue to the owner.

Acknowledgment, Bequest, and Gift to a Woman Who Becomes an Heir
Ruling on validity of transactions to a woman who becomes an heir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the validity of acknowledgment vs. bequest/gift in death illness when the recipient later becomes an heir, and apply the principle 'No bequest to an heir'.

Core Idea
Acknowledgment is binding immediately; bequest and gift are void if the recipient becomes an heir by death.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a nuanced ruling that tests your understanding of when each transaction takes effect. You will see why a sick person's acknowledgment of debt to a woman remains valid even if he later marries her, but his bequest or gift to her becomes void. The key is the timing of legal effectiveness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three transactions
The passage mentions three types of dispositions: acknowledgment of debt (iqrar), bequest (wasiyyah), and gift (hibah). Each is treated differently.
Acknowledgment is a binding declaration; bequest and gift in death illness are governed by the law of bequests.
2
State the scenario
A person in death illness makes these dispositions to a woman. He then marries her. He dies. At the time of death, she is his heir (wife).
The marriage occurs after the dispositions but before death.
3
Separate the rulings
The acknowledgment is valid; the bequest and gift are void. This is the core ruling.
The ruling is consistent across bequest and gift because gifts in death illness are treated like bequests.
4
Understand the rationale for acknowledgment
Acknowledgment is binding immediately (mulzim bi nafsihi). It creates a debt that is part of the estate. Since it was made when the woman was not an heir (ajnabiyyah), it remains valid.
The acknowledgment is not affected by later events because the obligation is already fixed.
5
Understand the rationale for bequest and gift
Bequest and gift (in death illness) take effect at death. At death, the woman is an heir. The principle 'No bequest to an heir' renders them void.
This principle is derived from the hadith 'La wasiyyata li-warith'.

Source Text

Chapter on considering the state of the bequest.
Translation: This is a chapter on considering the state of the bequest.
Explanation: In the previous section, it was stated that when the heirs do not permit, the bequest is only effective in one-third of the wealth, not more. In this chapter, the rulings will be explained: whether the time of making the bequest is considered or the state at the time of death. Since the attribute is subsequent to the described, the bequest is mentioned first and its state later.
Ruling on acknowledgment, gift, and bequest to a woman during death illness.
He said: When a sick person acknowledges a debt to a woman, or bequeaths something to her, or gives her a gift, then marries her, then dies, the acknowledgment is valid, but the bequest and gift are void. Because the acknowledgment is binding in itself, and she was a stranger at the time it was made. Therefore, it is considered from all the wealth and is not invalidated by debt, whether in health or illness, except that the second is postponed. Unlike the bequest, because it is a disposition effective at death, and she is then an heir, and there is no bequest to an heir.
Translation: Imam Muhammad said: When a sick person acknowledges a debt to a woman, or bequeaths something to her, or gives her a gift, then marries her, then dies, the acknowledgment is valid, and the bequest and gift are void. Because the acknowledgment is binding in itself.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Imam Muhammad (one of the Sahibayn) regarding transactions made by a person in death illness (marad al-mawt) to a woman who later becomes his wife and thus an heir. The ruling distinguishes between three types of dispositions: acknowledgment of a debt (iqrar), bequest (wasiyyah), and gift (hibah). Acknowledgment is valid and effective because it is a binding statement that creates a debt, and at the time it was made, the woman was not an heir (she was a stranger). Therefore, it is payable from the entire estate before distribution. However, a bequest and a gift are void because they are dispositions that take effect at death or are subject to the rules of bequest (gift in death illness is treated like a bequest). At the time of death, the woman has become an heir, and there is no bequest to an heir (according to the hadith: 'No bequest to an heir'). The key principle is that the status at the time the disposition becomes effective (death for bequest and gift) determines validity, whereas for acknowledgment, the status at the time of the statement determines validity because it is immediately binding.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a debt or right; it is a binding declaration that creates an obligation.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Death illness; a condition where death is imminent and legal transactions may be subject to additional rules to protect heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because at the time of death she is an heir, and there is no bequest to an heir
C) Because the marriage invalidates all previous transactions
D) Because the woman was a stranger at the time of bequest

Key Takeaway
Acknowledgment is binding at the time of statement; bequest and gift take effect at death, so if the recipient becomes an heir, they are void.

Hiba to a Slave or Mukatib During Death-Illness: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on hiba to a slave/mukatib during marad al-mawt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school invalidates a gift (hiba) to one's own slave during death-illness, and evaluate the two narrations on this issue.

Core Idea
A gift during death-illness is treated like a will; therefore, a gift to one's own slave or mukatib is void.

The rule that a gift during death-illness is akin to a will has significant implications. One such case is giving to one's own slave or mukatib, where the slave is considered an heir at the moment of death. In this lesson, we unpack the intra-Hanafi dispute that arises from two conflicting narrations: one upholding immediate ownership, the other subjecting it to will restrictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a gift (hiba) from a master to his own slave or mukatib during the master's death-illness (marad al-mawt). Determine the ruling according to the common narrations (عامۃ الروایات).
The common narrations rule that such a hiba is invalid (batil).
2
State the two narrations
There are two narrations within the Hanafi school: one holds the hiba valid because it is an immediate transfer of ownership; the other holds it invalid because it is like a will (wasiyyah).
The second narration is from the 'common narrations' and is preferred.
3
Analyze the dalil of each narration
The valid-narration argues that hiba is immediate (تملیک فی الحال) and at the time of the gift the slave is not an heir. The invalid-narration argues that during marad al-mawt, hiba is in the category of a will, and a will to an heir is impermissible.
The slave is considered an heir at death because he inherits? Actually, careful: a slave cannot inherit; but the text treats him as an heir for the purpose of will restrictions.
4
Determine the tarjih (preferred view)
The common narrations (عامۃ الروایات) are given preference over the isolated narration. Therefore, the mufta bihi position is that the hiba is invalid.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah supports the common narrations.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, such a hiba is void and the gifted property remains part of the estate, to be distributed among the heirs according to inheritance laws.
The same principle applies to gifts to a mukatib (a slave under contract of manumission).

Source Text

Now regarding a gift, there are two narrations: - It is permissible because a gift is an immediate transfer of ownership, and at the moment he is a slave who will not be an heir. This is also not correct because during death-illness it is in the category of a will, so just as the will is not valid, this will also not be valid.

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a gift (hiba) made by a slave owner to his own slave or to a mukatib (a slave under contract of manumission) during the owner's death-illness (marad al-mawt). The author first states the ruling from the common narrations (عامۃ الروایات) that such a gift is invalid because hiba during marad al-mawt is treated like a will (وصیت), and a will in favor of an heir is not permissible. At the time of death, the slave becomes an heir (since he is owned and cannot inherit, but after death he is freed? Actually careful: the slave is an heir? Actually slaves do not inherit. But the text says the slave is a heir? Context: The discuss is about a ghulam or mukatib who is a slave. In Hanafi law, a slave cannot inherit; but if the owner dies, the slave is inherited as property. So the reasoning: a will to an heir is invalid. The slave is considered an 'heir' in the sense that his ownership passes to the legal heirs? Wait, better to stick to the text: the commentary says 'at the time of death he is an heir' – this means the slave himself becomes an heir? The teacher should clarify that the dispute is about whether hiba during death-illness is treated as a will or as a valid immediate gift. The preferred view is that it is like a will, so restricted to one-third and subject to the same rules.

Key Terms
ہبہ (hibah): A gift, immediate transfer of ownership without compensation.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Death-illness, a disease that makes death likely, affecting legal capacity for gratuitous transfers.
وصیت (wasiyyah): A will, a bequest taking effect after death, limited to one-third of the estate.

Death-Illness for Chronic Conditions: Hiba Ruling
Clarification that chronic conditions without fear of death are not death-illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish chronic conditions from death-illness and apply the correct hiba ruling (all wealth vs. one-third) based on the criteria of fear of death and bedriddenness.

Core Idea
A chronic illness without fear of death does not restrict gifts – the person is treated as healthy.

This passage clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: not every ill person is in a state of marad al-mawt. Chronic conditions like being crippled (muq'ad) or hemiplegic (mafluj) that have persisted without imminent death are considered part of one's nature, not a death-illness. Therefore, gifts (hiba) during such states are valid from all wealth, just like a healthy person. Only when the condition worsens to bedriddenness and death is feared does the one-third limit apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the chronic conditions
List the four conditions mentioned: muq'ad (crippled), mafluj (hemiplegic), ashal (limp), maslul (tuberculosis). Note their common feature: they are long-term and the person does not fear death from them.
These are considered 'natural' due to their duration.
2
Apply the criterion of 'fear of death'
Determine if the illness causes fear of imminent death. If yes, it is marad al-mawt; if no, it is a chronic condition. The passage states that when these illnesses become prolonged without fear of death, they are not death-illness.
The key is the person's subjective fear and engagement in treatment.
3
Derive the hiba ruling for chronic cases
Since the person is considered like a healthy person, any gift (hiba) is valid from all his wealth, not restricted to one-third.
This is the default ruling for chronic conditions.
4
Identify the turning point: bedriddenness
If the chronic condition worsens to the point of bedriddenness (sahib al-firash) and death is feared, then it is treated as a new acute illness (marad al-mawt).
This changes the ruling.
5
Apply the new ruling for acute death-illness
If the person now gives a gift and dies within his days, the gift is limited to one-third of his wealth, like a will.
The one-third limit applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرض الموت کی وضاحت اور مقعد ، مفلوج، اشل مسلول کے ہبہ کا حکم
قال والمقعد والمفلوج والاشل والمسلول اذا تطاول ذلك ولم يخف منه الموت فهبته من جميع المال لانه اذا تقادم العهد صار طبعا من طباعه ولهذ لا يشتغل بالتداوى ولو صار صاحب فراش بعد ذلك فهو كمرض حادث
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور پانج اور فالج زدہ اور اشل (جسکے ہاتھ پاؤں شل ہو گئے ہوں ) اور مسلول (جس کو سل کا مرض ہو جس میں پھیپھڑے خراب ہو جاتے ہیں ) جب کہ یہ مرض لمبا ہو جائے اور اس سے موت کا خوف نہ رہے تو اس کا ہبہ پورے مال سے ہوگا اس لئے کہ جب عہد پرانا ہو گیا تو وہ اس کی طبیعتوں میں سے ایک طبیعت بن گئی اسی وجہ سے وہ دوا کرنے میں مشغول نہیں ہوتا اور اگر وہ اس کے بعد صاحب فراش ہو جائے تو وہ مرض جدید کے مثل ہو گا۔
تشریح جب بار بار مرض الموت کا ذکر آ رہا ہے تو یہاں سے مصنف اس کی وضاحت کرنا چاہتے ہیں، جس کا حاصل یہ کہ جس مرض سے ہلاکت کا خوف غالب ہو وہ مرض الموت ہے ورنہ نہیں چنا نچہ فرمایا کہ اگر کوئی شخص اپاہج ہو یعنی کھڑا ہونے کی قدرت نہیں رکھتا ، اور جس کو فالج ہو گیا ہو یا کوئی عضوشل ہو گیا ہو یا سل کی بیماری ہو ، اور یہ مرض اس کو زمانہ دراز تک رہے جس سے موت کا خوف نہ رہے تو یہ مرض الموت نہ ہوگا اور اگر وہ اس حالت میں ہبہ کرتا ہے تو اس کا ہبہ پورے مال سے ہوگا کیونکہ وہ
تندرست ہے۔
اس لئے کہ جب یہ بیماریاں طول اختیار کر جائیں تو وہ اس کی طبعی چیزیں بن جاتی ہیں اسی لئے آدمی ان کا علاج معالجہ بھی نہیں کرتا ۔
اور اگر وہ اس کے بعد صاحب فراش ہو جائے تو اس کو نیا مرض شمار کیا جاتا ہے۔
مرض الموت میں ہبہ کا حکم
وان وهب عند ما اصابه ذلك ومات من ايامه فهو من الثلث اذا صار صاحب فراش لانه يخاف منه الموت
ولهذا يتداوى فيكون مرض الموت والله اعلم

كتاب الوصايا
۱۶۴
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۹ ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے ہبہ کیا ان امراض کے لاحق ہونے کے وقت اور انھیں امراض میں مرگیا تو وہ ہبہ ایک تہائی سے معتبر ہوگا جب کہ وہ صاحب فراش ہو گیا ہو اس لئے کہ اس سے موت کا خوف ہوتا ہے اس وجہ سے وہ علاج معالجہ کرتا ہے تو وہ مرض الموت ہوگا ۔ واللہ اعلم تشریح اور اگر جب یہ امراض مذکورہ اس کو لاحق ہوئے اور وہ صاحب گیا ہو تو یہ مرض الموت ہوگا اور یہ ہبہ تہائی مال سے معتبر ہوگا اس لئے کہ اس سے موت کا خوف ہوتا ہے اسی وجہ سے انسان ایسی صورت میں علاج معالجہ میں مشغول ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس کو مرض الموت شمار کیا جائے گا۔
Clarification of death-illness and the ruling of hiba for the crippled, hemiplegic, one with a limp, and one with tuberculosis. He (Imam Muhammad) said: The crippled, the hemiplegic, the one with a limp, and the one with tuberculosis when this (illness) becomes prolonged and death is not feared from it, then his gift is from all his wealth. Because when the condition becomes old, it becomes a part of his nature, and therefore he does not engage in treatment. And if he becomes bedridden after that, then it is like a new illness. Translation: Muhammad said: ... (repeats). Commentary: Since the mention of death-illness is recurring, the author intends to clarify it. The gist is that the illness from which the fear of death predominates is death-illness, otherwise not. So he said: If a person is crippled (cannot stand), or hemiplegic, or has a limp, or has tuberculosis, and this illness persists for a long time without fear of death, then this is not death-illness. If he gives a gift in this state, his gift is from all his wealth because he is healthy. This is because when these illnesses become chronic, they become natural, so one does not even treat them. And if he becomes bedridden after that, it is considered a new illness. The ruling of hiba in death-illness: And if he gives a gift at the time of being afflicted with that and dies within his days, then it is from one-third when he becomes bedridden, because death is feared from it, and therefore he treats it, so it is death-illness. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage defines the legal concept of death-illness (marad al-mawt) in the Hanafi school, specifically addressing chronic conditions such as being crippled (muq’ad), hemiplegic (mafluj), having a limp (ashall), or suffering from tuberculosis (maslul). The key principle: marad al-mawt is not simply any illness but one where death is feared and the person is unable to attend to worldly affairs. Chronic conditions that persist for a long time without imminent death are considered part of the person's nature, not a death-illness. Therefore, gifts (hiba) made by such a person are valid from all their wealth, not limited to one-third. However, if the chronic condition suddenly worsens to the point of bedriddenness and death is feared, it becomes a new death-illness, and any gift then is treated like a will from one-third. The passage clarifies the criteria: fear of death and engagement in treatment indicate death-illness; chronic acceptance and lack of treatment indicate it is not. The ruling is drawn from Imam Muhammad's statement in the matn, and the commentary elaborates.

Key Terms
مقعد (muq'ad): A crippled person unable to stand or walk.
مفلوج (mafluj): A hemiplegic person, paralyzed on one side.
صاحب فراش (sahib al-firash): Bedridden, unable to leave the bed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does a gift from a person with tuberculosis (maslul) become limited to one-third?
A) If the tuberculosis has been chronic for years.
B) If the person becomes bedridden and death is feared.
C) If the person is receiving treatment.
D) If the gift is made at the onset of tuberculosis.

Key Takeaway
A chronic condition without fear of death does not restrict gifts to one-third; only acute death-illness (e.g., bedriddenness with fear) does.

Validity of Gratuitous Transfers in Death-Illness
Ruling on gratuitous transfers during death-illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that manumission, sale with favor (muhabah), and gifts during death-illness are valid but limited to one-third, and explain the reasoning based on heirs' rights.

Core Idea
Acts of gratuitous transfer during death-illness are valid but limited to one-third to protect heirs' rights.

This lesson examines a core Hanafi rule regarding acts of generosity during death-illness (marad al-mawt). The passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar clarifies that freeing a slave, selling below market value, or giving a gift are all legally valid, but their effect is restricted to one-third of the estate. This balance protects both the testator's autonomy and the heirs' entitlements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Acts
List the three acts mentioned in al-Quduri's text: manumission (itq), sale with favor (muhabah), and gift (hiba).
These are gratuitous transfers (tabarru'at) during death-illness.
2
State the Ruling
The text states that all these acts are 'valid' (ja'iz). Note the textual variant: some copies say 'so it is a will' (fahuwa wasiyyah).
The commentator says both mean the same: the act is considered from one-third.
3
Identify the Limitation
The ruling includes a limitation: the act is 'considered from one-third' (mu'tabar min al-thuluth) and the beneficiary shares with the legatees (ashab al-wasaya).
This means the total value of all gratuitous transfers cannot exceed one-third of the estate.
4
Understand the Reasoning
The reason is that during death-illness, the rights of heirs have attached to the property ('taluq haqq al-warathah'). Therefore, these acts are treated like wills to protect heirs, even though they are immediate (munajjaz) not deferred.
This is a key principle: death-illness restrictions apply to all gratuitous transfers.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Variant
Some copies of al-Quduri use 'valid' (ja'iz), others 'so it is a will' (fahuwa wasiyyah). The practical consequence is identical – the act is from one-third.
This shows the importance of textual transmission and the role of commentary in resolving ambiguities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بابُ العتق في مرض الموت
ترجمه مرض الموت میں آزاد کرنے کا باب
تشریح مرض الموت میں آزاد کرا وصیت کے درجہ میں ہے کیونکہ معتق ایسے زمانہ میں تبرع کر رہا ہے جب کہ اس کے مال کے ساتھ ورثا کا حق متعلق ہو گیا ہے، اس لئے اس کو کتاب الوصایا میں ذکر کیا گیا ہے لیکن صریح وصیت سے اس کو مؤخر بیان کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ صریح اصل ہے۔
مرض الموت میں غلام آزاد کرنے یا محابات کے ساتھ بیع کرنے اور ہبہ کرنے کا حکم
قال ومن اعتق في مرضه عبداً او باع و حابی او وهب فذلک کله جائز وهو معتبر من الثلث ويضرب به مع اصحاب الوصايا وفى بعض النسخ فهو وصية مكان قوله جائز والمراد الاعتبار من الثلث والضرب مع اصحاب الوصايا لا حقيقة الوصية ايجاب بعد الموت وهذا منجز غير مضاف واعتباره من الثلث لتعلق حق الورثة
ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے اپنے مرض الموت میں آزاد کیا یا بیچ کی اور اس میں محابات کی یا اس نے ہبہ کیا پس یہ سب جائز ہے اور یہ تہائی سے معتبر ہے اور وہ ثلث کے اندر اصحاب الوصایا کے ساتھ شریک ہوگا اور قدوری کے بعض نسخوں میں ہے، فہو دھیہ ، اس کے قول جانڑ کی جگہ پر اور مراد ثلث سے معتبر ہونا ہے اور اصحاب الوصایا کے ساتھ شریک ہونا ہے نہ کہ حقیقی وصیت اس لئے کہ وصیت ایسا ایجاب ہے جو کہ موت کے بعد ہے اور یہ اعتاق وغیرہ) منجر ہے جو موت کی جانب مضاف نہیں ہے اور اس کا اعتبار ثلث سے ہوتا ہے ورثا کا حق متعلق ہونے کی وجہ سے ۔ تشریح اولاً تو یہ بات واضح ہو کہ یہاں قدوری کے نسخے مختلف ہیں بعض نسخوں میں ہے، فذلک کلہ جائز اور بعض میں اس کے بجائے یوں ہے، فہو وصیة، ، اور دونوں باتوں کا قال ایک ہے۔ مرض الموت میں کسی نے اپنا غلام آزاد کیا یا اس نے بیع کی اور بیچ میں محابات کی مثلا دو ہزار کی چیز ہیں روپے میں فروخت کر دی ، یا اس نے یہ کیا تو یہ تمام صورتیں جائز ہیں (یہ بھی صحیح ہے اور اگر یوں کہا جائے کہ یہ تمام صورتیں وصیت ہیں یہ بھی جائز ہے )
Chapter of Manumission in Death-Illness. Translation: The chapter of freeing in death-illness. Commentary: Manumission in death-illness is in the category of a will because the manumitter is making a gratuitous transfer at a time when the right of the heirs has attached to his wealth. Therefore it is mentioned in the Book of Wills, but it is mentioned after explicit wills because the explicit is the origin. The ruling of freeing a slave, or selling with favor, or giving a gift in death-illness: He (al-Quduri) said: Whoever frees a slave during his death-illness, or sells with favor, or gives a gift, all that is valid, and it is considered from one-third, and he shares with the legatees. In some copies it is: 'so it is a will' instead of 'valid'. The meaning is consideration from one-third and sharing with legatees, not the reality of a will, because a will is a binding obligation after death, and this (manumission, etc.) is an immediate act not attributed to death. Its consideration from one-third is due to the attachment of the heirs' right. Commentary: First, it is clear that the copies of al-Quduri differ; in some copies it is 'all that is valid', and in others it is 'so it is a will'. But the ruling is the same: it is valid and from one-third. For example, if someone frees his slave, or sells an item worth 2000 for 1000 (favoring the buyer), or gives a gift, all these are valid (it is also correct to say they are like wills).
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter on manumission (itq) during death-illness. The author explains that acts like freeing a slave, selling with favor (muhabah), or giving a gift (hiba) during death-illness are all valid but have a special limitation: they are counted from one-third of the testator's estate and are shared among the beneficiaries of wills (as hab al-wasaya). The key point is that these acts are 'immediate' (munajjaz) and not 'attributed to death' (mudaf ila al-mawt) like a will, but because the rights of heirs have attached during death-illness, they are regulated similarly to wills. The passage also notes a textual variation in al-Quduri's work: some versions say 'all that is valid' while others say 'so it is a will'. The commentator clarifies that the practical effect is the same: validity from one-third. This reflects the Hanafi position that gratuitous transfers during death-illness are not void but are restricted to one-third to protect the heirs' rights.

Key Terms
محابات (muhabah): A sale with favor, where the seller sells below market value to benefit the buyer.
منجز (munajjaz): Immediate; an act taking effect in the present, not deferred to death.
اصحاب الوصایا (ashab al-wasaya): The beneficiaries of wills (or the legatees) who have claims up to one-third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Quduri, what is the status of a gift given during death-illness?
A) It is void because it harms the heirs.
B) It is valid without any limitation on amount.
C) It is valid but considered from one-third of the estate, and the donee shares with legatees.
D) It is only valid if it does not exceed one-half of the estate.

Key Takeaway
Gratuitous transfers during death-illness are valid but limited to one-third of the estate to balance the testator's generosity with the heirs' rights.

Marad al-Mawt: Definition and Effect on Hibah
Defining marad al-mawt and ruling on hibah during it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of marad al-mawt and explain why hibah during this state is limited to one-third of the estate.

Core Idea
Marad al-mawt is an illness causing fear of death; hibah in this state is treated like a bequest, valid only from one-third.

In this passage, the commentator defines the key legal concept of marad al-mawt (deathbed illness). Understanding this definition is crucial because it determines the validity and limits of voluntary dispositions like gifts (hibah) made by a terminally ill person. The ruling has significant implications for the rights of heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making a hibah during an illness that meets the criteria of marad al-mawt. The ruling: the hibah is valid but considered only from one-third of the estate, like a bequest.
The ruling applies only if the person dies from that illness.
2
Analyze the definition of marad al-mawt
Note the two elements: (1) the illness must cause fear of death, and (2) the person must seek medical treatment. Additionally, the person must be bedridden (sahib al-firash).
The definition is subjective – based on the patient's own fear and actions.
3
Understand the legal consequence
During marad al-mawt, the heirs' right to the estate attaches. Therefore, any voluntary disposition (like hibah) is treated as a bequest and limited to one-third.
This protects the heirs' inheritance rights.
4
Note the evidence and reasoning
The commentator reasons that because the person fears death and undertakes treatment, the illness is akin to a bequest situation. The ruling is derived from the general principle that deathbed gifts are restricted.
No specific Qur'an or hadith is cited in this passage; the reasoning is based on analogy (qiyas) to a wasiyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا
۱۶۴
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۹ ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے ہبہ کیا ان امراض کے لاحق ہونے کے وقت اور انھیں امراض میں مرگیا تو وہ ہبہ ایک تہائی سے معتبر ہوگا جب کہ وہ صاحب فراش ہو گیا ہو اس لئے کہ اس سے موت کا خوف ہوتا ہے اس وجہ سے وہ علاج معالجہ کرتا ہے تو وہ مرض الموت ہوگا ۔ واللہ اعلم تشریح اور اگر جب یہ امراض مذکورہ اس کو لاحق ہوئے اور وہ صاحب فراش ہو تو یہ مرض الموت ہوگا اور یہ ہبہ تہائی مال سے معتبر ہوگا اس لئے کہ اس سے موت کا خوف ہوتا ہے اسی وجہ سے انسان ایسی صورت میں علاج معالجہ میں مشغول ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس کو مرض الموت شمار کیا جائے گا۔
Book of Wills. 164. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, volume 19. Translation: And if he made a hibah at the time of the onset of these diseases and died from those diseases, then that hibah will be considered valid from one-third, provided he had become bedridden. Because it causes fear of death, and for that reason he undertakes medical treatment. So that will be marad al-mawt. And Allah knows best. Commentary: And if when these mentioned diseases afflict him and he is bedridden, then this is marad al-mawt, and this hibah will be considered from one-third of the wealth because it causes fear of death, and for that reason a person engages in medical treatment in such a situation. Therefore, it will be counted as marad al-mawt.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage defines the legal concept of marad al-mawt (deathbed illness). It states that when a person suffers from diseases that cause fear of death and he becomes bedridden, engaging in treatment, then that illness is considered marad al-mawt. In that state, any hibah (gift) he makes is valid only from one-third of his estate, just like a bequest. The key point is that the illness must be such that it naturally induces fear of death, evidenced by the person seeking medical care. The ruling is based on the principle that during marad al-mawt, the heirs' right to the estate becomes attached, so voluntary dispositions are limited to one-third.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A disease that causes fear of death and leads the person to seek medical treatment, while being bedridden.
ہبہ (hibah): A gift; transfer of ownership without exchange.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the person is confined to bed for more than three days.
B) When the disease causes fear of death and the person seeks medical treatment.
C) When the disease is incurable.
D) When the person makes a will.

Key Takeaway
Marad al-mawt is defined by subjective fear of death and objective treatment; hibah during it is limited to one-third of the estate.

Deathbed Transactions: Attached vs. Immediate Dispositions
General principle for deathbed transactions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between dispositions attached to death and immediate dispositions, and apply the one-third limitation rule taking into account the effect of recovery.

Core Idea
Attached to death = one-third always; immediate = depends on health; recovery resets the limitation.

In Hanafi fiqh, the rulings on a sick person's financial transactions depend on whether the disposition is tied to death (like a will) or executed immediately (like a gift). The key is the moment of attachment: if the disposition is conditioned on death, the one-third limit applies even if made in health. If immediate, only illness at the time matters. Recovery from illness retroactively treats the period as health, removing the limit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Read the passage and note the two types: dispositions attached to after death (mudaf ila ma ba'd al-mawt) and immediate dispositions (munajjaz). Examples: wasiyyah, tadbir vs. hibah, manumission.
Attachment (idafah) is a legal construct that changes the ruling.
2
State the ruling for attached dispositions
Any obligation made after death (e.g., a will) is from one-third, even if the person was healthy at the time of making the obligation. The ruling depends on the time of attachment, not the time of contract.
This is based on the principle: 'considering the state of attachment, not the state of the contract.'
3
State the ruling for immediate dispositions
For immediate dispositions, the ruling depends on the state at the time of contract. If healthy, it can be from the entire estate; if in marad al-mawt, it is limited to one-third.
This distinguishes from attached dispositions where health is irrelevant.
4
Apply the recovery rule
If the patient recovers from the illness, any limitation from that illness is removed. Recovery shows that no one had a right in his wealth.
Therefore, a will made during illness becomes unrestricted upon recovery, and an immediate hibah made during illness is no longer limited.
5
Test with examples from the text
Consider daman (guarantee) and kafala (surety) initiated in illness: they are treated like bequests (from one-third). Also, manumission attached to death (tadbir) is from one-third; immediate manumission depends on health at the time.
The text explicitly links daman and kafala to the bequest analogy.

Source Text

مریض کے مرض الموت کے تصرف کا حکم
وكذلك ما ابتداء المريض ايجابه على نفسه كا لضمان والكفالة فى حكم الوصية لا نه يتهم فيه كما في الهبة ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی ہر وہ تصرف کہ جس کی مریض نے اپنے نفس پر واجب کرنے کی ابتداء کی ہو جیسے منمان اور کفالت وصیت کے حکم میں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ اس میں مشکل ہبہ کے متہم ہے۔
تشریح اعماق وغیرہ کے مثل ہی مریض کا وہ تصرف ہے جس کو وہ اپنے نفس پر ابتدا ، واجب کرے جیسے کسی کا ضامن بن جائے یا کفیل بن جائے یہ بھی وصیت کے حکم میں ہے اس لئے کہ جیسے آدمی وصیت کے اندر متہم ہوتا ہے وہ تہمت یہاں بھی موجود ہے۔ متصرف کے ہر ایسے تصرف جس کی اضافت موت کے بعد سے متعلق کا کیا حکم
وكل ما أوجبه بعد الموت فهو من الثلث وان اوجبه في حال صحته اعتبار ابحال الاضافه دون حال العقد وما نفذه من التصرف فالمعتبر فيه حالة العقد فان كان صحيحا فهو من جميع المال وان كان مريضا فمن الثلث وكل مرض صح منه فهو كحال الصحة لان بالبرء تبين انه لا حق لا حد في ماله ترجمہ اور ہر ایسا عقد جس کا ایجاب مریض نے موت کے بعد کیا ہو تو وہ ثلث سے معتبر ہو گا اگر چہ اس نے اپنی صحت کی حالت میں اس کا ایجاب کیا ہو اضافت کی حالت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے نہ کہ عقد کی حالت کا، اور جس تصرف کو نا فذ کیا ہو تو اس میں عقد کی حالت معتبر ہے پس اگر وہ بوقت عقد صحیح ہو تو وہ پورے مال سے معتبر ہوگا اور اگر بوقت عقد مریض ہو تو تہائی سے معتبر ہوگا اور ہر وہ مرض جس سے مریض صحیح ہو گیا ہو تو وہ صحت کی حالت کے مثل ہے اس لئے کہ اچھا ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ بات واضح ہوگئی کہ اس کے مال میں کسی کا حق نہیں ہے۔
تشریح یہاں سے مصنف ایک قاعدہ کلیہ بیان فرماتے ہیں کہ متصرف نے جو تصرف ایسا کیا ہے جس کی اضافت موت کے بعد کی جانب کی ہو جیسے وصیت ہے اور تدبیر ہے وغیرہ وغیرہ تو وہ تصرف مال کی تہائی سے معتبر ہوگا وہ بوقت تصرف خواہ تندرست ہو یا مریض ہو کیونکہ اس صورت میں عقد کی حالت کا اعتبار نہیں ہے بلکہ اس میں اضافت کی حالت کا اعتبار ہے اور جس تصرف کو اس نے موت کی جانب مضاف نہیں کیا بلکہ اس کو بطور تجھیز کے کیا جیسے اعماق ہے ہبہ وغیرہ ، تو اس میں عقد کی حالت کا اعتبار ہے تو اگر وہ ایسے تصرف میں
Ruling on the disposition of the patient during marad al-mawt. Similarly, whatever obligation the patient initiates upon himself, such as daman (guarantee) and kafala (surety), is in the ruling of a bequest (wasiyyah) because he is suspected in it, as in hibah. Translation: And similarly, every disposition that the patient initiates as an obligation upon himself, like daman and kafala, is in the ruling of a bequest, because he is suspected in it, as in hibah. Commentary: Similar to manumission etc., the patient's disposition that he initially makes obligatory upon himself, such as becoming a guarantor (damin) for someone or a surety (kafil), this too is in the ruling of a bequest, because just as a person is suspected in a bequest, that suspicion exists here as well. Ruling on every disposition of the actor that is attached to after death. And every obligation he makes after death is from the third, even if he made it during health, considering the state of attachment, not the state of the contract. And whatever disposition he executes immediately, then the state of the contract is considered: if he was healthy at the time of the contract, it is from the entire wealth; if he was ill, it is from the third. And every illness from which the patient recovers is like the state of health, because by recovery it becomes clear that no one has any right in his wealth. Translation: And every contract whose obligation the patient makes after death, it is considered from the third, even if he made the obligation in a state of health, considering the state of attachment, not the state of the contract. And regarding the disposition that he executes (immediately), the state of the contract is considered: if he was healthy at the time of contract, it is from all the wealth; if he was ill, it is from the third. And every illness from which the patient recovers is like the state of health, because by recovery it becomes clear that no one has a right in his wealth. Commentary: From here, the author states a general principle: The disposition that the actor makes whose attachment is to after death, like a bequest (wasiyyah) and tadbir (manumission after death), etc., then that disposition will be considered from one-third of the wealth, whether at the time of disposition he was healthy or ill, because in this case the state of the contract is not considered; rather, the state of attachment is considered. And the disposition that he did not attach to death but executed immediately, like manumission, hibah, etc., in that the state of the contract is considered. So if in such a disposition...
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage sets out a general principle (qa'ida kulliyya) for distinguishing between different types of dispositions by a person who later becomes ill or dies. It covers two scenarios: 1) Obligations attached to after death (mudaf ila ma ba'd al-mawt) such as wills (wasiyyah) and tadbir: these are always from one-third, regardless of whether the person was healthy or ill at the time of making them, because the ruling depends on the time of attachment (death), not the time of the contract. 2) Immediate dispositions (munajjaz) such as manumission, hibah, and muhabah: here the state of the contract is what matters. If the person was healthy at the time of the contract, it is from the entire estate; if they were in marad al-mawt, it is from one-third. Additionally, if a person falls ill but then recovers, the illness is treated as a period of health regarding the limitation, because recovery shows that no one's right had actually attached. This principle ensures consistency in the Hanafi law of deathbed transactions, balancing the rights of heirs with the autonomy of the testator.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): A contract of guarantee; taking responsibility for a debt or liability of another.
کفالت (kafala): Surety; guaranteeing the presence or obligation of another person.
اضافت (idafah): Attachment of a disposition to a future event, specifically death in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person makes a will (wasiyyah) while healthy, but dies later, from what portion of the estate is the will enforced?
A) From the entire estate because they were healthy at the time.
B) From one-third because it is attached to death.
C) It is invalid because wills are only valid in illness.
D) From one-quarter as per the general rule.

Key Takeaway
The enforceability of a deathbed disposition hinges on whether it is attached to death (always one-third) or immediate (depends on health at contract, with recovery lifting limits).

Sick Person's Guarantee and Surety Treated Like a Will
States that a sick person's gratuitous obligations are treated like wasiyya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a sick person's voluntary guarantee or surety is treated like a will (limited to one-third of the estate) and explain the reasoning based on suspicion of favoritism.

Core Idea
A sick person's guarantee and surety are like a will – only binding from one-third due to suspicion of favoritism.

When a person in death-illness (marad al-mawt) voluntarily guarantees another's debt (daman) or becomes a surety (kafala), Islamic law treats this obligation like a will (wasiyya). This means the obligation can only be enforced against one-third of the estate, protecting the heirs from a potentially excessive deathbed favor. In this lesson, we explore why these acts are treated this way and how the ruling applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal treatment
The sick person initiates a guarantee or surety – a voluntary obligation for another. The passage states that this act is 'in the ruling of a will'.
The key phrase: 'فى حكم الوصية' – it is treated like a will.
2
Understand the underlying reason
The reason is suspicion (tuhma) that the sick person is favoring the beneficiary over the rightful heirs, similar to a gift or a will.
The text says 'because he is suspect in it as in a gift'.
3
Apply the one-third estate limit
Since it is like a will, the obligation can only be fulfilled from up to one-third of the deceased's estate. The heirs are not liable beyond that.
This is the default rule unless the heirs consent to execute more.
4
Note the scope
The ruling applies to all gratuitous obligations initiated by the sick person during marad al-mawt, not just guarantees and sureties, as indicated by the commentary.
The commentary mentions gifts to non-heirs (atmuq) as similar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك ما ابتداء المريض ايجابه على نفسه كالضمان والكفالة فى حكم الوصية لا نه يتهم فيه كما في الهبة
تشريح: اعماق وغيرہ کے مثل ہی مریض کا وہ تصرف ہے جس کو وہ اپنے نفس پر ابتدا واجب کرے جیسے کسی کا ضامن بن جائے یا کفیل بن جائے یہ بھی وصیت کے حکم میں ہے اس لئے کہ جیسے آدمی وصیت کے اندر متہم ہوتا ہے وہ تہمت یہاں بھی موجود ہے۔
And likewise, what the sick person initiates as an obligation upon himself, such as guarantee and surety, is in the ruling of a will, because he is suspect in it as in a gift. Commentary: Like 'atmuq (gift to non-heir) etc., it is the transaction of the sick person which he initiates as obligatory upon himself, such as becoming someone's guarantor or surety; this is also in the ruling of a will, because just as a person is suspect in a will, that suspicion is also present here.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage clarifies that when a person in death-illness (marad al-mawt) voluntarily takes on an obligation for another, such as becoming a guarantor (daman) or surety (kafala), this obligation is treated like a will (wasiyya). The reason is that the sick person is suspected of favoring the beneficiary to the detriment of the heirs, just as in a gift. Therefore, such obligations are only effective from one-third of the estate. This ruling is based on the principle that all gratuitous transactions by a death-ill person are subject to the one-third limit.

Key Terms
الضمان (al-daman): Guarantee: taking responsibility for another's debt or obligation.
الكفالة (al-kafala): Surety: guaranteeing the presence of a person or fulfillment of an obligation.
الوصية (al-wasiyya): Will: a disposition of property taking effect after death, limited to one-third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a sick person's guarantee (daman) treated like a will (wasiyya)?
A) Because the sick person is suspected of favoring the beneficiary over heirs.
B) Because guarantee is always a gift.
C) Because the sick person cannot make any obligations.
D) Because it is a condition of the contract.

Key Takeaway
A sick person's deathbed guarantee or surety is treated like a will and thus limited to one-third of the estate to protect heirs from potential favoritism.
