Post-Death vs Immediate Dispositions: The One-Third Rule
Explains distinction between idaafa and tanfidh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between dispositions added to after death (idaafa) and immediate executions (tanfidh), and apply the Hanafi rule for each regarding limitation to one-third of the estate.

Core Idea
Post-death dispositions always from 1/3; immediate ones depend on health at contract time.

The Hanafi school has a clear framework for how a person's transactions affect their estate after death. The key is whether the transaction is tied to death (like a will) or takes effect immediately (like a gift). This lesson unpacks the general rule from the Hidayah, showing how the timing of the obligation determines whether the transaction comes from the entire wealth or only one-third. We also see how recovery from illness changes the legal picture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Label each transaction as either 'added to after death' (idaafa) or 'immediate execution' (tanfidh). The rule for each is different.
Examples of idaafa: wasiyya (will), tadbir (promise of freedom after death). Examples of tanfidh: immediate gift, freeing a slave now.
2
Apply the rule to idaafa
For idaafa, the ruling is always from one-third, no matter when the person made the contract. The critical moment is death, not the contract time.
Even if the person was healthy when writing the will, it still comes from one-third.
3
Apply the rule to tanfidh
For tanfidh, consider the person's health at the moment of the contract. If healthy, it comes from all wealth; if sick (marad al-mawt), it comes from one-third.
The sickness here is the death-illness that usually leads to death.
4
Account for recovery
If the person recovers from the illness, any transactions made during that illness are treated as if they were made in health. Recovery shows no right of heirs had attached.
This is because the right of heirs only becomes effective at death; recovery cancels that right retroactively.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل ما أوجبه بعد الموت فهو من الثلث وان اوجبه في حال صحته اعتبارا بحال الاضافه دون حال العقد وما نفذه من التصرف فالمعتبر فيه حالة العقد فان كان صحيحا فهو من جميع المال وان كان مريضا فمن الثلث وكل مرض صح منه فهو كحال الصحة لان بالبرء تبين انه لا حق لا حد في ماله
تشريح: يہاں سے مصنف ایک قاعدہ کلیہ بیان فرماتے ہیں کہ متصرف نے جو تصرف ایسا کیا ہے جس کی اضافت موت کے بعد کی جانب کی ہو جیسے وصیت ہے اور تدبیر ہے وغیرہ وغیرہ تو وہ تصرف مال کی تہائی سے معتبر ہوگا وہ بوقت تصرف خواہ تندرست ہو یا مریض ہو کیونکہ اس صورت میں عقد کی حالت کا اعتبار نہیں ہے بلکہ اس میں اضافت کی حالت کا اعتبار ہے اور جس تصرف کو اس نے موت کی جانب مضاف نہیں کیا بلکہ اس کو بطور تجھیز کے کیا جیسے اعماق ہے ہبہ وغیرہ تو اس میں عقد کی حالت کا اعتبار ہے تو اگر وہ ایسے تصرف میں بوقت عقد تندرست ہو تو وہ پورے مال سے معتبر ہوگا اور اگر بوقت عقد مریض ہو تو تہائی مال سے معتبر ہوگا۔ حضرت مصنف آگے ایک قاعدہ اور بیان فرماتے ہیں کہ جس مرض سے مریض شفایاب ہو گیا ہو تو وہ مرض نہیں رہا بلکہ وہ صحت کے مثل ہے، کیونکہ جب مریض اچھا ہو گیا تو اس سے یہ بات معلوم ہو گئی کہ اس کے مال کے ساتھ کسی کا حق وابستہ نہیں ہوا ہے۔
And everything that he makes obligatory after death is from the third, even if he made it obligatory during his health, considering the state of addition (to after death) not the state of the contract. And whatever disposition he executes, the consideration is the state of the contract. So if he was healthy at the time of contract, it is from all the wealth; if he was sick, then from the third. And every illness from which he recovers is like the state of health, because by recovery it becomes clear that no one has a right in his wealth.
Commentary: From here the author states a general rule: The transaction that the doer performed such that its addition is to after death—like wasiyya and tadbir etc.—then that transaction is considered from one-third of the wealth, whether at the time of transaction he was healthy or sick, because in this case the state of the contract is not considered, rather the state of addition is considered. And a transaction that he did not add to death but performed as an immediate execution—like 'atmuq, gift, etc.—then in that the state of the contract is considered. So if at the time of contract he was healthy, it is from the entire wealth; if at the time of contract he was sick, then from one-third. And the author further states a rule: any illness from which the patient recovers is like health, because by recovery it becomes clear that no right of anyone has attached to his wealth.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage lays down two foundational principles for transactions of a sick person. First, for dispositions that are conditioned upon death (like wills, tadbir, etc.), the effective moment is the addition to after death, not the time of making the contract. Therefore, even if the person was healthy when he made the will, it still comes from one-third of the estate because it only takes effect after death. Second, for dispositions executed immediately—like gifts or manumissions that take effect during lifetime—the validity depends on the person's health at the time of the contract. If he is healthy, the transaction is valid from the entire wealth; if he is in death-illness, it is limited to one-third. Additionally, if a person recovers from his illness, any transactions made during that illness are retrospectively treated as if made in health, because recovery shows that no right of heirs had attached to the wealth.

Key Terms
الاضافة (al-idaafah): Attribution or addition of a contract to a future time (after death).
التنفيذ (al-tanfidh): Execution; a contract that takes immediate effect.
البرء (al-buru'): Recovery from death-illness, which retrospectively cancels the limitation to one-third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man in marad al-mawt makes an immediate gift of a car to his brother. He then recovers fully and later dies from a different illness. From which part of his estate is the car taken?
A) From one-third, because it was made during marad al-mawt.
B) From the entire estate, because recovery retroactively treats it as a healthy person's gift.
C) From one-half, because it's a gift to a non-heir.
D) It is invalid because he was sick.

Key Takeaway
The key distinction: if a disposition is added to after death (idaafa), it always comes from one-third; if executed immediately (tanfidh), the health at contract time determines the limit, but recovery cancels the limitation.

Priority Between Mu'jabat and Itq: The Sequence Rule
Intra-Hanafi dispute on priority when one-third is insufficient

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on the priority between mu'jabat and itq when the one-third is insufficient, and apply the mufta bihi ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
When mu'jabat and itq conflict in death-illness, Imam Abu Hanifa considers sequence; the Sahibayn always prefer itq.

In death-illness, all wills are equal except three privileged transactions: itq (emancipation), tadbir, and mu'jabat (underpriced sale). These are executed before other wills. But what happens when two privileged transactions conflict and the one-third cannot cover both? This lesson resolves the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the priority between mu'jabat and itq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the privileged transactions
Recognize that itq, tadbir, and mu'jabat are given priority over ordinary wills in death-illness. The dispute concerns only mu'jabat and itq; tadbir is not part of this specific conflict.
Mu'jabat is a sale at below market price; the undervalue is treated as a gift from the one-third.
2
State the default rule for wills
All ordinary wills share the one-third proportionally. The privileged transactions, however, are executed first from the one-third before any other will.
3
Explain the scenario triggering the dispute
A sick person makes both a mu'jabat and an itq during death-illness, but the one-third is insufficient to cover both fully. The question: which gets priority?
The passage assumes both transactions are valid and limited to the one-third.
4
Articulate the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that itq (emancipation) is always preferred over mu'jabat, regardless of the order in which they were performed.
Their reasoning: emancipation is a pure act of worship without material exchange, giving it a stronger religious value.
5
Articulate Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes based on sequence: if mu'jabat was done first, it is preferred; if itq was done first, both share equally.
For Abu Hanifa, the earlier transaction is more deserving because the sick person committed to it first, but if itq precedes, both are equally privileged and the one-third is divided proportionally.
6
Identify the mufta bihi and reason
The later Hanafi school relies on Imam Abu Hanifa's view as it respects the order of actions and gives effect to both transactions.
This is recorded in the Zahir al-Riwayah and affirmed by later commentators like al-Marghinani.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وان حابي ثم اعتق وضاق الثلث عنهما فالمحاباة اولى عند ابي حنيفة وان اعتق ثم حابى فهما سواء وقالا العتق اولى في المسألتين
ترجمہ: قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر مریض نے محابات کی پھر آزاد کیا اور ثلث ان دونوں سے تنگ ہو گیا تو ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک محابات اولی ہے اور اگر اس نے آزاد کیا پھر محابات کی تو وہ دونوں برابر ہیں اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ دونوں مسئلوں میں عتق اولی ہے۔
تشريح: مرض الموت کی تمام وصایا برابر ہوتی ہیں ایک کو دوسرے پر فضیلت نہیں ہوتی لہذا تمام اصحاب الوصايا ثلث میں برابر کے شریک ہوتے ہیں یعنی اپنے اپنے حصہ کے بقد رثلث میں سب شریک ہوتے ہیں البتہ تین چیزیں ایسی ہیں جو تمام وصیتوں سے مقدم ہوتی ہیں: 1- مرض الموت کا عتق 2- مرض الموت کی تدبیر 3- مرض الموت کی محابات یہ تین چیزیں دیگر وصایا سے مقدم ہوتی ہیں لہذا اگر ان تینوں میں سے کسی کے ساتھ دیگر وصایا جمع ہو جائیں تو ثلث کے اندر سے پہلے ان کو پورا کیا جائے گا اور اگر ان کو ادا کر کے ثلث میں کچھ بچ جائے تو دیگر اصحاب اوصایا کو ملے گا ورنہ کچھ نہیں ملے گا۔ لیکن اگر محابات اور عتق جمع ہو جائیں تو اب کون متقدم ہوگا تو اس میں صاحبین اور امام ابوحنیفہ کا اختلاف ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ عتق ہر حال میں محابات سے اولی ہے، اور امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر پہلے مریض نے محابات کی ہو اور اس کے بعد آزاد کیا ہو تو اس صورت میں تو محابات عتق سے اولی ہے اور اگر اس نے پہلے آزاد کیا ہو اور پھر اس نے محابات کی ہو تو دونوں برابر ہیں، برابر ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ثلث میں دونوں برابر کے شریک ہوں گے۔ اور محابات کے مقدم ہونے کا یہ مطلب یہ ہے کہ ثلث کے اندر پہلے محابات کو جاری کیا جائے گا اگر کچھ بچ جائے تو مابقی میں عتق نافذ ہوگا ورنہ نہیں، اور عتق کے مقدم ہونے کا یہ مطلب ہے کہ ثلث سے پہلے عتق کو نافذ کریں گے اگر کچھ بچ جائے تو مابقی میں محابات کو جاری کریں گے ورنہ نہیں۔
He (al-Quduri) said: And if a sick person made a mu'jabat (underpriced sale) then emancipated, and the one-third is insufficient for both, then according to Abu Hanifa the mu'jabat has priority. And if he emancipated then made a mu'jabat, then the two are equal. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Emancipation has priority in both cases.
Commentary: All wills in death-illness are equal, no priority over each other. However, three things have priority over all other wills: 1) emancipation (itq) in death-illness, 2) tadbir (suspensive emancipation on death), 3) mu'jabat (underpriced sale) in death-illness. If any of these three are combined with other wills, they are fulfilled first from the one-third. If something remains after them, other will beneficiaries receive, otherwise nothing. But if mu'jabat and itq are combined, then there is a disagreement between the Two (Sahibayn) and Imam Abu Hanifa. The Two said: Emancipation is always preferred over mu'jabat. Imam Abu Hanifa said: If the sick person first made a mu'jabat and then emancipated, then mu'jabat is preferred over emancipation; if he first emancipated and then made a mu'jabat, then the two are equal. Equal means they share the one-third equally. Priority of mu'jabat means: first the mu'jabat is executed from the one-third; if something remains, then emancipation is executed, otherwise not. Priority of emancipation means: first emancipation is executed from the one-third; if something remains, then mu'jabat is executed, otherwise not.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific intra-Hanafi dispute regarding priority when a sick person makes both a mu'jabat (a sale at undervalue, effectively a gift-like transaction) and an emancipation (itq) within death-illness (marad al-mawt), and the one-third of the estate cannot cover both. The text first establishes that in general, all wills share equally in the one-third except for three privileged categories: itq (emancipation), tadbir (suspensive emancipation), and mu'jabat. These three are executed before other wills. However, when these three conflict among themselves, a hierarchy arises. The dispute is between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The Two hold that emancipation (itq) always takes precedence over mu'jabat, regardless of order. Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes based on the order: if the mu'jabat was done first, it is preferred; if emancipation was done first, they share equally. The practical consequence is reflected in how the one-third is allocated: if mu'jabat is preferred, the mu'jabat's value is taken first; if itq is preferred, the emancipation value is taken first. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the later Hanafi school is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, as it gives effect to the sequence of transactions while protecting the right of emancipation as an act of devotion.

Key Terms
المحاباة (al-muhaabah): A sale at an undervalue (less than market price) during death-illness, treated as a gift of the difference.
العتق (al-itq): Emancipation of a slave, if done in death-illness, is limited to one-third and has priority over non-privileged wills.
التدبير (al-tadbir): A suspensive emancipation conditioned on the master's death; treated like a will and privileged.
أولى (awlaa): Preferable; having priority for execution from the one-third estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position, if a sick person first emancipates a slave (itq) and then makes a mu'jabat (underpriced sale), and the one-third is insufficient for both, how are the one-third proceeds distributed?
A) Emancipation gets full priority, mu'jabat gets nothing.
B) Mu'jabat gets full priority, emancipation gets nothing.
C) They share the one-third equally.
D) Neither is valid.

Key Takeaway
When both mu'jabat and itq are made in death-illness and the one-third is insufficient, the mufta bihi position (Imam Abu Hanifa) gives priority to the earlier transaction; if simultaneous, they share equally.

General Rule for Multiple Bequests Within One-Third and Three Exceptions
General rule for multiple bequests with three exceptions and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi general rule for distributing multiple bequests within the one-third, identify the three exceptions, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding precedence of emancipation and muḥābāh.

Core Idea
All bequests within one-third share equally, but emancipation and muḥābāh in death-illness take priority because they are irrevocable.

This passage from Sharh al-Hidayah presents a foundational general principle (qāʿidah kulliyyah) in the law of wills. Most bequests that fit within the one-third are treated equally and proportionally. However, three specific types of dispositions are stronger and override others. Understanding this rule and its exceptions, as well as the scholarly difference within the Hanafi school on their mutual precedence, is essential for correctly distributing an estate when multiple bequests are present.

Guided Path
1
Understand the General Rule of Proportional Equality
Learn that when multiple bequests are made and none individually exceeds one-third, all beneficiaries share the one-third pool proportionally. No single bequest is given priority. The text illustrates with an example: estate 12,000, bequests total 8,000 within 4,000 third, each gets half of their bequest.
This applies only if each bequest is within one-third individually.
2
Identify the Three Exceptions
Memorize the three exceptions: (1) unconditional emancipation (ʿitq) during death-illness, (2) valid tadbīr (emancipation conditioned on death), and (3) muḥābāh (preferential sale) during death-illness. These are given priority over regular bequests.
Invalid tadbīr (e.g., 'one month after death') is not an exception.
3
Analyze Why Exceptions Are Stronger (Irrevocability)
The text explains that these three are 'stronger' (aqwā) because they cannot be rescinded (faskh) by the testator. Other bequests can be revoked. Muḥābāh cannot be rescinded by the testator but can be rescinded by the buyer, which becomes the point of dispute.
Strength is measured by immunity from rescission by the testator.
4
Examine the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Precedence Between Emancipation and Muḥābāh
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if muḥābāh was executed first, it takes precedence over emancipation; if emancipation was first, they are equal. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that emancipation always takes precedence because it cannot be rescinded by anyone, while muḥābāh can be rescinded by the buyer.
The dispute hinges on who can rescind (testator only vs. buyer also).
5
Apply the Rule to a Scenario
Given a death-illness scenario with multiple bequests and one of the exceptions, work out the distribution: first allocate to the exception(s), then proportionally share the remainder among regular bequests. If the exceptions exceed the third, regular bequests get nothing.
Use the example from the text or create your own.

جیسے مدبر بنا دینا، کہ مدبر کی آزادی موصی کی موت پر ہوگی اور تدبیر کو صحیح کی قید سے اس لئے مقدم کیا تا کہ تدبیر فاسد سے احتراز ہو جائے جیسے اگر موصی نے یوں کہا کہ یہ غلام میری موت سے ایک ماہ بعد آزاد المحاباة لا يلحقه الفسخ من جهة الموصى واذا قدم ذلك فما بقى من الثلث بعد ذلك يستوى فيه من سواهما من اهل الوصايا ولا تقدم البعض على البعض ترجمہ اور وہ عتق مقدم کیا گیا ہے جس کو ہم نے ابھی ذکر کیا ہے اس لئے کہ وہ اقویٰ ہے اس لئے کہ اس کو موصی کی جانب سے فسخ لاحق نہیں ہوسکتا اور اس کے غیر کو فسخ لاحق ہو جاتا ہے اور ایسے ہی محابات اس کو موصی کی جانب سے فسخ لاحق نہیں ہوتا اور جب کہ ان کو (عتق و محابات ) مقدم کیا گیا ہے پس ان کے بعد ثلث میں سے جو باقی بچے اس میں وہ لوگ شریک ہوں گے جو اہل وصایا میں سے ان دونوں کے علاوہ ہیں اور بعض کو بعض پر مقدم نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح اب یہاں سے مصنف یہ بیان کرتے ہیں کہ ان تینوں چیزوں کو باقی وصایا پر کیوں مقدم کیا جاتا ہے تو فرماتے ہیں کہ معتق کو مقدم کرنے کی وجہ تو یہ ہے کہ حق اقویٰ ہے جس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بعد عتق اگر موصی عتق کو فسخ کرنا چاہے تو فسخ نہیں کر سکتا اور عتق کے علاوہ جو دیگر وصایا ہیں ان کو فسخ لاحق ہوتا ہے یعنی اگر موصی ان وصایا سے رجوع کرلے تو رجوع صحیح ہے، اور تدبیر صحیح بھی عتق کے اندر ہی داخل ہوگئی ہے۔ اب رہی محابات تو وہ بھی دیگر وصایا سے اقویٰ ہے کیونکہ اگر موصی خود یہ چاہے کہ بیع کے اندر محابات کو فسخ کروں تو نہیں کر سکتا، بہر حال عتق و محابات دیگر وصایا سے مقدم ہیں، تو اگر ان سے ثلث کا کچھ حصہ بچ رہا تو اس مابقی میں تمام اصحاب الوصایا برابر کے شریک ہوں گے اور کسی کو کسی پر ترجیح نہیں دی جائے گی۔ صاحبین کی دلیل لهما في الخلافية ان العتق اقوى لانه لا يلحقه الفسخ والمحاباة يلحقها ولا معتبر بالتقديم في الذكر لانه لا يوجب التقدم في الثبوت ترجمہ اختلافی مسئلہ میں صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عتق اقویٰ ہے اس لئے کہ عتق کو فسخ لاحق نہیں ہوسکتا اور محابات کو فسخ لاحق ہوسکتا ہے اور ذکر میں تقدیم کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہ ( تقدیم فی الذکر ) ثبوت کے اندر قدم کو واجب نہیں کرتا۔ تشریح یہاں سے مصنف متن کے مسئلہ اختلافیہ پر فریقین کے دلائل بیان فرماتے ہیں ، صاحبین کے نزدیک عتق مقدم ہوتا ہے اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اگر محابات مقدم ہو تو محابات عتق سے مقدم ہوتی ہے اور اگر عتق مقدم ہو تو دونوں برابر ہوتے ہیں۔ تو صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ عتق محابات سے اقویٰ ہے، کیسے؟ اس لئے کہ عتق فسخ نہیں ہوسکتا اور محابات فسخ ہو سکتی ہے، یعنی معتق چاہے کہ عتق کو فسخ کر دوں تو نہیں کر سکتا اور اگر غلام چاہے کہ عتق کو فسخ کر دوں تو نہیں کر سکتا اور محابات اگر چہ موصی کی جانب سے فسخ کو قبول نہیں کر سکتی لیکن مشتری کی جانب سے فسخ کو قبول کر سکتی ہے۔
Translation and the general principle in this is that in wills, when no will exceeds one-third, each of the will-holders will share in the third with all of their will. One will not be given precedence over another, except for the emancipation which is executed in death-illness, and if that emancipation which is suspended upon the testator's death, like a valid tadbir, and a preferential sale (muḥābāh) in a sale when the muḥābāh occurs in death-illness, because all wills are equal and their equality in entitlement necessitates equality in the entitlement itself. Explanation: Here the author of al-Hidayah departs from the original issue and presents a general principle of this chapter: he says that when many wills are gathered and none of them individually exceeds one-third, then all the will-holders will share equally, and no one will have superiority over another. For example: Zaid's total estate is twelve thousand rupees, one-third of which is four thousand rupees. Zaid made a will of one thousand for Amr, two thousand for Bakr, three thousand for Khalid, and two thousand for Sajid, the total of which is eight thousand, but individually no will exceeds one-third. Therefore all wills are valid and they will all share in the third, but proportionally. So each will receive half of his bequest, the total being four thousand, which is one-third of the total estate. Thus Amr gets five hundred, Bakr one thousand, Khalid one thousand five hundred, and Sajid one thousand rupees, and their total is four thousand. In summary, no one has superiority over another. But three things are exempt from this general principle: if any of these are combined with other wills, then those other wills are suppressed before them. In the third, first whatever of these three is present will be executed; if something remains, then the other will-holders will share proportionally; and if nothing remains, there will be nothing for the will-holders. And those three things are: (1) Emancipating a slave unconditionally (tanjīzan) in death-illness. (2) An emancipation that is suspended upon the testator's death, such as making a mudabbar; the mudabbar's freedom occurs upon the testator's death. It is conditioned as a valid tadbir to avoid invalid tadbir. For example, if the testator says, 'This slave is free one month after my death,' this is not a valid tadbir, so it will not be given precedence over other will-holders; rather it will share with them. But if it is a valid tadbir, like the testator says, 'This slave is free upon my death,' then this emancipation is given precedence over other will-holders. (3) A preferential sale (muḥābāh) in a sale when the muḥābāh occurs in death-illness. In any case, these three things are independent. Apart from them, all other wills are such that none has superiority over another; rather they are all equal. And when the cause of entitlement is equal, then the entitlement itself is equal. And the emancipation which we mentioned previously is given precedence because it is stronger: because it cannot be rescinded by the testator, while others can be rescinded. Similarly, muḥābāh cannot be rescinded by the testator. And when these (emancipation and muḥābāh) are given precedence, then after them, whatever remains of the third, those other than these two among the will-holders will share equally, and one will not be given precedence over another. Explanation: Here the author explains why these three things are given precedence over other wills. He says that the reason for giving precedence to the emancipation is that the right is stronger. The proof is that after emancipation, if the testator wants to rescind the emancipation, he cannot do so; but other wills can be rescinded, meaning if the testator revokes those wills, the revocation is valid. And valid tadbir is included within emancipation. As for muḥābāh, it too is stronger than other wills because if the testator himself wants to rescind the muḥābāh in the sale, he cannot. In any case, emancipation and muḥābāh are given precedence over other wills. Then if some part of the third remains after them, all will-holders share equally in what remains, and no one is given preference over another. The proof of the Two Companions (Sahibayn): In the disputed issue, the proof of the Two Companions is that emancipation is stronger because it cannot be rescinded, while muḥābāh can be rescinded, and precedence in mention is not considered because it does not necessitate precedence in existence. Explanation: Here the author presents the proofs of the two parties on the disputed issue. According to the Two Companions, emancipation is given precedence; according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if muḥābāh is made first, it takes precedence over emancipation, and if emancipation is made first, they are equal. The Two Companions say: emancipation is stronger than muḥābāh. How? Because emancipation cannot be rescinded, while muḥābāh can be rescinded. That is, the emancipator cannot rescind the emancipation, and the slave cannot rescind it either. As for muḥābāh, although it cannot accept rescission from the testator's side, it can accept rescission from the buyer's side.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage from Sharh al-Hidayah (Ashraf al-Hidayah) presents a general principle (qāʿidah kulliyyah) in the book of wills (kitāb al-waṣāyā). The passage begins by stating that when multiple bequests (waṣāyā) are made and none individually exceeds one-third of the estate, all beneficiaries share equally in the one-third pool. No beneficiary is given priority over another. The author provides a numerical example to illustrate: if the total estate is 12,000 and each bequest is within the 4,000 third, each recipient gets a proportional share. The general principle has three exceptions: (1) emancipation of a slave unconditionally (tanjīzan) during death-illness; (2) a valid tadbīr (emancipation suspended upon death); and (3) a preferential sale (muḥābāh) occurring in death-illness. These three are given precedence over other bequests. The reason given is that these three are 'stronger' (aqwā) because they cannot be rescinded (faskh) by the testator, whereas other bequests can be revoked. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Two Companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The Two Companions argue that emancipation is always stronger than muḥābāh because emancipation cannot be rescinded by either party, while muḥābāh can be rescinded by the buyer. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if muḥābāh is made first, it takes precedence over emancipation; if emancipation is made first, they are equal. The passage explains that the strength of emancipation lies in its irrevocability, while muḥābāh is also irrevocable from the testator's side but revocable from the buyer's side. The commentary emphasizes that the dispute does not affect the general rule of equal sharing among other bequests after these exceptions are satisfied.

Key Terms
وصیة (wasiyya): A bequest or will made by a person regarding his property after death.
ثلث (thulth): One-third of the testator's estate, the maximum that can be bequeathed freely.
عتق (ʿitq): Emancipation of a slave, here specifically executed in death-illness (marad al-mawt).
تدبیر (tadbīr): A declaration that a slave will be free upon the master's death.
محابات (muḥābāh): A sale where the seller gives a discount or favorable price; here occurring in death-illness and treated as a bequest of the difference.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of a transaction or legal act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the three exceptions to the general rule that bequests share equally within the one-third?
A) Emancipation in death-illness
B) Valid tadbir
C) Muḥābāh in death-illness
D) A bequest to a relative

Key Takeaway
Emancipation and muḥābāh in death-illness take priority over ordinary bequests because they are irrevocable, but their mutual precedence is disputed among Hanafi jurists.

Relative Precedence of 'Itq and Muhabah in Terminal Illness
Intra-Hanafi dispute on precedence of 'itq and muhabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the relative precedence of 'itq (emancipation) and muhabah (sale at undervalue) in terminal illness, and apply the ruling based on the order of occurrence.

Core Idea
In terminal illness, muhabah (sale at undervalue) is stronger according to Imam due to its contractual nature, while 'itq is stronger according to Sahibayn due to its irrescindability.

When a terminally ill person makes both a bequest of emancipation and a sale at an undervalue, a conflict arises over which takes priority from the one-third of the estate. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Imam Abu Hanifa argues that muhabah, being embedded in a commutative contract, is stronger; his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, argue that 'itq, which cannot be rescinded by anyone, is stronger. This lesson examines the proofs of both sides and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two dispositions and why they are preferred over other bequests
Recognize that both 'itq and muhabah are stronger than other wills because they cannot be rescinded by the testator. They are given first priority from the one-third of the estate.
2
Understand the Sahibayn's proof that 'itq is stronger
The Sahibayn argue that 'itq is stronger because it can never be rescinded by anyone (neither testator nor slave), whereas muhabah can be rescinded by the buyer (e.g., if the buyer fails to pay the remaining fair price). They also dismiss precedence by mere mention.
Key concept: irrescindability (la yalhaqu al-faskh)
3
Understand Imam Abu Hanifa's proof that muhabah is stronger
Imam argues that muhabah is established within a commutative contract (bay'), making it a gift only in meaning (ma'nan) but not in form. A commutative contract is inherently stronger than a pure gift. Therefore, muhabah, despite potential rescission from the buyer's side, is stronger as a disposition from the testator.
Key concept: contractual strength vs. pure gift
4
Apply the rule based on order of occurrence
If muhabah occurs first, according to Imam it repels 'itq entirely; according to Sahibayn, 'itq always wins regardless of order. If 'itq occurs first, Imam says they compete equally, while Sahibayn still give 'itq full priority.
Practical consequence: thamarah al-khilaf

ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ محابات اقومی ہے اس لئے کہ محابات عقد معاوضہ کے ضمن میں ثابت ہوتی ہے تو محابات تبرع ہوگا اپنے معنی کے اعتبار سے نہ کہ اپنے صیغہ کے اعتبار سے اور اعتاق تبرع ہے صیغہ اور معنی کے اعتبار سے پس جب کہ اولاً محابات پائی گئی تو محابات اضعف ( عتق ) کو دور کر دے گا اور جب کہ پہلے عشق پایا گیا اور معتق ثابت ہو گیا اور وہ محابات کو دور کرنے کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا تو اس کی ضروریات میں سے مزاحمت ہے۔ تشریح یہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ محابات عنق سے مقدم ہے اس لئے کہ محابات عقد بیچ کے ضمن میں ثابت ہوتی ہے جس کو مصنف نے عقد معاوضہ سے تعبیر کیا ہے تو محابات اپنے صیغہ اور الفاظ کے اعتبار سے تبرع نہیں ہے بلکہ الفاظ کے اعتبار سے یہ عقد بیع ہے البتہ معنی کے اعتبار سے یہ تبرع ہے اور اعتاق لفظ اور معنی ہر اعتبار سے تبرع ہے تو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ محابات اقومی ہے کیونکہ عقد معاوضہ خالص تبرع سے اقوئی ہوا کرتا ہے۔ تو جب اقولی یعنی محابات پہلے سے ہوگی اور وہاں اضعف یعنی عشق جانا چاہے گا تو اقوئی اس کو دھکا دے کر دور کر دے گا اور جب محابات کے سامنے اس کا پنجہ بھی نہیں سکے گا تو ثبوت کہاں سے ہو گا۔ اور اگر پہلے عشق پایا جائے اور بعد میں محابات پائی جائے تو عشق چونکہ اضعف ہے اس وجہ سے عتق محابات کو دھکیل نہیں سکتا لہذا ان دونوں کے درمیان مزاحمت ثابت ہوگئی اور جب دونوں کے درمیان مزاحمت ثابت ہوگئی تو نا چار کہنا پڑے گا کہ دونوں مساوی
Book of Wills. And only the emancipation which we mentioned earlier is given precedence because it is stronger; for rescission does not affect it from the testator's side, while it affects others. Similarly, muhabah (sale at undervalue) is not affected by rescission from the testator's side. When that is given precedence, then whatever remains of the one-third after that, all other recipients of wills (other than these two) share equally, and one is not given precedence over another. Translation: And that 'itq (emancipation) which we have just mentioned is given precedence because it is stronger, because rescission from the testator cannot affect it, while rescission does affect other than it. Similarly, muhabah is not affected by rescission from the testator. And when these two (i'tq and muhabah) are given precedence, then whatever remains of the one-third after them, all those who are recipients of wills other than those two will share in it equally, and some will not be given precedence over others. Commentary: Here the author explains why these three things are given precedence over other wills... (continues). The proof of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): For them in the controversial matter: 'itq is stronger because rescission does not affect it, while rescission does affect muhabah. And no consideration is given to precedence in mention, because it does not necessitate precedence in established reality. Translation: In the controversial matter, the proof of the two companions is that 'itq is stronger because 'itq cannot be affected by rescission, while muhabah can be affected by rescission. And precedence in mention is not considered, because it does not necessitate precedence in established reality. Commentary: Here the author presents the proofs of the two parties on the controversial issue... (continues). The proof of Imam Abu Hanifah: And his proof is that muhabah is stronger because it is established within a commutative contract, so it is a gift in its meaning not in its form, while emancipation is a gift in form and meaning. So if muhabah occurs first, it repels the weaker (emancipation); and if emancipation occurs first and is established and it does not allow repulsion, then necessary from it is competition. Translation: And the proof of Abu Hanifah is that muhabah is stronger because muhabah is established within a commutative contract, so muhabah will be a gift in its meaning, not in its form. And emancipation is a gift in form and meaning. So when muhabah first appeared, muhabah will repel the weaker (emancipation); and when emancipation first occurred and became established, and it does not allow repulsion, then competition is necessary. Commentary: This is the proof of Imam Abu Hanifah, the gist of which is that muhabah takes precedence over emancipation... (continues).
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the relative precedence between 'itq (emancipation) and muhabah (sale at undervalue) in a terminal illness. The author first establishes that both 'itq and muhabah are stronger than other types of bequests because they cannot be rescinded by the testator. They are thus given priority from the one-third. Then the dispute arises: between 'itq and muhabah, which takes precedence if both are made? The Ṣāḥibayn (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad) argue that 'itq is stronger because it cannot be rescinded by anyone, while muhabah can be rescinded by the buyer. They also dismiss any claim to precedence based on mere verbal mention. Imām Abū Ḥanīfa disagrees: muhabah is stronger because it is embedded in a commutative contract (bay'), making it a gift only in meaning, not in form. A commutative contract is stronger than a pure gift like 'itq. Therefore, if muhabah occurs first, it repels 'itq entirely. If 'itq occurs first and is already established, muhabah cannot be repelled, so they compete equally and share the one-third proportionally. The commentary explains the reasoning with examples and clarifies that the dispute is based on different considerations: the Ṣāḥibayn focus on the potential for rescission, while Imām focuses on the nature of the transaction. The author does not explicitly state which position is muftā bihi, but the structure and detail suggest both are recognized in the school.

Key Terms
عتق (ʿitq): Emancipation of a slave, here specifically a bequest of emancipation in terminal illness (also includes tadbīr).
محاباة (muḥābāh): A sale at an undervalue (where the price is less than market value), treated as a gift to the extent of the undervalue in terminal illness.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of a contract or disposition.
تبرع (tabarruʿ): A gift or gratuitous transfer of property without compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what happens if both 'itq and muhabah occur in the same terminal illness, with 'itq occurring first?
A) 'Itq takes full priority because it cannot be rescinded.
B) Muhabah takes full priority because it is a sale.
C) They compete equally and share the one-third proportionally.
D) Both are invalid because the testator cannot make two bequests from the one-third.

Key Takeaway
In terminal illness, the precedence between 'itq and muhabah depends on the reasoning: Sahibayn prioritize irrescindability (always 'itq), while Imam prioritizes contractual strength (order-dependent).

Precedence of Muhabah vs Itq in Marad al-Mawt
Dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on priority of muhabah and itq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the priority between muhabah and itq in marad al-mawt, explain the reasoning behind each view, and identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position and its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Strength in law is measured by revocability or embeddedness: Sahibayn value irrevocability; Abu Hanifa values contractual binding.

When a terminally ill person makes both a muhabah (sale at undervalue) and an itq (manumission), and together they exceed one-third of the estate, the estate cannot fully honour both. The Hanafi school splits on which takes priority. The Sahibayn hold that itq, being irrevocable, is stronger and must be executed first. Imam Abu Hanifa argues that muhabah, embedded in an exchange contract, is conceptually stronger and should prevail when it occurs first; otherwise they compete. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists weigh conflicting interests in bequests.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (both variants)
Identify the two positions within the Hanafi school: The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that itq is always stronger and takes precedence. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that muhabah is stronger if it occurs first; if itq occurs first, they compete equally.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that of the Sahibayn.
2
Identify the opponent's (Sahibayn's) proof
The Sahibayn argue that itq is irrevocable (cannot be annulled), while muhabah can be rescinded because it is part of a sale contract. Irrevocability makes itq a stronger act of charity.
The example in the text (buyer purchasing a 4000 dirham item for 1000) shows that muhabah is subject to faskh.
3
Follow Imam Abu Hanifa's proof
Imam argues that muhabah is embedded in a contract of exchange (aqd mu'awada), which is stronger than a pure gift like itq. Being part of a binding sale gives it legal resilience, even if revocable by rescission.
He uses the principle that a contract of exchange is stronger than a pure gift.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response within the school
Imam Abu Hanifa counters that revocability alone does not determine strength; being part of an exchange contract gives muhabah a superior basis. However, the Sahibayn's view ultimately prevailed as the relied-upon position.
The tarjih (preference) is based on the practical certainty of itq's irrevocability.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under the mufta bihi view (Sahibayn), itq is fully executed first, and muhabah is reduced to fit within the one-third limit. Under Imam's view, if muhabah occurs first, it takes full effect; if itq occurs first, both share the third proportionally.
The difference affects how heirs and beneficiaries receive the remaining estate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مثلا مشتری نے چار ہزار درہم کی چیز ایک ہزار درہم میں خریدی اور بائع مریض کا کوئی مال اس مبیع کے علاوہ نہیں ہے اور وارثوں نے اجازت نہ دی تو مشتری سے کہا جائے گا کہ تم کو صرف میت کے تہائی مال سے محابات ملے گی، اور باقی قیمت میت کے ورثا کیلئے پوری کرنی پڑے گی، ورنہ بیع کو فسخ کردے، تو اب مشتری کو اختیار ہے چاہے باقی قیمت دیدے اور چاہے بیچ کو فسخ کر دے تو معلوم ہوا کہ محابات ایسی چیز ہے جس کو فسخ لاحق ہو سکتا ہے اور عتق کو کسی بھی طرح فسخ لاحق نہیں ہو سکتا۔
سوال چلئے ٹھیک ہے، مگر جب یہاں محابات پہلے واقع ہوئی ہے تو ذکر لفظی کی تقدیم کی وجہ سے محابات کو تقدیم حاصل ہونی چاہئے؟ جواب حقیقی معنی کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے نہ کہ تقدیم لفظى كا، ولا معتبر بالتقديم الخ یعنی ذکر میں تقدیم کا کچھ اعتبار نہیں ہے کیونکہ زبانی الفاظ میں محابات کا مقدم واقع ہونا قوت و ثبوت میں مقدم ہو جانے کو واجب نہیں کرتا۔
اس لئے کہ قوت تو معنوی چیز ہے جس میں زبانی ذکر کا کوئی دخل نہیں ہے۔
خلاصہ کلام صاحبین نے عتق ومحابات میں عتق کو اولی اور مقدم قرار دیا ہے اور اس کی بنیاد قابل فسخ ہونے اور نہ ہونے پر رکھی ہے اور امام صاحب نے محابات کو مقدم رکھا ہے انہوں نے دوسرے اعتبار سے محابات کو ترجیح دی ہے۔
امام صاحب کی دلیل
وله ان المحاباة اقوى لا نها تثبت فى ضمن عقد المعاوضة فكان تبرعا بمعناه لا بصيغته والاعتاق تبرع صيغة ومعنى فاذا وجدت المحاباة اولا دفع الاضعف واذا وجد العتق اولا وثبت وهو لا يحتمل الدفع كان من ضرورته المزاحمة
ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ محابات اقومی ہے اس لئے کہ محابات عقد معاوضہ کے ضمن میں ثابت ہوتی ہے تو محابات تبرع ہوگا اپنے معنی کے اعتبار سے نہ کہ اپنے صیغہ کے اعتبار سے اور اعتاق تبرع ہے صیغہ اور معنی کے اعتبار سے پس جب کہ اولاً محابات پائی گئی تو محابات اضعف (عتق) کو دور کر دے گا اور جب کہ پہلے عتق پایا گیا اور معتق ثابت ہو گیا اور وہ محابات کو دور کرنے کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا تو اس کی ضروریات میں سے مزاحمت ہے۔ تشریح یہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ محابات عتق سے مقدم ہے اس لئے کہ محابات عقد بیع کے ضمن میں ثابت ہوتی ہے جس کو مصنف نے عقد معاوضہ سے تعبیر کیا ہے تو محابات اپنے صیغہ اور الفاظ کے اعتبار سے تبرع نہیں ہے بلکہ الفاظ کے اعتبار سے یہ عقد بیع ہے البتہ معنی کے اعتبار سے یہ تبرع ہے اور اعتاق لفظ اور معنی ہر اعتبار سے تبرع ہے تو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ محابات اقومی ہے کیونکہ عقد معاوضہ خالص تبرع سے اقوئی ہوا کرتا ہے۔ تو جب اقولی یعنی محابات پہلے سے ہوگی اور وہاں اضعف یعنی عتق جانا چاہے گا تو اقوئی اس کو دھکا دے کر دور کر دے گا اور جب محابات کے سامنے اس کا پنجہ بھی نہیں سکے گا تو ثبوت کہاں سے ہو گا۔ اور اگر پہلے عتق پایا جائے اور بعد میں محابات پائی جائے تو عتق چونکہ اضعف ہے اس وجہ سے عتق محابات کو دھکیل نہیں سکتا لہذا ان دونوں کے درمیان مزاحمت ثابت ہوگئی اور جب دونوں کے درمیان مزاحمت ثابت ہوگئی تو ناچار کہنا پڑے گا کہ دونوں مساوی اور برابر ہیں۔
For example, if a buyer purchased an item worth four thousand dirhams for one thousand dirhams, and the sick seller has no property besides this commodity, and the heirs do not grant permission, then the buyer will be told: 'You will only receive the muhabah (gifted portion) from one-third of the deceased's estate, and you must pay the remaining price to the heirs of the deceased, otherwise rescind the sale.' So the buyer has the option: either pay the remaining price or rescind the sale. Thus it is known that muhabah is something that can be subject to annulment (faskh), while itq (manumission) cannot be annulled in any way. 
Question: This is fine, but since muhabah occurs first here, should muhabah have precedence due to its verbal mention? Answer: Actual meaning is considered, not verbal precedence. 'And precedence in mention is not considered' — meaning that precedence in mention does not necessitate precedence in strength and establishment, because strength is a conceptual matter in which verbal mention has no role. 
Summary: The Sahibayn considered itq to be superior and prior over muhabah, basing this on whether it can be annulled or not. Imam (Abu Hanifa) held muhabah to be prior, giving preference to muhabah from another perspective. 
Imam's Proof: 'Wa lahu anna al-muhabata aqwa li annaha tathbutu fi dimni aqdi al-mu'awadati fa kanat tabarru'an bi ma'naha la bi sighatiha, wa al-i'taqu tabarru'un sighatan wa ma'nan. Fa iza wujidat al-muhabatu awwalan dafa'a al-ad'afa, wa iza wujida al-'itqu awwalan wa thabata wa huwa la yahtamilu al-daf'a kana min daruratihi al-muzahamah.' 
Translation: The proof of Abu Hanifa is that muhabah is stronger because it is established within the contract of exchange. Thus muhabah is a gift in meaning, not in its form. Whereas itq is a gift in form and meaning. Therefore, when muhabah occurs first, it repels the weaker (itq). When itq occurs first and is established, and it does not admit of being repelled, then necessarily there is competition (muzahamah) between them. Elaboration: This is the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa. Its conclusion is that muhabah is prior to itq because muhabah is established within a sale contract — which the author expressed as 'contract of exchange'. So muhabah is not a gift in its form and words; rather, in words it is a sale contract, but in meaning it is a gift. Itq is a gift in both word and meaning. From this it is understood that muhabah is stronger, because a contract of exchange is stronger than a pure gift. So when the stronger (muhabah) occurs first and the weaker (itq) seeks to enter, the stronger pushes it away. And when itq occurs first and is established, it cannot be repelled, so there is competition between them. If the weaker (itq) occurs first and then muhabah comes later, since itq is weaker, it cannot repel muhabah; thus competition is established. When competition is established, it must be said that they are equal.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the priority between muhabah (a sale at undervalue amounting to a gift) and itq (manumission) when both occur from a person in marad al-mawt (death illness) and the total exceeds one-third of the estate. The text begins with a practical example: a sick person sells an item worth 4000 dirhams for 1000 dirhams, making a muhabah of 3000. If the heirs do not approve, the buyer may either pay the full price (4000) to the heirs or rescind the sale. This shows that muhabah is subject to faskh (annulment) because it is part of a contract, whereas itq is not revocable. A question arises: since muhabah is mentioned first in the example, does verbal precedence give it priority? The answer is no; only substantive strength matters. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that itq is stronger because it is irrevocable. Imam Abu Hanifa differs: muhabah is stronger because it is embedded in a binding exchange contract (aqd mu'awada), making it more robust than a pure gift like itq. He reasons by way of analogy: when both occur, the stronger (muhabah) pushes away the weaker (itq) if it occurs first; if itq occurs first, it cannot be pushed away, so they compete and are treated equally. This ikhtilaf is based on whether revocability or embeddedness in a contract gives greater strength.

Key Terms
محابات (muhabah): A transaction in which a seller sells an item for less than its market value, the difference being a gift in meaning but embedded in a sale contract.
عتق (itq): Manumission of a slave, which is a pure gift in both form and meaning and is irrevocable.
ممارضہ (muzahamah): Competition or conflict between two claims when they cannot both be fully satisfied from the estate; they share proportionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why is itq given priority over muhabah in marad al-mawt?
A) Because itq is mentioned first in the Quran
B) Because itq is irrevocable, while muhabah can be annulled
C) Because itq is a gift in meaning only
D) Because itq occurs within a contract of exchange

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that itq (manumission) always takes precedence over muhabah (contractual gift) in marad al-mawt because it is irrevocable, whereas muhabah is subject to annulment.

Subsidiary Cases on Muhabah and Itq Precedence
Two subsidiary cases applying Imam Abu Hanifa's principle to sequences of muhabah and itq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Imam Abu Hanifa's rule of precedence (taqdim) to sequences of muhabah and itq in marad al-mawt, and distinguish it from the Sahibayn's position.

Core Idea
When muhabah and itq compete within the one-third, Imam Abu Hanifa prioritizes the earlier; the Sahibayn always prioritize itq.

Imam Abu Hanifa established a principle that when muhabah and itq occur in marad al-mawt, the one that came first is stronger and takes priority, unless the later is itq, which competes. This lesson applies that principle to two specific sequences: muhabah followed by itq followed by another muhabah, and itq followed by muhabah followed by another itq. The Sahibayn simplify the rule: itq always overrides muhabah regardless of order. Understanding this internal Hanafi dispute sharpens your ability to resolve complex gift and manumission conflicts within the one-third limit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base principle
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that earlier acts are stronger: if muhabah precedes itq, muhabah excludes itq from the third; if itq precedes muhabah, they compete equally. The Sahibayn hold itq always takes full priority.
The principle is derived from the idea that muhabah is a financial transaction while itq is an act of worship; Abu Hanifa balances them on timing.
2
Analyze Case 1: muhabah → itq → muhabah
First, divide the third equally between the two muhabahs because both are equal as contracts. Then, take the second muhabah’s half and split it equally with the itq because the itq preceded that muhabah, making them compete.
This yields the itq getting 1/4, each muhabah 1/4 of the estate after the third.
3
Analyze Case 2: itq → muhabah → itq
First, divide the third between the first itq and the muhabah because the itq preceded the muhabah, so they compete. Then, the itq’s share is divided equally between the two itqs because both itqs are equal.
The muhabah gets 1/4, each itq 1/4 after the third.
4
Compare with al-Sahibayn's view
Al-Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that itq always takes the entire third, and muhabah only gets what remains if any. They reject the timing-based competition.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام صاحب کے اصول پر متفرع ہونے والے دو جزئیے
وعلى هذا قال ابو حنيفه اذا حابي ثم اعتق ثم حابى قسم الثلث بين المحابتين نصفين لتساويهما ثم ما اصاب المحاباة الاخيرة قسم بينها وبين العتق لان العتق مقدم عليها فيستو يان ولو اعتق ثم حابي ثم اعتق قسم الثلث بين العتق الاول والمحاباة وما اصاب العتق قسم بينه وبين العتق الثانى وعندهما العتق اولى بكل حال
ترجمہ اور اس اصول کی بنیاد پر ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا جب کہ مریض نے محابات کی پھر آزاد کیا پھر محابات کی تو ثلث کو دونوں محابتوں کے در میان آدھا آدھا کیا جائے گا ان دونوں کے مساوی ہونے کی وجہ سے پھر جو مقدار کہ آخری محابات کو پہنچی ہے اس کو محابات اور معتق کے درمیان تقسیم کیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ محقق محابات پر مقدم ہے پس دونوں برابر ہوں گے اور اگر مریض نے آزاد کیا پھر محابات کی پھر آزاد کیا تو ثمث کو عشق اول اور محابات کے درمیان تقسیم کیا جائے گا اور جو مقدار کہ عتق کے حصہ میں پڑے اس کو عتق اول اور عتق ثانی کے درمیان تقسیم کیا جائے گا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ہر حال میں عتق اولی ہے۔
تشریح امام ابو حنیفہ کے بیان فرمودہ اصول کے مطابق ان کے نزدیک اس اصول پر دو متفرع ہونے والی جزئیوں کو پیش فرماتے ہیں - مریض نے مرض الموت میں ایک غلام کو آزاد کیا اور دو شخصوں کے ساتھ بیع میں محابات کی جسکی ترتیب اس طرح ہے اولاً محابات کی تھی اور ثانیاً غلام آزاد کیا اور ثالثاً پھر محابات کی تو یہاں کیا حکم ہوگا؟
تو فرمایا کہ ثلث کو دونوں محابات کے درمیان تقسیم کر لیا جائے گا کیونکہ یہ دونوں محابات برابر ہیں اس لئے کہ دونوں کا وقوع عقد معاوضہ کے ضمن میں ہوا ہے، پھر جو ثلث کا نصف آخری محابات کے حصہ میں پڑا ہے اس نصف کو آخری محابات اور معتق کے درمیان تقسیم کیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ آخری محابات سے پہلے عشق آیا ہے اور جب عشق پہلے آنے اور محابات کے بعد میں آئے تو مزاحمت کی وجہ سے وہاں محقق اور محابات برابر کے شریک ہوا کرتے ہیں لہذا یہاں بھی ایسا ہی ہوگا۔
- اور اگر پہلے مریض نے آزاد کیا ہو اور پھر مخابات کی ہو اور پھر ثالثا آزاد کیا ہو تو اب کیا حکم ہوگا؟
تو چونکہ یہاں محابات سے معتق مقدم ہے لہذا قاعدہ مذکورہ کے مطابق ثلث کو عتق اول اور محابات کے درمیان تقسیم کیا جائے گا، پھر جو محابات کے حصہ میں آیا اس میں کوئی ردو بدل نہ ہوگا، اور جو عشق کے حصہ میں آیا ہے اس کو عشق اول اور عشق ثانی کے درمیان تقسیم کر دیا جائے گا جس کی وجہ ظاہر ہے۔ اور یہ سب تفصیل امام ابوحنیفہ کے قول کے مطابق ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ہر حال میں عقیق ہی کو مقدم رکھا جائے گا۔
Two subsidiary cases branching from Imam's principle: 
'And on this basis, Abu Hanifa said: If he made a muhabah, then freed a slave, then made another muhabah, the third (of the estate) is divided between the two muhabahs equally because they are equal. Then what falls to the second muhabah is divided between it and the itq, because the itq precedes the muhabah, so they become equal. If he freed a slave, then made a muhabah, then freed another slave, the third is divided between the first itq and the muhabah. And what falls to the itq is divided between the first and second itq. According to them (Sahibayn), itq is always stronger.'
Translation: On the basis of this principle, Abu Hanifa said: When a sick person made a muhabah, then freed a slave, then made another muhabah, the third is divided equally between the two muhabahs because they are equal. Then the amount that reaches the second muhabah is divided between the muhabah and the itq, because the itq precedes the muhabah, so they become equal. If the sick person freed a slave, then made a muhabah, then freed another slave, the third is divided between the first itq and the muhabah. And what falls to the itq is divided between the first and second itq. And according to the Sahibayn, itq is always stronger.
Elaboration: According to Imam Abu Hanifa's stated principle, he presents two subsidiary cases. Case 1: In marad al-mawt, a man freed one slave and made muhabah with two persons in a sale, in this order: first muhabah, then freed a slave, then second muhabah. What is the ruling? He said: The third is divided equally between the two muhabahs because both occur within a contract of exchange, so they are equal. Then the half of the third that fell to the second muhabah is divided between that muhabah and the itq, because the itq came before the second muhabah, and when itq comes first and muhabah later, there is competition (muzahamah), so they share equally. Case 2: If the sick person first freed a slave, then made a muhabah, then freed another slave. Here, since itq precedes muhabah, according to the mentioned rule, the third is divided between the first itq and the muhabah. Whatever falls to the muhabah remains as is. Whatever falls to the itq is divided between the first and second itq. This detail is according to Imam Abu Hanifa's statement. According to the Sahibayn, in all cases itq is given priority.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage illustrates two subsidiary cases (juz'iyyat) derived from Imam Abu Hanifa's principle that muhabah is stronger than itq when it occurs first, but weaker if itq precedes. The text provides the Arabic matn from the Hidayah and then an Urdu explanation. In Case 1 (muhabah → itq → muhabah), the third is first split evenly between the two muhabahs, then the share of the second muhabah is split with the itq because the itq preceded that muhabah, causing competition. In Case 2 (itq → muhabah → itq), the third is split between the first itq and the muhabah; then the itq's share is split between the two itqs. The Sahibayn reject this and hold that itq is always stronger and takes priority regardless of order. This shows the practical application of the qa'idah that when the stronger (muhabah, per Abu Hanifa) precedes, it excludes the weaker; when the weaker precedes, they compete. The Sahibayn's view is simpler: itq always overrides muhabah.

Key Terms
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum that can be bequeathed or gifted in marad al-mawt without heirs' permission.
مزاحمت (muzahamah): Competition between two claims when the third is insufficient; they share proportionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, in the case of muhabah → itq → muhabah, what is the first step in distributing the one-third?
A) Divide it equally between the itq and the first muhabah
B) Divide it equally between the two muhabahs
C) Give it all to the itq
D) Divide it between the itq and the second muhabah

Key Takeaway
In intra-Hanafi disputes, understanding both the Imam's and the Sahibayn's positions is essential; the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view that itq always takes priority.

Will to Buy and Free a Slave with Specified Amount: Partial Loss
Ruling on a will to purchase and free a slave with 100 dirhams when some money is lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Sahibayn's view that a will to purchase and free a slave is executed with the remainder prevails over Imam Abu Hanifa's view, and apply the analogy to Hajj will.

Core Idea
A will for an act of devotion (qurbah) is executed as far as possible, even if the specified amount diminishes.

In this lesson, we examine a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens when a testator wills that a slave be purchased and freed using a specific sum, but part of that sum is lost. Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn reach different conclusions, hinging on whether the will is tied to the exact amount or to the underlying act of devotion. The Sahibayn's view, which becomes mufta bihi, draws an analogy to the will for Hajj. Let's explore the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State clearly the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa and of the Sahibayn regarding a will to use 100 dirhams to buy and free a slave when one dirham is lost.
Imam Abu Hanifa says the will is void; Sahibayn say it is executed with the remainder.
2
Understand Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa hold that the will is void? Note his focus on the specification of the exact amount as a condition.
He treats the wording as a conditional grant; if the condition (full sum) fails, the will fails.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's analogy to Hajj
How do the Sahibayn analogize to a will for Hajj? Both are qurbah (acts of devotion), so the will should be fulfilled as much as possible.
The analogy (qiyas) is based on the shared illa of devotion.
4
Note the tarjih (mufta bihi)
Which view is relied upon in the Hanafi school and why? Cite the authority weight and the practical benefit.
The Sahibayn's view is mufta bihi; it is from Zahir al-Riwayah and more practical.
5
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence of the difference? When is the will executed and when void?
Following Imam Abu Hanifa, the will is void and money returns to heirs; following Sahibayn, it is partially executed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موصی کا ان سو دراہم کا غلام خرید کر آزاد کر دینا کے الفاظ سے وصیت کا حکم، اقوال فقہاء
قال ومن أوصى بان يعتق عنه بهذه المائة عبد فهلك منها در هم لم يعتق عنه بما بقى عند ابي حنيفة وان كانت وصيته بحجة يحج عنه بما بقى من حيث بلغ وان لم يهلك منها وبقى شى من الحجة يرد على الورثة وقالا يعتق عنه بما بقى لانه وصية بنوع قربة فيجب تنفيذها ما امكن اعتبار بالوصية بالحج
ترجمہ: "اور جس نے وصیت کی کہ اس کی طرف سے اس سو درہم سے ایک غلام خرید کر آزاد کیا جائے، تو اگر اس میں سے ایک درہم بھی ہلاک ہو گیا تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس (بقیہ) سے غلام آزاد نہیں کیا جائے گا، حالانکہ اگر اس کی وصیت حج کے بارے میں ہوتی تو جہاں تک ممکن ہو بقیہ سے اس کی طرف سے حج کیا جاتا، خواہ اس میں سے کچھ ہلاک نہ ہوا ہو اور حج سے بچا ہوا مال وارثوں کو لوٹا دیا جاتا۔ اور (صاحبین) نے کہا: اس سے بقیہ کے ساتھ غلام آزاد کیا جائے گا، کیونکہ یہ وصیت ایک قسم کی قربت ہے، لہٰذا جہاں تک ممکن ہو اسے نافذ کرنا واجب ہے، حج کی وصیت پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔ "
تشریح: یہ ایک نئے موضوع کا آغاز ہے: وصیت بخرید غلام و اعتاق. موصی نے وصیت کی کہ میرے سو درہم سے ایک غلام خرید کر آزاد کر دو۔ اب اگر وہ سو درہم میں سے ایک درہم بھی گم ہو جائے تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک وصیت باطل ہو جائے گی اور بقیہ سے غلام نہیں خریدا جائے گا، کیونکہ وصیت مشروط ہے اس مال کے پورے ہونے پر، جیسے کسی نے کہا "اس سو درہم سے" تو یہ تعیین ہے، اگر مال کم ہو تو وصیت منتفی ہو جاتی ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ جتنا مال بچا ہے اس سے غلام خرید کر آزاد کیا جائے گا، کیونکہ یہ قربت کی وصیت ہے، اسے ممکنہ حد تک نافذ کرنا چاہیے، جیسے حج کی وصیت میں اگر مال کم ہو تو بقیہ سے حج کیا جاتا ہے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کا استدلال: حج کی وصیت میں عبادت مقصود ہے، اس لیے تخفیف ممکن ہے؛ جبکہ یہاں عتق (آزادی) مقصود ہے جو ایک خاص فعل ہے، اس میں کمی نہیں ہو سکتی۔ صاحبین قیاس کرتے ہیں کہ دونوں قربت ہیں، اس لیے حکم یکساں ہونا چاہیے۔
The ruling of a will expressed in the words 'buy a slave and free him with these one hundred dirhams', statements of the jurists.
'He said: Whoever makes a will that a slave be purchased and freed on his behalf with this one hundred dirhams, then if one dirham of it is lost, it will not be freed with the remainder according to Abu Hanifa. But if his will was for Hajj, Hajj would be performed on his behalf with the remainder wherever it reaches, even if nothing is lost and something remains from the Hajj, it is returned to the heirs. They (Sahibayn) said: He will be freed with the remainder because it is a will of a type of devotion, so it must be executed as much as possible, by analogy with the will for Hajj.'
Elaboration: This is the beginning of a new topic: will to buy a slave and free him. The testator made a will: 'With my one hundred dirhams, buy a slave and set him free.' Now if even one dirham of that hundred is lost, according to Imam Abu Hanifa the will becomes void and a slave will not be purchased with the remainder, because the will is conditional upon the full amount, just as if someone said 'with this hundred dirhams' that indicates specification; if the money is reduced, the will is nullified. The Sahibayn say: The slave will be purchased and freed with whatever amount remains, because this is a will for an act of devotion; it should be implemented as much as possible, just as in the will for Hajj, if the money is insufficient, Hajj is performed with the remainder. Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning: In the will for Hajj, the act of worship is the objective, so reduction is possible; here manumission (itq) is the objective, which is a specific act that cannot be reduced. The Sahibayn analogize: both are acts of devotion, so the ruling should be the same.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage addresses a new issue: a will to use a specified sum (100 dirhams) to purchase and free a slave. The question is whether the will can be partially executed if part of the money is lost. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the will is completely invalidated because the specification of 'this hundred dirhams' makes the grant specific to that exact amount; if any is lost, the subject matter is no longer intact. The Sahibayn, by contrast, compare this to a will to perform Hajj: if the bequeathed amount is insufficient, Hajj is performed with whatever remains, and any excess is returned to the heirs. They argue that both are types of devotion (qurbah), so the will should be fulfilled as far as possible. Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes: Hajj is a worship that can be performed with whatever is available (e.g., a shorter journey), but manumission is a singular act that requires full payment; a person cannot be partially freed. The Urdu commentary explains that Imam Abu Hanifa sees the wording as a conditional specification, while the Sahibayn see the underlying intention (qurbah) as overriding the form. The mufta bihi in this case is the view of the Sahibayn, as it is more flexible and aligns with the general principle of fulfilling wills to the extent possible.

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyyah): A bequest or will instructing that an act be done with specified property after death.
قربت (qurbah): An act of devotion or drawing near to Allah, such as Hajj or manumission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why should a will to purchase and free a slave with a specified sum be executed with the remaining amount if some is lost?
A) Because the will creates a debt that must be paid fully
B) Because it is a type of devotion, so it should be fulfilled as much as possible
C) Because the testator's intention is to free a specific slave
D) Because the remaining money can be used for other charitable purposes

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the relied-upon position is that a will for an act of devotion (qurbah) is executed with the remaining amount, by analogy to the will for Hajj.
