Resolving Conflicting Claims on Timing of Emancipation: Legatee vs Heir
Explaining a Hanafi ruling on conflicting claims over timing of emancipation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on burden of proof and the maxim of attributing events to the nearest time to determine whose statement is accepted when the legatee and heir disagree on whether emancipation occurred during health or illness.

Core Idea
When legatee and heir disagree on timing, the heir's statement is accepted because the legatee is the claimant and events are attributed to the nearest time.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in Hanafi inheritance law: a testator leaves a bequest of one-third to a legatee and also frees a slave. The legatee and heir agree the slave was freed, but dispute whether it was during health (all property) or fatal illness (one-third only). The ruling turns on two key principles: the allocation of burden of proof between claimant and denier, and the legal maxim that events are attributed to the nearest time. Understanding this ruling will enable you to resolve similar conflicts in inheritance cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their claims
The legatee claims emancipation during health; the heir claims during illness. Determine the legal effect of each claim: health emancipation is not a bequest and uses all property; illness emancipation is a bequest limited to one-third and takes precedence over other bequests.
2
Apply burden of proof rules
The legatee is the claimant (mudda'i) because he asserts a right that contradicts the default presumption. The heir is the denier (munkir). The claimant must bring evidence; the denier's statement is accepted with oath.
The default presumption is that the emancipation occurred during illness (nearest time).
3
Apply the maxim of attributing events to the nearest time
The emancipation is a new event (hadith). Events are attributed to the nearest possible time of which there is certainty. The nearest time is the illness, which supports the heir.
This is a Hanafi usul principle: al-hawadith tunzalu ila aqrab al-awqat.
4
Identify exceptions
If the legatee provides evidence (bayyina) that the emancipation was in health, his statement is accepted. Also, if after executing the emancipation from one-third a surplus remains (i.e., the slave's value is less than one-third), that surplus goes to the legatee.
The surplus goes to the legatee because there is no rival claimant for it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن اوصى بثلث ماله لاخر فاقر الموصى له والوراث ان الميت اعتق هذا العبد فقال الموصى له اعتقه في الصحة وقال الوارث اعتقه فى المرض فالقول قول الوارث ولا شي للموصى له الا ان يفضل من الثلث شي او تقوم له البينة ان العتق في الصحة
ترجمه: محمد نے فرمایا اور جس نے اپنے ثلث مال کی کسی دوسرے شخص کے لئے وصیت کی پس موصى له اور وارث نے اقرار کیا کہ میت نے اس غلام کو آزاد کیا ہے پس موصى له نے کہا کہ اس کو صحت میں آزاد کیا ہے اور وارث نے کہا کہ اس کو مرض میں آزاد کیا ہے تو وارث کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور موصى له کے لئے کچھ نہ ہو گا مگر یہ کہ ثلث سے کچھ بچ جائے یا موصى له کے لئے بینه قائم ہو جائے کہ عتق حالت صحت میں ہوا ہے۔
شرح: تشریح زید مرحوم نے خالد کے لئے اپنے ثلث مال کی وصیت کی اور زید کا ایک غلام ہے خالد اور زید کا وارث اس بات کا اقرار کرتے ہیں کہ زید نے اس کو آزاد کیا ہے، البتہ ان دونوں کا اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ کب آزاد کیا ہے۔ خالد تو کہتا ہے کہ حالت صحت میں آزاد کیا ہے اور وارث کہتا ہے کہ حالت مرض میں آزاد کیا ہے، خالد کے کہنے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ یہ غلام صحت کی حالت میں آزاد کیا گیا ہے تو یہ وصیت کے درجہ میں نہیں ہے لہذا پورے مال سے اس کا عتق نافذ ہوگا اور جو مال باقی ہے اس کے ثلث کا میں مستحق ہوں، اور زید کا وارث کہتا ہے کہ زید نے اس کو حالت مرض میں آزاد کیا ہے اور حالت مرض کا اعتاق وصیت سے مقدم ہے اور اس کا نفاذ ثلث مال میں ہوتا ہے اور عتق دیگر وصایا سے مقدم ہوتا ہے لہذا خالد کے حق سے مقدم ہوگا۔ تو ثلث سے اولاً غلام کا عتق نافذ ہوگا اگر غلام کی آزادی کے بعد ثلث میں سے کچھ بچ جائے تو وہ خالد کو ملے گا اور اگر نہ بچے تو نہیں ملے گا تو یہاں کس کا قول معتبر ہو گا ؟ فرمایا کہ اگر خالد اپنے دعوے پر بینه قائم کر دے تو خالد کا قول معتبر ہو گا ورنہ وارث کا قول معتبر ہو گا اس لئے کہ یہاں خالد مدعی ہے اور وارث منکر ہے اور مدعی کا فریضہ ہے کہ وہ گواہ قائم کرے ورنہ مع الیمین منکر کا قول معتبر ہوا کرتا ہے، لہذا فرماتے ہیں۔ موصى له مدعی اور وارث منکر ہے اور منکر کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوتا ہے
لان الموصى له يدعى استحقاق ثلث ما بقى من التركة بعد العتق لان العتق فى الصحة ليس بوصية ولهذا ينفذ من جميع المال والوارث ينكره لان مدعاه العتق فى المرض وهو وصية والعتق فى المرض مقدم على الوصية بثلث المال فكان منكرا والقول قول المنكر مع اليمين
ترجمه: اس لئے کہ موصى له عتق کے بعد ترکہ ما بقی کے ثلث کے استحقاق کا دعویٰ کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ عتق حالت صحت میں وصیت نہیں اس وجہ سے وہ (حق صحت) پورے مال سے نافذ ہوتا ہے اور وارث اس کا انکار کرتا ہے اس لئے وارث کا دعویٰ مرض الموت کے اندر آزاد کرنے کا ہے اور یہ (مرض الموت میں آزاد کرنا) وصیت ہے اور مرض الموت میں عتق ثلث مال کے سلسلہ میں وصیت پر مقدم ہے تو وارث منکر ہوگا اور قول منکر کا معتبر ہوتا ہے مع اس کی یمین کے۔
تشریح: یہاں خالد (موصى له) مدعی اور وارث منکر کیوں ہے تو فرمایا کہ خالد دعویٰ کرتا ہے کہ نفاذ عتق کے بعد جو ترکہ باقی رہا میں اس کے ثلث کا مستحق ہوں اس لئے کہ عتق صحت کی حالت میں ہو چکا ہے اور وارث اس سے منکر ہے اس لئے کہ وارث کا دعویٰ یہ ہے کہ موصی نے مرض الموت میں آزاد کیا ہے اور مرض الموت میں آزاد کرنا وصیت ہے اور مرض الموت کا عتق دیگر وصایا پر مقدم ہوا کرتا ہے۔ خلاصہ کلام: وارث کی غرض یہ ہے کہ موصى له کے لئے کچھ نہیں ہے تو وارث کو منکر شمار کیا گیا اور منکر کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوا کرتا ہے۔
وارث کا قول معتبر ہونے کی دوسری دلیل: ولان العتق حادث والحوادث تضاف الى اقرب الاوقات المتيقن بها فكان الظاهر شاهد اللوارث فيكون القول قوله مع اليمين الا ان يفضل شى من الثلث على قيمة العبدلا نه لا مزاحم له فيه او تقوم له البيئة ان العتق في الصحة لان الثابت بالبينة كالثابت معاينة وهو خصم في اقامتهما لا ثبات حقه
ترجمه: اور اس لئے کہ عتق حادث ہے اور حوادث مضاف ہوتے ہیں اقرب الاوقات کی جانب ان کے سلسلہ میں تیقن کی وجہ سے تو ظاہر حال وارث کے لئے شاہد ہو گیا تو قول وارث کا معتبر ہو گا مع اس کی یمین کے مگر یہ کہ غلام کی قیمت پر ثلث میں سے کچھ بچ جائے اس لئے کہ موصى له کا اس فاضل میں کوئی مزاحم نہیں ہے یا موصى له کے لئے بینه قائم ہو جائے اس بات پر کہ عتق صحت کی حالت میں ہوا ہے اس لئے کہ جو چیز بینه سے ثابت ہو وہ ایسی ہے جسے چشم دید طریقے پر ثابت ہو اور موصى له خصم ہو گا اقامت بینه کے سلسلہ میں اپنے حق کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے۔
تشریح: وارث کا قول معتبر ہونے کی یہ دوسری دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ عتق پہلے سے تو ہے نہیں معلوم ہوا کہ یہ عتق حادث ہے اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ حادث کی اضافت اقرب الاوقات کی جانب ہوا کرتی ہے کیونکہ اس اضافت میں جو تیقن ہے وہ البعد الاوقات کی جانب اضافت میں نہیں ہے اور اقرب الاوقات حالت مرض ہے تو اس اعتبار سے بھی ظاہر حال وارث کے لئے شاہد ہوا اس لئے وارث کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوگا۔
البتہ اگر ثلث میں عتق کو نافذ کرنے کے بعد کچھ بچ رہے تو وہ خالد (موصى له) کو دیدیا جائے گا کیونکہ اس فاضل میں اب کوئی اس کا مزاحم نہیں ہے۔ یا پھر خالد گواہ قائم کر دے کہ عتق حالت صحت میں واقع ہوا ہے تو اب خالد کا قول معتبر ہو گا اس لئے کہ بینه کے ذریعہ جو بات ثابت
He (Muhammad) said: And whoever bequeaths one-third of his property to another, then the legatee and the heir confess that the deceased emancipated this slave. The legatee says: He emancipated him in health. And the heir says: He emancipated him in illness. So the statement is the statement of the heir, and nothing is for the legatee unless something remains from the third, or the legatee establishes evidence that the emancipation was in health.
Translation: Muhammad said: And whoever makes a bequest of one-third of his property to another person, then the legatee and the heir confess that the deceased emancipated this slave. The legatee said: He emancipated him in health. And the heir said: He emancipated him in illness. So the statement of the heir will be considered, and nothing will be for the legatee unless something remains from the third, or the legatee establishes evidence that the emancipation occurred in health.
Commentary: Explanation: Zaid, deceased, bequeathed one-third of his property to Khalid, and Zaid has a slave. Khalid and Zaid's heir both agree that Zaid emancipated this slave. However, they differ as to when he emancipated him. Khalid says he emancipated him in health, and the heir says he emancipated him in illness. Khalid's meaning is that this slave was emancipated in health, so it is not in the category of a bequest; therefore it is executed from the entire property, and I am entitled to one-third of the remaining property. Zaid's heir says that Zaid emancipated him in illness, and emancipation during illness takes precedence over bequests and is executed from one-third of the property, and emancipation takes precedence over other bequests. So it will take precedence over Khalid's right. So from the third, first the slave's emancipation is executed. If after the slave's emancipation something remains from the third, then that goes to Khalid. If nothing remains, then he gets nothing. So here, whose statement is considered? It is said: If Khalid establishes evidence for his claim, then Khalid's statement is considered; otherwise the heir's statement is considered, because here Khalid is the claimant and the heir is the denier, and the claimant's duty is to produce witnesses; otherwise, with the oath, the denier's statement is considered. Therefore they say: The legatee is the claimant and the heir is the denier, and the denier's statement with the oath is considered.
Because the legatee claims entitlement to one-third of what remains of the estate after the emancipation, because emancipation during health is not a bequest, and therefore it is executed from all the property. And the heir denies it, because his claim is that the emancipation was during illness, and that is a bequest, and emancipation during illness takes precedence over the bequest of one-third of the property. So he is the denier, and the statement is the statement of the denier with the oath.
Translation: Because the legatee claims entitlement to one-third of the remaining estate after the emancipation, because emancipation during health is not a bequest, and for that reason it is executed from all the property. And the heir denies it, because his claim is the emancipation during the illness, and this (emancipation during illness) is a bequest, and emancipation during illness takes precedence over the bequest of one-third of the property. So the heir would be the denier, and the statement of the denier is considered, along with his oath.
Commentary: Here, Khalid (the legatee) is the claimant and the heir is the denier. Why? It is said that Khalid claims that after the execution of the emancipation, he is entitled to one-third of the remaining estate, because the emancipation occurred in health. And the heir denies this, because the heir's claim is that the testator emancipated him during illness, and emancipation during illness is a bequest, and emancipation during illness takes precedence over other bequests. Summary: The heir's aim is that there is nothing for the legatee, so the heir is counted as the denier, and the denier's statement with the oath is considered.
The second proof for the heir's statement being considered: And because the emancipation is an event (hadith), and events are attributed to the nearest possible time regarding which there is certainty. Thus the apparent situation bears witness for the heir, so his statement is accepted with his oath, unless something remains from the third over the value of the slave, because there is no rival for him in that surplus, or the legatee establishes evidence that the emancipation was in health, because what is established by evidence is like what is established by direct sight, and he is a contestant in establishing it to prove his right.
Translation: And because the emancipation is an occurrence, and occurrences are attributed to the nearest time with certainty regarding them. So the apparent situation became a witness for the heir, so the heir's statement will be considered with his oath, unless something remains from the third over the slave's price, because the legatee has no rival in that surplus, or the legatee establishes evidence that the emancipation occurred in health, because what is established by evidence is like that established by direct sight, and the legatee is a contestant in establishing evidence to prove his right.
Commentary: This is the second proof for the heir's statement being considered. The summary is that the emancipation was not known to exist before; it is known that this emancipation is a new event, and the rule is that a new event is attributed to the nearest time, because in that attribution there is certainty which is not present in attribution to the farthest times, and the nearest time is the state of illness. So from this perspective as well, the apparent situation witnesses for the heir, therefore the heir's statement with the oath is considered.
However, if after executing the emancipation from the third, something remains, then that will be given to Khalid (the legatee), because in that surplus there is no rival for him. Or if Khalid produces witnesses that the emancipation occurred in health, then Khalid's statement will be considered, because what is established through evidence is like that established by direct sight.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Wasaya presents a specific ruling within Hanafi fiqh concerning conflicting claims between a legatee (musa lahu) and an heir (warith) regarding the timing of a slave's emancipation by the testator. The passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn (likely from al-Hidayah or al-Quduri). The ruling is stated first, then two proofs are provided.

The scenario: A testator (musi) bequeaths one-third of his property to a legatee. The testator also had a slave. Both the legatee and the heir agree that the testator emancipated this slave, but they disagree on when. The legatee claims the emancipation occurred during the testator's health (sihha), while the heir claims it occurred during the testator's terminal illness (marad al-mawt). The ruling: The heir's statement is accepted (with his oath), unless the legatee provides evidence (bayyina) that the emancipation was during health, or unless after deducting the slave's value from one-third of the estate, there is a surplus, which then goes to the legatee.

The first proof is based on the rules of evidence and burden of proof. The legatee is considered the claimant (mudda'i) because he claims a right (the remaining one-third after emancipation) that contradicts the apparent situation (the emancipation being in illness, which is more likely). The heir is the denier (munkir). The principle is: 'The claimant must produce evidence, and the denier's statement is accepted with his oath.' Since the legatee cannot prove his claim, the heir's statement prevails.

The second proof is based on a legal maxim (qawida): 'Events (hawadith) are attributed to the nearest possible time.' Since the emancipation is a new event and did not exist before, and the nearest time before the death is the period of illness, the default assumption is that it occurred during illness unless proven otherwise. This external evidence (zahir al-hal) supports the heir. Therefore, the heir's statement is accepted.

The commentary clarifies that if the legatee can produce witnesses, he becomes the one whose statement is accepted. Similarly, if after the emancipation there remains some surplus from the one-third (i.e., the value of the slave is less than one-third), that surplus goes to the legatee regardless of the timing, because there is no competing claim. This ruling balances the interests of both parties while adhering to the principles of Islamic jurisprudence.

Key Terms
موصى له (musa lahu): The person in whose favor a bequest (wasiyya) is made; the legatee.
وارث (warith): The person who inherits from the deceased; the legal heir.
عتق ('itq): Emancipation of a slave; setting free.
صحة (sihha): State of health; the opposite of marad (illness). During health, transactions are effective from all property.
مرض (marad): Illness, specifically terminal illness (marad al-mawt) that causes death. During such illness, gifts and bequests are limited to one-third.
مدعى (mudda'i): Claimant; the one who asserts a right or fact that is not apparent.
منكر (munkir): Denier; the one who denies the claim; his statement is accepted with his oath if the claimant fails to prove.
بينة (bayyina): Evidence; usually two male witnesses or one male and two females.
قرب الاوقات (aqrab al-awqat): The nearest possible time to which an event can be attributed for certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a testator bequeaths one-third to a legatee, and both legatee and heir agree the testator freed a slave but disagree on the timing (health vs. illness), what is the default ruling if the legatee provides no evidence?
A) The legatee's statement is accepted because he benefits from the emancipation.
B) The heir's statement is accepted with his oath, and the legatee gets nothing unless a surplus remains from the one-third.
C) The court must divide the estate equally between the legatee and the heir.
D) The slave's value is deducted from the entire estate.

Key Takeaway
In disputes over the timing of an emancipation, the heir's statement is accepted with oath unless the legatee provides evidence or a surplus remains from the one-third, because the legatee is the claimant and events are attributed to the nearest time.

Acceptance of Heir's Statement in Dispute over Emancipation Timing
Explaining why heir's claim prevails in dispute with legatee over emancipation timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that events are attributed to the nearest certain time to determine whose statement is accepted in a dispute between heir and legatee over the timing of emancipation.

Core Idea
Events are attributed to the nearest certain time, making the heir's statement prevail unless evidence proves otherwise.

In a dispute over whether a testator emancipated a slave during health or death-illness, the heir and the legatee have conflicting claims. This passage explains why the Hanafi school accepts the heir's statement with oath, based on a general legal principle. Understanding this rule clarifies how procedural presumptions operate in inheritance and will disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify parties and claims
The legatee (mūṣā lahu) claims emancipation occurred in health, making the slave's value taken from the whole estate. The heir claims it occurred in death-illness, limiting it to one-third. The heir denies the legatee's claim, so he is the denier (munkir).
2
Apply first justification: denier's statement accepted
In Hanafi procedure, the denier's statement is accepted with oath unless the claimant provides evidence. Since the heir denies the entire claim, his statement is taken.
This is based on the rule: al-munkir lahu al-qawl.
3
Apply second justification: events attributed to nearest time
Emancipation is an event. The principle al-hawadith tuḍāfu ilā aqrab al-awqāt al-mutayaqqan bihā attributes it to the nearest certain time, which is death-illness. Thus the apparent state supports the heir.
This principle shifts the presumption.
4
Identify exceptions
If after applying the one-third limit there is surplus (fāḍil), the legatee takes it without dispute. Also, if the legatee brings evidence (bayyinah) that emancipation was in health, his claim prevails.
Evidence overrides the presumption.
5
Understand procedural nuance
Although emancipation is a right of the slave, here the legatee is the claimant and the proper opponent to the heir, so the legatee can bring evidence to prove his claim.
This clarifies that the legatee has standing.

ترجمہ اس لئے کہ موصی اعتق کے بعد ترکہ مابقی کے ثمث کے استحقاق کا دعویٰ کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ عشق حالت صحت میں وصیت نہیں اس وجہ سے وہ (حق صحت ) پورے مال سے نافذ ہوتا ہے اور وارث اس کا انکار کرتا ہے اس لئے وارث کا دعوی مرض الموت کے اندرز آزاد کرنے کا ہے اور یہ (مرض الموت میں آزاد کرنا ) وصیت ہے اور مرض الموت میں عشق ثلث مال کے سلسلہ میں وصیت پر مقدم ہے تو وارث منکر ہوگا اور قول منکر کا معتبر ہوتا ہے مع اس کی یمین کے۔
تشریح یہاں خالد (موضی (ہ) مدعی اور وارث منکر کیوں ہے تو فرمایا کہ خالد دعوی کرتا ہے کہ نفاذ عتیق کے بعد جو تر کہ باقی رہا میں اس کے ثلث کا مستحق ہوں اس لئے کہ عتق صحت کی حالت میں ہو چکا ہے اور وارث اس سے منکر ہے اس لئے کہ وارث کا دعوی یہ ہے کہ موصی نے مرض الموت میں آزاد کیا ہے اور مرض الموت میں آزاد کرنا وصیت ہے اور مرض الموت کا عشق دیگر وصایا پر مقدم ہوا کرتا ہے۔ خلاصہ کلام . وارث کی غرض یہ ہے کہ موصی لا کے لئے کچھ نہیں ہے تو وارث کو منکر شار کیا گیا اور منکر کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوا کرتا ہے۔
وارث کا قول معتبر ہونے کی دوسری دلیل
ولان العتق حادث والحوادث تضاف الى اقرب الاوقات المتيقن بها فكان الظاهر شاهد اللوارث فيكون القول قوله مع اليمين الا ان يفضل شى من الثلث على قيمة العبدلا نه لا مزاحم له فيه او تقوم له البيئة ان العتق في الصحة لان الثابت بالبينة كالثابت معاينة وهو خصم في اقامتهما لا ثبات حقه
ترجمہ اور اس لئے کہ عشق حادث ہے اور حوادث مضاف ہوتے ہیں اقرب الاوقات کی جانب ان کے سلسلہ میں تیقن کی وجہ سے تو ظاہر حال وارث کے لئے شاہد ہو گیا تو قول وارث کا معتبر ہو گا مع اس کی یمین کے مگر یہ کہ غلام کی قیمت پر ثلث میں سے کچھ بچ جائے اس لئے کہ موصی لہ کا اس فاضل میں کوئی مزاحم نہیں ہے یا موضی لہ کیلئے بینہ قائم ہو جائے اس بات پر کہ عشق صحت کی حالت میں ہوا ہے اس لئے کہ جو چیز بینہ سے ثابت نہو وہ ایسی ہے جسے چشم دید طریقے پر ثابت ہو اور موصی این خصم ہو گا ۔ اقامت بینہ کے سلسلہ میں اپنے حق کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے ۔
تشریح وارث کا قول معتبر ہونے کی یہ دوسری دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ عحق پہلے سے تو ہے نہیں معلوم ہوا کہ یہ حق حادث ہے اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ حادث کی اضافت اقرب الاوقات کی جانب ہوا کرتی ہے کیونکہ اس اضافت میں جو تیقن ہے وہ البعد الا واقات کی جانب اضافت میں نہیں ہے اور اقرب الاوقات حالت مرض ہے تو اس اعتبار سے بھی ظاہر حال وارث کے لئے شاہد ہوا اس لئے وارث کا قول مع السیمین معتبر ہوگا۔
البتہ اگر شاٹ میں عقیق کو نافذ کرنے کے بعد کچھ بیچ رہے تو وہ خالد ( موضی (1) کو دیدیا جائے گا کیونکہ اس فاضل میں اب کوئی اس کا مزاحم نہیں ہے۔ یا پھر خالد گواہ قائم کر دے کہ معتق حالت صحت میں واقع ہوا ہے تو اب خالد کا قول معتبر ہو گا اس لئے کہ بینہ کے ذریعہ جو بات ثابت
ہو جائے وہ ایسی ہے جیسے معامیہ ثابت ہوئی ہو۔
سوال امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک تو عشق حق العبد ہے لہذا جب تک غلام کی طرف سے دعوئی نہ ہو تو اقامت بعینہ کیسے ہو سکتا ہے؟ جواب یہاں ہم نے غلام کو مدعی نہیں ٹھہرایا ہے بلکہ مدعی موضی لہ ہے اور موضی لہ ہی وارث کا خصم ہے نہ کہ غلام اور اس کی جانب سے دعوئی موجود ہے اور دعوے کے بعد اقامت بینہ درست ہے کیونکہ جہاں خالد کو ضرورت ہے کہ وہ اپنا حق ثابت کرے تو اقامت بینہ کے سلسلہ میں موضی راہی کو خصم ٹھہرایا جائے گا۔
Translation: Because the testator after emancipation claims entitlement to one-third of the remaining estate because emancipation in health is not a will, therefore that (right of health) takes effect from the entire estate, and the heir denies this; so the heir claims that the emancipation occurred in death-illness, and this (emancipation in death-illness) is a will, and emancipation in death-illness takes precedence over other wills concerning one-third of the estate; therefore the heir is the denier, and the statement of the denier is accepted with his oath. Explanation: Here Khalid (the legatee) is the claimant and the heir is the denier because Khalid claims entitlement to one-third of the remainder after emancipation, while the heir claims the emancipation was in death-illness. Summary: The heir's benefit is that nothing goes to the legatee, so the heir is made the denier and his statement with oath is accepted. The second reason for accepting the heir's statement: "And because emancipation is an event, and events are attributed to the nearest time that is certain, so the apparent state bears witness for the heir; thus the heir's statement is accepted with his oath, unless something from the one-third is surplus over the slave's value, for then there is no rival for him in that surplus, or the legatee establishes evidence that the emancipation was in health, because what is established by evidence is like what is established by direct observation, and he is the opponent in presenting it to prove his right." Explanation: The rule is that events are attributed to the nearest time, and the nearest time is death-illness, so the heir's statement is accepted. If after emancipation there is a surplus in the estate, it goes to the legatee, or if the legatee brings witnesses, his statement is accepted. Question: According to Imam Abu Hanifah, emancipation is the right of the slave, so how can the legatee bring evidence without the slave's claim? Answer: Here we have made the legatee the claimant, not the slave; the legatee is the opponent of the heir, and the claim is from his side, so he may bring evidence.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning a dispute between a legatee (who claims an emancipation occurred in health) and the heir (who claims it occurred in death-illness). The text first explains the translation of the matn: the testator's emancipation in health takes effect from the entire estate, while if it occurs in death-illness, it is a will and limited to one-third. The heir denies the legatee's claim, so the heir becomes the denier (munkir), and his statement is accepted with oath. The commentary then provides a second reason: because emancipation is an event, and based on the legal principle that events are attributed to the nearest certain time, the apparent state (that it happened in death-illness) supports the heir. The heir's statement is thus accepted unless there is a surplus from the one-third (which goes to the legatee without dispute) or the legatee brings evidence (bayyinah) that the emancipation was in health, in which case the legatee's claim prevails. The passage then addresses a question: since Imam Abu Hanifa considers emancipation a right of the slave, why can the legatee bring evidence? The answer clarifies that in this case, the legatee is the claimant, not the slave, and he is the proper opponent to the heir; therefore, he may bring evidence to prove his claim.

Key Terms
موصی (mūṣī): The testator who makes a will; in this context, the person who emancipates a slave.
موصی لہ (mūṣā lahu): The legatee; the person in whose favor the will is made, here the legatee claiming benefit from emancipation.
عتق (‘itq): Emancipation of a slave, which can be a will or a direct act.
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence, typically through two male witnesses or one male and two females in financial matters.

D) The testator's intention is presumed to favor the heir.

Key Takeaway
The heir's statement is accepted in a dispute over emancipation timing because events are attributed to the nearest certain time, making the heir the denier whose word is taken with oath unless evidence contradicts.

Slave Emancipation and Debt: The Dispute on Work for Value
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether slave must work for value when heir affirms both emancipation in health and debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn regarding whether a slave must work for his value when an heir affirms both emancipation in health and a debt.

Core Idea
When emancipation and debt appear together by one affirmation, freedom is given but work for value is disputed.

This lesson examines a specific case where a testator leaves only a slave as his estate. The slave claims emancipation in health, and a creditor claims a debt. The heir affirms both. All Hanafi jurists agree the slave is free, but they differ on whether the slave must work to pay his value to the creditor. This intra-madhhab dispute illustrates how different interpretations of the same facts lead to different legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case facts
Read the passage carefully. Note that the testator leaves only a slave. The slave claims emancipation in health, and a creditor claims a debt. The heir affirms both claims in one statement.
The key is that both claims are affirmed simultaneously by the same person.
2
State the agreed ruling
All three imams agree that the slave is free. The dispute is only about whether the slave must work (sa'ya) to pay his value.
Freedom is not contested.
3
State Abu Hanifah's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifah holds that the slave must work for his value. His reasoning is based on the priority of debt: since the emancipation and debt both arise, and the slave is the only asset, the debt must be paid first, so the slave works to pay it.
Abu Hanifah requires sa'ya.
4
State the Sahibayn's position and reasoning
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the slave is free and does not need to work. Their reasoning: both emancipation and debt emerged from the same affirmation, so they are simultaneous. Emancipation in health does not require compensation even if there were debts.
Sahibayn say no sa'ya.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifah, the slave must work to pay the debt. Under the Sahibayn, the slave is free and the creditor has no recourse against the slave. The later relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Sahibayn's view.
The difference affects whether the creditor can collect from the slave.

Source Text

The ruling concerning the slave who claims emancipation and the man who claims a debt, and the heir affirms both - statements of the jurists. He (Muhammad) said: And whoever left a slave, and the slave said to the heir, 'Your father emancipated me in health,' and a man said, 'I have a thousand dirhams against your father,' and he (the heir) said, 'You both have spoken truthfully,' then the slave must work for his value according to Abu Hanifah, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He is free and does not work for anything, because the debt and the emancipation in health both appeared together by the heir's affirmation in one statement, so it is as if they were simultaneous, and emancipation in health does not require compensation even if there is debt on the emancipator. Translation: He said: And whoever leaves a slave, and the slave says to the heir that his father emancipated him in health, and a man says that the father owed a thousand dirhams, and the heir affirms both, then according to Abu Hanifah the slave must work for his value, but the two (Sahibayn) say he is free and owes nothing because the debt and emancipation appeared together by the heir's single affirmation. Explanation: Zayd died leaving only a slave. The slave claims emancipation in health, and another person claims a debt of a thousand dirhams. The heir affirms both. All agree the slave is free, but differ on whether he must work for his value. Abu Hanifah says he must work; the Sahibayn say not, because both obligations emerged simultaneously from the heir's affirmation, so emancipation in health (which does not require compensation) prevails.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) over a specific case. The case: A testator dies leaving only a slave as his estate. The slave claims the testator emancipated him in health. Another person claims the testator owed him a thousand dirhams. The heir affirms both claims (i.e., confirms the emancipation and the debt). All jurists agree that the slave is free because the heir's affirmation validates the emancipation. The dispute is whether the slave must then work (sa'ya) to pay his value (i.e., to cover the debt that competes with the emancipation). Imam Abu Hanifah holds that the slave must work for his value because the emancipation and debt are both established by the heir's testimony; since the slave is the only asset, the debt takes priority, but the emancipation is also effective, so the slave works to pay the debt. The Sahibayn argue that since both the emancipation and debt emerged simultaneously from the same statement, it is as if they existed together; and a valid emancipation in health does not require the slave to compensate even if the testator had debts. Therefore, the slave is free without any work obligation. The commentary explains the reasoning: the Sahibayn rely on the principle that emancipation in health takes effect fully and does not create a lien (sa'ya) on the slave, regardless of debts.

Key Terms
سعایہ (sa‘āyah): Work or effort required from a slave to earn money to pay his value (qīmah) when emancipated in a contested situation.
صاحبین (ṣāḥibayn): The two companions: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the chief disciples of Abu Hanifah.
دین (dayn): Debt owed by the testator, which competes with other claims on the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the slave is not a legal person
B) Because emancipation in health and debt emerged simultaneously, and emancipation in health does not require compensation
C) Because the heir's affirmation is invalid
D) Because the creditor did not present evidence

Key Takeaway
In an intra-Hanafi dispute, both Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn agree on the slave's freedom but differ on the obligation to work; the later preferred view is that of the Sahibayn, with no work required.

The Definition of Neighbors in a Will: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the definition of 'neighbor' in a will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on who qualifies as a 'neighbor' in a will, differentiate the qiyas and istihsan reasoning, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa restricts 'neighbor' to the adjacent; the Sahibayn expand it using istihsan — custom overrides strict analogy.

When a testator makes a will for 'my neighbors,' the meaning of 'neighbor' becomes critical. Imam Abu Hanifa applies strict linguistic qiyas: only those whose properties physically adjoin the testator's property. His disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, use istihsan to include all residents of the same mahallah who attend the same mosque. This passage from Al-Hidayah presents both arguments. Understanding this dispute illustrates how Hanafi jurists balance literal texts with customary practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The dispute is about the definition of 'neighbor' (jar) in a will made for neighbors. The testator's intention is fixed, but the legal interpretation of the term determines who benefits.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof (qiyas)
Abu Hanifa limits 'neighbor' to those whose properties are physically adjacent (mulasiqun). His proof is qiyas: the literal meaning of 'jar' is adjacency, and by analogy with shuf'ah (pre-emption) which requires adjacency.
This is a clear example of qiyas jali (manifest analogy).
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof (istihsan)
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad expand the definition to include not only adjacent owners but also all residents of the same mahallah (neighborhood) who are gathered by the same mosque. Their proof is istihsan: common usage of 'neighbor' is broader than literal adjacency.
Istihsan here overrides the strict qiyas due to widespread customary practice.
4
Analyze the qiyas panel
Trace the qiyas: the asl is the literal meaning of 'jar', the hukm of the asl is that it refers to the adjacent person, the far' is the will scenario, and the illa is adjacency. Note the Sahibayn's objection: common usage contradicts this illa.
The objection leads to the istihsan override.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its rationale
The text indicates that the Sahibayn's view is istihsan and is preferred in practice. Later Hanafi fatwa relies on the broader definition because it aligns with custom and fulfills the testator's presumed intention.
Tarjih authority: The passage states 'this is istihsan' implying preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن أوصى لجيرانه فهم الملاصقون عند أبي حنيفة وقالا هم الملاصقون وغيرهم ممن يسكن محلة الموصى ويجمعهم مسجد المحلة وهذا استحسان وقوله قياس لان الجار من المجاورة وهى الملاصقة حقيقة ولهذا يستحق الشفعة بهذا الجوار ولانه لما تعذر صرفه الى الجميع يصرف الى أخص الخصوص وهو الملاصق
He (al-Quduri) said: And whoever makes a will for his neighbors, then they are the adjacent ones (al-mulasiqun) according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: They are the adjacent ones and others besides them from among those who reside in the mahallah of the testator and whom the mosque of the mahallah gathers together. And this is istihsan. And his saying (Abu Hanifa's) is qiyas, because 'neighbor' (al-jar) is derived from proximity (al-mujawara), and it is literally adjacency. For this reason, pre-emption is established by this adjacency. And because when it is impossible to distribute to all (people), it is distributed to the most specific of the specific, which is the adjacent one.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage addresses the definition of 'neighbors' (jiran) when a person makes a will in favor of his neighbors. The ruling is from the Book of Wills. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that only those whose properties are physically adjacent (mulasiq) to the testator's property qualify. This is based on qiyas: the literal meaning of 'neighbor' is adjacency, and pre-emption (shuf'ah) rights are also linked to this type of adjacency. The Sahibayn, using istihsan, expand the definition to include not only adjacent owners but also other residents of the same mahallah (neighborhood) who attend the same mosque. This is istihsan because the term 'neighbor' in common usage is broader. Abu Hanifa's position is strict qiyas; the Sahibayn's is istihsan. The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa's view, fewer people benefit; under Sahibayn, more. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is often the Sahibayn's due to customary understanding.

Key Terms
ملاصقون (mulasiqun): Those whose properties share a common boundary with the testator's property; physically adjacent.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that allows departing from strict analogy for a more equitable ruling based on custom or need.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Only those whose property is physically adjacent
C) All residents of the same mahallah
D) Anyone who attends the same mosque

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the definition of 'neighbor' in a will is resolved by preferring the customary interpretation (istihsan) over strict linguistic analogy (qiyas), expanding the beneficiaries to those sharing the same mosque and mahallah.

Dispute over the Meaning of 'Jiran' in a Bequest
Intra-Hanafi dispute on interpreting 'jiran' in bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the interpretation of 'jiran' in a bequest and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When a bequest is made to 'neighbors', the Sahibayn include all who share the testator's locality and mosque, overriding Abu Hanifa's adjacency-only qiyas.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a classical intra-Hanafi dispute on the meaning of 'jiran' (neighbors) in a bequest. While all agree only house neighbors (jar dar) are meant, they differ on whether it includes only physically adjacent houses or also those in the same neighborhood and mosque. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) use istihsan based on custom and a hadith, while Abu Hanifa relies on qiyas from the word's derivation and analogy with shuf'a. Understanding this dispute teaches you how Hanafi scholars balance linguistic derivation, analogy, and juristic preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of neighbors
Recognize the three categories of 'jar' mentioned: jar qarabat (relative), jar ard (land), jar dar (house). Understand that all agree only jar dar is intended in the bequest.
This classification narrows the dispute to the interpretation of jar dar.
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's qiyas
Trace his argument: 'jar' derives from 'mujawara' meaning physical adjacency, so the true neighbor is the adjacent one. Also, shuf'a only applies to adjacent neighbors, so by analogy the bequest should be limited to them. When not all neighbors can be covered, the most specific (akhass al-khusus) must be taken, i.e., the adjacent neighbor.
Abu Hanifa uses linguistic derivation and legal analogy.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's istihsan
Identify their argument: custom ('urf) calls all residents of a neighborhood and mosque attendees 'neighbors'. The hadith 'لا صلوة لجار المسجد الا في المسجد' is interpreted broadly by 'Ali to include all who hear the call. The purpose of the bequest is general goodwill, which includes non-adjacent neighbors, provided there is mixing (ikhtilat) through shared mosque.
Istihsan overrides qiyas based on custom and hadith.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, only those with physically attached houses receive; under Sahibayn, all who live in the same locality and share the same mosque are included.
This directly affects the distribution of the bequest.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Note that the text presents the Sahibayn's view as the stronger proof, and later Hanafi fatwa relies on this position. The relied-upon view is that of the Sahibayn.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's istihsan-based opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۶ اور ابوحنیفہ کا قول قیاس ہے اس لئے کہ جار مجاورت سے مشتق ہے اور مجاورت حقیقت میں ملاصقت ہے اس وجہ سے جار اس پڑوس کی وجہ سے شفعہ کا مستحق ہوتا ہے اور اس لئے کہ جب وصیت تمام پڑوسیوں کی طرف پھیرنا متعذر ہے تو اس کو اخص الخصوص کی جانب پھیر دیا جائے گا اور اخص الخصوص جار ملاصق ہے۔ تشریح زید نے یہ وصیت کی کہ میرے مال کا ثلث میرے پڑوسیوں کیلئے ہے تو اس سے کون سا پڑوسی مراد ہوگا، کیونکہ پڑوسی کئی قسم کے ہوتے ہیں ایک جار قرابت ، جس سے قرابت کا پڑوس ہو ۔ اور دوسرا جار ارض یعنی زمین کا پڑوسی اور تیسرا اجار دار، یعنی گھر کا پڑوسی ، اور یہاں بالاتفاق جار سے مراد جار قرابت اور جار ارض نہیں ہے البتہ جار دار مراد ہے۔ پھر اس کی تفسیر میں اختلاف ہے، تو امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ جیران سے مراد وہ پڑوسی ہیں جن کا گھر موصی کے گھر سے متصل اور ملاصق ہوان کے دروازے قریب ہوں یا دور ہوں ۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ جیران سے ملاصقین بھی ہیں اور ساتھ ہی وہ لوگ بھی اس میں داخل ہیں جو موصی کے محلہ میں رہتے ہیں اور جو موصی کی مسجد کے نمازی ہیں۔ صاحبین کا قول استحسان ہے اور امام ابو حنیفہ کا قیاس ہے، قیاس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جار مجاورت سے مشتق ہے اور مجاورت حقیقیہ ملاحقت کو کہتے ہیں ، لہذا جن کا گھر موصی کے گھر سے متصل ہے انھیں کے واسطے وصیت ہوگی اور جار ملاصق بھی پڑوس کی وجہ سے شفعہ کا مستحق ہوتا ہے لوگ مستحق شفعہ نہ ہوں گے۔ اور دوسری وجہ یہ بھی ہے کہ تمام جیران کی طرف وصیت کو پھیر نا مستعد رہے کیونکہ جار قرابت اور جار ارض اس میں داخل نہیں ہیں بلکہ اس میں تخصیص کی گئی ہے تو اس کو احسن الخصوص کی طرف پھیرا جائے گا اور اخص الخصوص جار ملاصق ہے۔
استحسانی دلیل
وجه الاستحسان أن هؤلاء كلهم يسمون جيرانا عرفا وقد تايد بقوله لا صلوة لجار المسجد الافي المسجد و قسره بكل من سمع النداء ولان المقصد برا لجيران واستحبابه ينتظم الملاصق وغيره الا انه لا بد من الاختلاط و ذالك عند اتحاد المسجد
ترجمہ استحسان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ تمام لوگ عرفاً پڑوسی کہلاتے ہیں اور رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فرمان سے اس کی تائید ہوتی ہے کہ مسجد کے پڑوسی کی نماز نہیں ہوتی مگر مسجد میں اور عصر علی نے ) اس کی تفسیر کی ہے ہر اس شخص کے ساتھ جو اذان کو سنے اور اس لئے کہ وصیت کا مقصد پڑوسیوں کے ساتھ بھلائی کرنا ہے اور اس کا استباب ملاصق اور غیر ملاصق دونوں کو شامل ہے مگر اختلاط ضروری ہے اور اختلاط مسجد کے اتحاد کے وقت ہو گا۔
تشریح یہ استحسان کی دلیل ہے کہ عرف میں ان تمام لوگوں کو جو ایک محلہ میں رہتے ہیں اور ایک مسجد کے نمازی ہیں پڑوسی کہا جاتا ہے، اور ایک حدیث سے اس کی تائید ہوتی ہے، حدیث میں ہے، لا صلوة لجار المسجد الا في المسجد ، یعنی مسجد کے پڑوسی کی نماز مسجد ہی میں ہوگی تو یہاں مسجد کے پڑوی وہ شخص مراد نہیں ہے جس کا گھر مسجد سے متصل ہے بلکہ ہر وہ شخص مراد ہے جو بھی مسجد کی اذان کو سنتا ہے اور حضرت علی سے اس کی یہی تفسیر منقول ہے نیز موصی کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ اپنے پڑوسی کے ساتھ بھلائی کرے اور یہ امر مستحب ہے لیکن بھلائی کا یہ استحباب فقط ملاصق ہی کے لئے مخصوص نہیں ہے بلکہ ملاصق اور غیر ملاصق دونوں کو شامل ہے لیکن موصی اور موصی لہ میں کچھ نہ کچھ تو اختلاط ہونا چاہئے تو اتحاد مسجد کی وجہ سے اختلاط متحقق ہے۔
Book of Bequests. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary Hidaya vol. 16. And Abu Hanifa's opinion is qiyas because 'jar' is derived from 'mujawara' and mujawara in reality is physical adjacency, so a neighbor is entitled to shuf'a due to this neighborhood, and because when it is impossible to turn the bequest to all neighbors, it is turned to the most specific of the specific, and the most specific of the specific is the adjacent neighbor. Explanation: Zaid made a bequest that one-third of his property is for his neighbors, so which neighbor is meant? Because there are several types of neighbors: one is jar qarabat (relative neighbor), second is jar ard (land neighbor), third is jar dar (house neighbor). Here by agreement, jar qarabat and jar ard are not meant, rather jar dar is meant. Then there is difference in its interpretation. Imam Abu Hanifa said that 'jiran' means those whose house is attached and adjacent to the testator's house, whether their doors are near or far. And the Sahibayn said that 'jiran' includes the adjacent ones as well as those who live in the testator's neighborhood and those who pray in his mosque. The Sahibayn's opinion is istihsan and Abu Hanifa's is qiyas. The proof of qiyas: 'jar' is derived from 'mujawara' and real mujawara is physical adjacency, therefore the bequest will be only for those whose house is adjacent to the testator's house, and the adjacent neighbor is entitled to shuf'a due to neighborhood, but others are not entitled to shuf'a. The second reason: Turning the bequest to all neighbors is not possible because jar qarabat and jar ard are not included in it, rather specification has been made, so it will be turned to the most specific of the specific, and the most specific is the adjacent neighbor. Proof of istihsan: The proof of istihsan: That all these are called neighbors customarily, and it is supported by his saying: 'There is no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque' and he interpreted it with everyone who hears the call, and because the purpose of the bequest is goodness to neighbors and its recommendation includes both adjacent and non-adjacent, except that there must be mixing, and that is when there is unity of mosque. Translation: The proof of istihsan is that all these people are customarily called neighbors, and this is supported by the command of the Messenger (peace be upon him) that the neighbor of the mosque's prayer is not valid except in the mosque, and 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) interpreted it as every person who hears the call, and because the purpose of the bequest is to do good to neighbors, and its recommendation includes both adjacent and non-adjacent, but mixing is necessary, and mixing occurs when the mosque is the same. Explanation: This is the proof of istihsan: that customarily all these people who live in one neighborhood and pray in one mosque are called neighbors, and a hadith supports this. The hadith says: 'لا صلوة لجار المسجد الا في المسجد' i.e., the prayer of the neighbor of the mosque is only in the mosque. So here the neighbor of the mosque does not mean the person whose house is adjacent to the mosque, but rather every person who hears the call to prayer from the mosque. And this interpretation is transmitted from 'Ali. Also the testator's purpose is to do good to his neighbor, and this is a recommended act, but this recommendation is not specific only to the adjacent neighbor, but includes both adjacent and non-adjacent. However, there must be some mixing between the testator and the beneficiary, and this mixing is realized through sharing the same mosque.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the interpretation of 'jiran' (neighbors) in a bequest. The author first identifies three types of neighbors: jar qarabat (relative), jar ard (land neighbor), and jar dar (house neighbor). By agreement, only jar dar is intended. Then the dispute arises: Imam Abu Hanifa restricts 'jiran' to those whose house is physically adjacent (mulasiq) to the testator's house, regardless of door proximity. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) extend it to include all residents of the same neighborhood and mosque. The author explains that Abu Hanifa's position is based on qiyas: the word 'jar' is derived from 'mujawara' which means physical adjacency, and also by analogy to shuf'a (pre-emption) which only applies to adjacent neighbors. The Sahibayn's position is based on istihsan: custom ('urf) considers all such people as neighbors, and the hadith 'لا صلوة لجار المسجد الا في المسجد' supports this broader interpretation, as explained by 'Ali that 'neighbor of the mosque' includes all who hear the call. The purpose of the bequest is general goodwill, and sharing a mosque provides sufficient mixing (ikhtilat) to include non-adjacent neighbors. The text thus follows the classical Hanafi method of presenting the proof for each position, with the Sahibayn's view being the mufta bihi in later fatwa, though Abu Hanifa's is the qiyas.

Key Terms
جار (jar): In this passage, 'jar' is analyzed linguistically as derived from 'mujawara' (neighboring, physical adjacency). It is used in three types: jar qarabat (relative), jar ard (land), jar dar (house). The dispute focuses on jar dar.
ملاصق (mulasiq): Physically adjacent or touching. Abu Hanifa requires the neighbor's house to be mulasiq (attached) to the testator's house.
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that overrides qiyas in favor of a stronger evidence or custom. Here, Sahibayn use istihsan based on 'urf and hadith to include non-adjacent neighbors.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning. Abu Hanifa uses qiyas by deriving from the meaning of 'jar' and analogy with shuf'a.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), who is included as a 'jar' in a bequest to neighbors?
A) Only those whose house is attached to the testator's house
B) Only relatives living nearby
C) Both adjacent neighbors and those in the same neighborhood who attend the same mosque
D) Only those who own property adjacent to the testator

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi position on bequests to neighbors is the Sahibayn's istihsan-based view, which includes all who share the testator's locality and mosque.

Neighbor Extent and Slave Inclusion: Hanafi vs Shafi'i and Sahibayn
Refutation of Shafi'i and intra-Hanafi clarification on slave inclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i's 40-house neighbor limit and apply the mufta bihi ruling on slave inclusion in a bequest to neighbors.

Core Idea
Shafi'i's 40-house neighbor hadith is weak; Hanafi custom-based neighbor range and Sahibayn's slave exclusion are mufta bihi.

This passage continues the discussion on bequests to neighbors from the previous lesson. Here, the author refutes Imam al-Shafi'i's claim that neighborhood extends to forty houses, deeming the supporting hadith weak and the view far from qiyas. Then, an intra-Hanafi dispute is presented: whether a resident slave is included in the term 'jar.' Imam Abu Hanifa includes the slave due to the absolute nature of the word, while the Sahibayn exclude him because the bequest would effectively go to his non-resident master. The passage sharpens our understanding of how Hanafi scholars evaluate evidence and prioritize rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i claim and its Hanafi refutation
Find the statement attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i about the extent of neighborhood. Then locate the author's critique: why is it far-fetched and what is wrong with the hadith?
The author does not repeat the full hadith; he simply declares it weak.
2
Extract the Hanafi consensus on who qualifies as a neighbor
The passage states that the term 'jar' includes both resident and owner, male and female, Muslim and dhimmi. Confirm that this is the agreed Hanafi position.
This part is not disputed among the Hanafis.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on the resident slave
Identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa includes the slave because the word 'jar' is absolute (mujmal/absolute); Sahibayn exclude because the bequest would go to the master who is not a neighbor. Note the reasoning behind each.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view, as the author signals.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Compare the outcomes: under Abu Hanifa, the slave receives; under Sahibayn, the slave does not receive and the bequest for that share is ineffective. Also contrast with Shafi'i: if his view were taken, neighbors up to 40 houses would be included.

Source Text

پڑوسی کے بارے میں امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
وما قاله الشافعى الجوار الى اربعين دار ابعيد وما يروى فيه ضعيف قالو او يستوى فيه الساکن و المالك والذكر والانثى والمسلم والدمى لان اسم الجاريتنا ولهم ويدخل فيه العبد الساکن عنده لا طلاقه ولا يدخل ما لان لـ الوصية له وصية لمولاه وهو لاد وهو غير ماکن
ترجمہ اور جو بات کی شافعی نے فرمائی ہے کہ پڑوس چالیس ۴۰ گھروں تک ہے یہ بات بعید ہے اور اس میں جو حدیث روایت کی جاتی ہے وہ ضعیف ہے مشائخ نے فرمایا ہے اور اس میں ساکن اور مالک اور مرد اور عورت اور مسلم اور ڈمی سب برابر ہیں اس لئے کہ لفظ جاران تمام کو شامل ہے اور اس میں ساکن غلام داخل ہے ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جار کے مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک داخل نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ غلام کے لئے وصیت ہو گی حالانکہ آقا سا کن نہیں ہے۔ تشریح امام شافعی نے فرماتے ہیں کہ پڑوس چالیس گھروں تک ہے یعنی ہر سمت سے دس دس گھر تک ، اور یہ حدیث بھی ہے جس سے امام شافعی نے استدلال کیا ہے ، تو اس کے بارے میں مصنف نے فرمایا کہ امام شافعی کی یہ بات بعید از قیاس ہے اور جو حد بیث انہوں نے پیش کی ہے یہ حدیث ضعیف ہے۔ پھر علی اختلاف القولین جار میں خواہ وہ ہو جو اس مکان یا محلہ میں مالکانہ حیثیت سے رہتا ہو یا وہ ہو جو عاریت وغیرہ کے طریقہ پر رہتا ہو اور خواہ مرد ہو یا عورت ہو اور خواہ مسلمان ہو یا ڈمی ہو اس لئے کہ لفظ جار میں یہ سب داخل ہیں۔ اور اگر کوئی غلام رہتا ہو اور اس کا گھر موصی کے گھر سے ملاصق ہو تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک وہ غلام بھی وصیت میں داخل ہوگا اس لئے کہ جار کے اطلاق میں غلام بھی داخل ہے، اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ غلام ساکن جار کے اندر داخل ہوگا اور وہ وصیت کا حقدار نہ ہوگا کیوں کہ اگر غلام کے لئے وصیت کو جائز مان لیا جائے تو یہ وصیت اس کے آقا کیلئے ہو جائے گی حالانکہ یہاں نہیں رہتا اور نہ وہ موصی کا پڑوی ہے۔
Imam Shafi'i's point of view regarding the neighbor. And what al-Shafi'i said: 'Neighborhood extends to forty houses' is far-fetched, and the hadith reported in this regard is weak. They said: It is equal in it the resident and the owner, the male and the female, the Muslim and the dhimmi, because the noun 'jar' includes them all. And it includes the resident slave with him due to its absoluteness, but it does not include... because the bequest for a slave is a bequest for his master, and he is not residing. Translation: And what Shafi'i said that neighborhood extends to forty houses is far-fetched, and the hadith narrated in this regard is weak. The scholars (masha'ikh) said: In this, the resident and the owner, male and female, Muslim and dhimmi are all equal, because the word 'jiran' includes all. And the resident slave is included according to Abu Hanifa due to the absoluteness of 'jar', but according to the Sahibayn he is not included because the bequest for the slave would be for the master, while the master is not a resident. Explanation: Imam Shafi'i says that neighborhood extends to forty houses, i.e., ten houses in each direction, and there is a hadith that Imam Shafi'i used as evidence. The author says that Shafi'i's statement is far from analogy (qiyas) and the hadith he presented is weak. Then, according to the two opinions (i.e., Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn), the term 'jar' includes whoever resides in that house or locality as an owner or on loan, etc., whether male or female, Muslim or dhimmi, because the word 'jar' includes all. And if a slave lives there and his house is adjacent to the testator's house, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa that slave will be included in the bequest because the absolute term 'jar' includes the slave, but the Sahibayn say that the resident slave will not be included in 'jar' and he will not be entitled to the bequest because if the bequest for the slave is allowed, it would become a bequest for his master, who is not residing and is not a neighbor of the testator.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues: first, Imam Shafi'i's claim that neighborhood extends to forty houses in all directions (up to 40 houses). The author (presumably al-Hidayah or its commentator) dismisses this as far-fetched and states the supporting hadith is weak. The Hanafi position does not define a specific number but relies on custom and the mosque connection as previously discussed. Second, the passage discusses whether a slave who is a resident neighbor is included in a bequest to neighbors. Under Imam Abu Hanifa's view, the absolute term 'jar' includes a resident slave, so the slave benefits. Under Sahibayn, the slave is not included because the bequest would actually go to the master, who is not a resident neighbor. This is a practical difference: if the testator bequeaths to neighbors, a slave living next door would receive under Abu Hanifa, but under Sahibayn the master would not receive (since he doesn't live there) and the slave cannot own property, so the bequest would be invalid for that portion. The passage thus shows both a refutation of Shafi'i and an intra-Hanafi clarification. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the view of Sahibayn that a slave is not included.

Key Terms
جار ساکن (jar sākin): A resident neighbor, whether owner or tenant, who lives in the house adjacent to the testator.
عبد ساکن (abd sākin): A slave who resides in a house adjacent to the testator. The dispute is whether he is included in 'jar'.
بعید از قیاس (ba'id an al-qiyas): Far from analogy; a ruling that does not follow standard analogical reasoning and is thus rejected.
ضعیف (da'if): Weak (hadith terminology); a hadith that does not meet the criteria for authentication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the word 'jar' does not include slaves in Arabic usage.
B) Because the bequest would go to the slave's master, who is not a resident neighbor.
C) Because slaves are not considered legal persons in Islamic law.
D) Because the bequest would be invalid due to uncertainty.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects Shafi'i's 40-house neighbor range as unsupported and holds that a resident slave is not included in a bequest to neighbors because the benefit would go to a non-resident master.

Defining As-har (In-laws) for Bequests
Ruling with proof defining the beneficiaries of a bequest to in-laws.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify who qualifies as an 'as-har' (in-law) for the purpose of a bequest and apply the Hanafi definition based on the prophetic precedent.

Core Idea
As-har are the wife's mahram relatives, not all in-laws.

This passage from al-Quduri clarifies a key term in bequest law. When someone leaves a will to their 'as-har', it is not a vague category. The Hanafi school, following Muhammad al-Shaybani and Abu 'Ubaydah, defines as-har specifically as the mahram relatives of the testator's wife. The proof comes from the Prophet's marriage to Safiyyah, where he freed her mahram relatives and called them his as-har.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the key term
The passage states that a bequest to as-har is for every mahram relative of the testator's wife. Note the term 'dhū rahim muhram' (mahram relative).
Mahram means permanently forbidden to marry.
2
Examine the proof
The Prophet freed Safiyyah's mahram relatives after marrying her, and they were called his as-har. This shows that a husband's as-har are his wife's mahram relatives.
The hadith is a Prophetic action (fi'l), which is a source of law.
3
Understand the scope
Only mahram relatives of the wife are included. Non-mahram relatives (e.g., wife's sister) are excluded from the bequest.
Mahram includes father, brother, son, uncle, etc. from the wife's side.
4
Note the authority
This interpretation is attributed to Muhammad al-Shaybani and Abu 'Ubaydah, making it the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school.
Other scholars may have differing views, but this is the chosen view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصہار کا مصداق اول
قال ومن اوصى لا صهاره فالوصية لكل ذى رحم محرم من امراته لماروى ان النبي عليه السلام لما تزوج صفية اعتق كل من ملك من ذى رحم محرم منها اكراما لها وكانوا يسمون اصهار النبي عليه السلام وهذا التفسير اختيار محمد و ابي عبيدة
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے اپنے اصہار کے لئے وصیت کی تو وصیت اس کی بیوی کے ہر ذی رحم محرم کے لئے ہوگی بوجہ اس کے کہ مروی ہے کہ نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جب صفیہ سے نکاح کیا تو ہر اس شخص نے آزاد کر دیا تھا جو ان کے ذی رحم محرم کا مالک تھا صفیہ کے اکرام کے لئے اور وہ اصہار نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم کہلاتے تھے۔ اور یہ تفسیر محمد اور ابو عبیدہ کا انتخاب ہے۔
First meaning of in-laws (as-har). He (al-Quduri) said: And whoever makes a bequest to his as-har, the bequest is for every mahram relative of his wife, because it is narrated that when the Prophet (peace be upon him) married Safiyyah, he freed every person who owned any mahram relative of hers, as an honor to her, and they were called the as-har of the Prophet (peace be upon him). And this interpretation is the choice of Muhammad and Abu 'Ubaydah. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And whoever makes a bequest to his as-har, the bequest will be for every mahram relative of his wife, due to the narration that when the Prophet (peace be upon him) married Safiyyah, he freed every person who owned a mahram relative of hers, to honor her, and they were called the as-har of the Prophet. And this interpretation is the choice of Muhammad and Abu 'Ubaydah.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'as-har' (in-laws) in the context of a bequest. The ruling from al-Quduri states that if someone bequeaths to his as-har, the beneficiaries are all mahram relatives of his wife (i.e., those who are permanently unmarriageable to her, such as her father, brother, son, uncle, etc.). The proof is the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) when he married Safiyyah bint Huyayy: he freed all the captives who were mahram relatives of hers, and these were referred to as his as-har. This indicates that 'as-har' includes the wife's mahram relatives. The interpretation is attributed to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Abu 'Ubaydah (a renowned early scholar). It is not mentioned here whether this is the only view or if there is dispute; the text presents it as the authoritative interpretation. The bequest will be distributed among these mahram relatives (who are also defined as dhawi arham, but with the condition of being mahram) according to their shares or equally if not specified. This lesson is a straightforward definition and ruling with a naqli proof from the Prophetic practice.

Key Terms
أصهار (as-hār): In-laws. Specifically, the wife's mahram relatives (those with whom marriage is permanently forbidden).
ذو رحم محرم (dhū rahim muhram): A mahram relative via blood (nasab) or marriage (sihr) with whom marriage is permanently prohibited. Here specifically referring to the wife's mahram relatives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who are the beneficiaries of a bequest made to 'as-har' (in-laws) according to this passage?
A) All relatives of the testator's wife, including non-mahram
B) Only the testator's father-in-law and mother-in-law
C) The testator's wife's mahram relatives only
D) The testator's own relatives by blood

Key Takeaway
As-har in Hanafi fiqh are specifically the mahram relatives of the testator's wife, as demonstrated by the Prophet's freeing of Safiyyah's mahram relatives.

Definition of Aqarib in Bequests: Hanafi, Sahibayn, and Shafi'i Views
Defines aqarib for wills with three scholarly positions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of aqarib in bequests, identify the linguistic and Quranic evidence used to exclude parents and children, and compare the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Imam al-Shafi'i with their practical consequences.

Core Idea
In bequests, 'aqarib' excludes parents and children because linguistic custom and Quranic conjunction treat them as separate categories.

When a testator leaves a bequest to his 'aqarib' (relatives), who exactly qualifies? This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya presents a key inter-madhhab dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa defines aqarib narrowly — only relatives through an intermediary, excluding direct ancestors and descendants. The Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i adopt broader definitions. Understanding this difference is crucial for executing bequests correctly and respecting the testator's intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position and its linguistic basis
State Abu Hanifa's definition of 'aqarib' as relatives through an intermediary, not direct. Note that calling one's father 'qarib' is considered disobedience because the father-child relationship is direct, not mediated.
Linguistic custom ('urf lughawi) is a key tool in Hanafi usul.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence (al-Baqarah 2:180)
The verse places 'parents' and 'near relatives' side by side with a conjunction ('wa'). In Arabic, this normally indicates separation — parents are not included in 'aqrabin'. This is the core dalil for excluding parents and, by analogy, children.
The dalala of this conjunction is zanni, but combined with linguistic custom it carries strong weight.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (Sahibayn)
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani define 'aqarib' as all descendants of the last father in Islam. Their position is broader than Abu Hanifa's but still excludes direct lineage (parents and children) based on the same verse.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; the mufta bihi position may depend on the context.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i defines 'aqarib' as descendants of the nearest father (i.e., the testator's immediate paternal ancestor). This is narrower than the Sahibayn but still includes more than Abu Hanifa's.
The Shafi'i position relies more on the apparent meaning of the term.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In practice, if a testator leaves a bequest to 'aqarib', under Abu Hanifa only indirect relatives (e.g., cousins once removed) benefit; under the Sahibayn all descendants of the testator's last Muslim ancestor share; under Shafi'i only descendants of his nearest paternal ancestor share.
The difference can be significant in large families.

اور جس نے اپنے والد کا نام قریب رکھا تو یہ نام رکھنا اس کی جانب سے نافرمانی ہوگا اور یہ اس لئے کہ قریب عرف لسانی میں وہ شخص ہے جو اپنے غیر کی جانب اپنے غیر کے وسیلہ سے قرابت رکھے اور والد اور اولاد کی قرابت بذات خود ہوتی ہے اور ظاہر لفظ کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جائے گا اجماع کے منعقد ہونے کے بعد ظاہر کے چھوڑنے پر پس ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اقرباء مقدر ہوں گے اس طریقہ کے ساتھ جس کو ہم نے ذکر کر دیا ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اسلام کے اندر آخری باپ کے ساتھ اور شافعی کے نزدیک قریبی باپ کے ساتھ۔
تشریح نیز امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ شریعت نے صلہ رحمی کا حکم دیا ہے اور قطع رحمی سے منع کیا ہے اور قطع رحمی کرنے والوں کے متعلق وعید شدید وارد ہوئی ہے ، تو موصی کا مقصد اقرباء کے لئے وصیت کرنے سے یہ ہے کہ زندگی کے اندر صلہ رحمی کے سلسلہ میں جو کوتا ہی اس سے ہوئی ہے اس کی تلافی ہو سکے، اور صلہ رحی ذور تم محرم [؟] کے ساتھ واجب ہے اور وں [؟] کے ساتھ نہیں ، یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر ذور تم محرم تنگدست ہو تو اس پر ان کا نفقہ واجب ہے اور جو ذور تم محرم نہ ہو اس کا نفقہ اس پر واجب نہیں ہے۔
اور والدین اور اولادا قرباء میں داخل نہیں ہیں لہذاوہ اس وصیت کے اندر بھی داخل نہ ہوں گے۔
کیونکہ ارشاد باری ہے الوصية للوالدين والا قربين بالمعروف حقاً على المتقين تواقر بین کے والدین پر عطف کرنے سے یہ بات واضح ہو گئی کہ اقر بین میں والدین داخل نہیں ہیں اور جب اقر بین سے والدین خارج ہو گئے تو اولا د بھی خارج ہو جائے گی لہذا ان دونوں کو قریب نہیں کہا جائے گا۔ اور جو اپنے باپ کو قریب کہے تو وہ نافرمان اور عساق [؟] کہلاتا ہے جیسے بعض احمقوں کا طریقہ ہوتا ہے کہ وہ معمولی سا کوئی عہدہ پا کر باپ کو باپ کہنے سے شرماتے ہیں اور یوں کہتے ہیں کہ یہ ہمارے قریبی ہیں۔ نیز امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ بھی ہے کہ عرف لسانی میں قریب اس کو کہتے ہیں جس کے قرابت کے غیر کے واسطہ سے ہو اور والدین اور اولاد کی قرابت بلا واسطہ ہوتی ہے۔
سوال ... اقرباء میں بظاہر تمام قریبی لوگ داخل ہیں تو الا قرب فالاقرب کے قاعدہ سے قرابت کے باوجود ان کو خارج کرنا لازم آتا ہے؟
جواب پھر تو ظاہر کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے تمام انسان اقرباء میں داخل نہیں کیونکہ سب موصی کے جدامجد حضرت آدم علیہ السلام کی اولاد ہیں، تو تمام انسانوں کو وصیت میں داخل کرنا چاہئے مگر بالا جماع [؟] ظاہر کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا۔ جب ظاہر کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا تو پھر امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اقرباء میں وہ قیودات ہیں جن کا ذکر کیا گیا ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اقرباء سے مراد اسلام کے اندر جو آخری باپ ہے اس کی اولاد ہے ( کما ذکرنا ) اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک جو قریبی باپ ہے اس کی اولا داقرباء میں داخل ہوگی۔
And whoever calls his father 'qarib' (relative), this naming is disobedience on his part, and that is because 'qarib' in linguistic custom is a person who has kinship through another to someone else, and the kinship of father and child is intrinsic. And the apparent meaning of the word will not be considered after consensus to abandon the apparent. So according to Abu Hanifa, 'aqarib' will be determined in the manner we have mentioned. And according to the Sahibayn, with the last father in Islam, and according to Shafi'i, with the nearest father. Explanation: Also Imam Abu Hanifa says that Shari'ah has commanded maintaining family ties and prohibited severing them, and a severe threat has come regarding those who sever ties. So the testator's purpose in making a bequest for relatives is to compensate for the negligence in maintaining family ties during his life. And maintaining family ties is obligatory with dhawil arham [blood relatives through females] and not with others. For this reason, if a dhu rahim mahram is needy, maintenance for them is obligatory upon him, and for the one who is not a dhu rahim mahram, maintenance is not obligatory. And parents and children are not included in 'aqarib'; therefore they will not be included in this bequest. Because Allah's command is: 'Bequest is prescribed for parents and near relatives according to custom, as a duty upon the righteous.' So by the conjunction of 'aqrabin' with 'parents', it becomes clear that parents are not included in 'aqrabin'. And when parents are excluded, children also will be excluded. Hence both will not be called 'qarib'. And whoever calls his father 'qarib' is disobedient and called 'a'iq' (disobedient), like some foolish people who, upon obtaining a minor position, are ashamed to call their father 'father' and say, 'He is my relative.' Also Imam's argument is that in linguistic custom, 'qarib' is called one whose kinship is through an intermediary, while the kinship of parents and children is direct. Question: Apparently all relatives are included in 'aqarib'; so by the rule of 'the closest then the closest', does it necessitate excluding them despite kinship? Answer: Then if the apparent were considered, all humans would be included in 'aqarib' because all are descendants of the forefather Adam (peace be upon him), so all humans should be included in the bequest, but by consensus the apparent was not considered. When the apparent was not considered, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, 'aqarib' has the restrictions that have been mentioned. And according to the Sahibayn, 'aqarib' means the descendants of the last father in Islam (as we mentioned), and according to Imam Shafi'i, the descendants of the nearest father are included in 'aqarib'.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the definition of 'aqarib' (relatives) in the context of bequests. The author first presents the ruling that calling one's own father 'qarib' is an act of disobedience, because linguistically 'qarib' refers to a relative through an intermediary, whereas the father-child relationship is direct. After mentioning that the apparent meaning of the word is abandoned due to consensus, he outlines the positions of the three major imams: Abu Hanifa holds that 'aqarib' are determined by a specific method (described elsewhere, likely based on inheritance proximity), the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider them as the descendants of the last father in Islam, and Imam Shafi'i considers them as the descendants of the nearest father. The commentary then elaborates Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the purpose of a bequest to relatives is to compensate for the testator's shortcomings in maintaining family ties, which is obligatory only with dhawil arham (relatives through females, i.e., those with a mahram relationship via females). Since parents and children have a direct and stronger bond, they are excluded from the term 'aqarib' in the bequest, as supported by the Quranic verse that separates parents from 'aqrabin'. The author also addresses a potential objection: if the apparent meaning of 'aqarib' includes all relatives, then by the principle of 'the closest then the closest', closer relatives might be excluded. The response is that the apparent meaning is not adhered to because of consensus; thus Abu Hanifa's restricted definition applies. The key point is the distinction between direct and indirect kinship.

Key Terms
اقرباء (aqarib): Relatives intended in a bequest; according to Abu Hanifa, those related through an intermediary, excluding parents and children.
صلہ رحمی (silat rahim): Maintaining family ties, which is obligatory with dhawil arham (relatives through females) in terms of financial support.
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahim mahram): A relative through a female line who is a mahram for marriage purposes and thus eligible for obligatory maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary evidence used to exclude parents from the definition of 'aqarib'?
A) A hadith stating 'aqarib are those through an intermediary'
B) The linguistic custom that 'qarib' implies mediated kinship and the Quranic conjunction separating parents from aqrabin
C) A consensus of the Companions
D) The principle that parents are not needy

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of 'aqarib' in bequests excludes parents and children because the term linguistically implies indirect kinship, and the Quranic verse distinguishes them as separate categories.
