Distribution of Bequest Among Paternal and Maternal Uncles
Intra-Hanafi dispute on bequest distribution to relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on distributing a bequest to relatives and explain the practical difference.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa gives the closest relatives the entire bequest; the Sahibayn share equally among all relatives named.

When a person makes a bequest to his 'aqarib' (relatives), but those relatives include paternal uncles (closer) and maternal uncles (more distant), do all share equally? Imam Abu Hanifa and his disciples Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) differ. This lesson examines their reasoning and the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the bequest
The testator has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles; he bequeaths to 'aqarib'. Note the two types of uncles.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
He gives the entire bequest to the two paternal uncles, considering them closer, analogous to inheritance.
Key principle: al-aqrab fa al-aqrab.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
They divide the bequest equally into four shares among all four uncles.
No preference for closeness.
4
Understand the underlying principle
Abu Hanifa applies the principle of 'al-aqrab fa al-aqrab' in wills; the Sahibayn do not extend this rule from inheritance to wills.
The difference is about extending the inheritance principle to wills.
5
Note the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, maternal uncles get nothing; under Sahibayn, each uncle gets one quarter.
This shows the concrete impact of the ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و اذا اوصى لا قاربه وله عمان و خالان فالوصية لعميه عنده اعتبارا للاقرب كما فى الارث وعندهما بينهم ارباعا اذهما لا يعتبر ان الاقرب
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب کہ اس نے اپنے اقرباء کے لئے وصیت کی اور اس کے دو چا اور دو ماموں ہیں تو اس کے دونوں چچاؤں کے لئے ہوگی ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اقرب کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے جیسے میراث میں اور صاحبین کے نزدیک وصیت چار حصوں پر ہوگی اس لئے کہ صاحبین اقرب کا اعتبار نہیں کرتے ۔
تشریح امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک وصیت میں میراث کے مثل الاقرب فالاقرب کا قاعدہ جاری ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ قاعدہ نہیں ہے، لہذا اگر کسی نے اپنے اقرباء کے لئے وصیت کی اور اس کے اقرباء میں سے دو چا اور دو ماموں موجود ہیں تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزد یک چا ماموں سے اقرب ہیں لہذا اپوری وصیت دونوں چالیس گے اور ماموں کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا، اور صاحبین کے نزدیک وصیت کے چار حصے کر دئیے جائیں اور ہر ایک برابر کا شریک ہوگا۔
He (al-Quduri) said: And if he makes a bequest for his relatives and he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then the bequest is for his two paternal uncles according to him (Abu Hanifa), considering the closest relative as in inheritance. And according to them (the Sahibayn), it is divided into fourths among them because they do not consider the closest relative. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And when he made a bequest for his relatives and he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then it will be for his two paternal uncles according to Abu Hanifa, considering the closer relative, like in inheritance. And according to the Sahibayn, the bequest will be in four shares because the Sahibayn do not consider the closer relative. Explanation: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the rule of 'the closest then the closest' applies in bequests like in inheritance, and according to the Sahibayn, this rule does not apply. Hence, if someone made a bequest for his relatives and among his relatives there are two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then according to Abu Hanifa, the paternal uncle is closer than the maternal uncle, so the entire bequest will go to the two paternal uncles, and the maternal uncles will get nothing. And according to the Sahibayn, the bequest will be divided into four shares, and each will be an equal partner.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (though it is inter-madhhab in the sense that Sahibayn differ from Abu Hanifa) regarding the distribution of a bequest made to 'aqarib' when there are both paternal uncles (chacha) and maternal uncles (mamu). Al-Quduri's matn states the ruling: according to Abu Hanifa, the bequest goes entirely to the two paternal uncles because they are closer relatives than maternal uncles, analogously to inheritance law where agnatic relatives take precedence over cognatic ones. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the bequest is divided equally among all four uncles, because they do not give preference to the closest relative; instead, all relatives included in the term 'aqarib' share equally. The commentary reiterates that for Abu Hanifa, the principle of 'al-aqrab fa al-aqrab' (the nearest then the nearest) applies in wills, whereas for the Sahibayn, it does not. The practical consequence is that in Abu Hanifa's view, the maternal uncles receive nothing, while in the Sahibayn's view, each uncle gets one quarter of the bequest.

Key Terms
الاقرب فالاقرب (al-aqrab fa al-aqrab): The principle of giving precedence to the closest relative over the more distant one, applied by Abu Hanifa in wills.
اعتبار الاقرب (i'tibar al-aqrab): Consideration of the closest relative as the criterion for distribution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone makes a bequest to his 'aqarib' and has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, how does Abu Hanifa distribute the bequest?
A) All four uncles share equally.
B) The two paternal uncles get the entire bequest.
C) The two maternal uncles get the entire bequest.
D) The bequest is invalid because of unknown heirs.

Key Takeaway
In a bequest to relatives, Abu Hanifa gives to the closest relatives; the Sahibayn share equally among all relatives named.
